    - The `?` keyboard-shortcuts overlay (`#shortcuts-overlay.open`) never rendered in any capture, so regressions in font size, spacing, or per-theme color mapping would have landed without the design-review pipeline catching them.
    - The confirmation-dialog action-count-stacking branch had no capture — only the 2-action `kill-confirmation-modal` scene existed, so the stacked layout's per-theme rendering was unverified.
    - The mobile trailing running-indicator chip and edge-glow overlays in `app/static/js/mobile_chrome.js` were only indirectly exercised by the existing single-running-tab scene; no scene captured the multi-running state where the chip renders a count ≥ 2 and both edge glows are active.
    - Starred-row amber stripes and alternating-row bands already needed verification against the seeded dataset, not a new scene.
  - **After:**
    - `tests/js/e2e/ui-capture.desktop.capture.js` gains `shortcuts-overlay`, which drives `window.showShortcutsOverlay()` on a fresh home and asserts `#shortcuts-overlay.open` is visible.
    - `tests/js/e2e/ui-capture.desktop.capture.js` also gains `confirm-modal-three-actions-stacked`, which drives `window.showConfirm` with three role-typed actions — primary `save`, destructive `discard`, cancel `keep editing` — on a 1024-wide desktop viewport and asserts both `[data-confirm-card]` visibility and the `.modal-actions-stacked` class.
    - `tests/js/e2e/ui-capture.mobile.capture.js` gains `main-running-indicator-chip`, which runs `LONG_RUN_CMD` in tabs 1 and 2, then opens tab 3 so tabs 1 and 2 are both inactive and running; the scene asserts `#mobile-running-chip` is visible and `.mobile-running-count` renders `2`.
    - The audit also confirmed the existing history-drawer and history-sheet scenes already exercise the starred-row amber stripe and alternating-row banding patterns via deterministic seeding in `scripts/playwright/run_e2e_server.sh`, so no seeder changes were needed.
    - `tests/README.md`'s capture-spec table rows were updated to list the added scene names in the description column so operators running the pack know what to expect in the output directory.
  - **Tests:** no new test count changes — each added scene is a step inside the existing `desktop screenshot capture pack` / `mobile screenshot capture pack` Playwright tests (both gated by `RUN_CAPTURE=1` via dedicated configs so they never run in the normal `test:e2e` suite). Suite totals unchanged: 842 pytest + 666 Vitest + 197 Playwright = **1,705 tests**.
- **Interaction-contract and theme-audit coverage now enforce the confirmation-dialog and semantic-color rules end to end** — the two highest-value design-system contracts now have integration-layer drift protection.
  - **Before:**
    - The Confirmation Dialog Contract was thoroughly covered at the unit layer by `tests/js/unit/ui_confirm.test.js` (42 cases against a stubbed `#confirm-host`), but no test exercised the rules against the real mounted host with the live `showModalOverlay` / `refocusComposerAfterAction` / `closeTopmostDismissible` / `window.matchMedia` wiring.
    - The Semantic Color Contract from `THEME.md` (`--amber` / `--red` / `--green` / `--muted` must stay distinct per theme) had no automated guard; the existing theme audit measured token-vs-surface contrast, which cannot catch same-signal colors collapsing toward each other.
  - **After:**
    - `tests/js/e2e/interaction-contract.spec.js` gains a `UI interaction contract — confirmation dialog` block with 5 new Playwright cases covering default focus, Escape dismissal through `closeTopmostDismissible`, viewport-reactive stacked actions, action-count stacked actions, and `onActivate: () => false` gating.
    - `tests/js/e2e/theme-audit.spec.js` gains a second top-level `test()` case that walks every theme, reads `--amber` / `--red` / `--green` / `--muted` as computed RGB, converts each to CIELAB, computes all 6 pairwise deltaE76 values, prints a per-theme report, and hard-fails any theme whose minimum pair drops below deltaE 10.
    - Calibration reference: every shipping theme currently lands well above 10 for every pair — the tightest (`newsprint` green/muted) sits at 14.7 — so the new audit acts as a regression tripwire rather than a current-state cleanup.
  - **Tests:** 6 new Playwright cases total — 5 in `interaction-contract.spec.js` (the new confirmation-dialog block) + 1 in `theme-audit.spec.js` (the new semantic-color-distinctness case). `tests/README.md` appendix gains matching rows for all six. Verified the theme-audit gate is a real tripwire by temporarily tightening the threshold to 15 and confirming `newsprint` at 14.7 fails with a clear message naming the collapsed pair. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 666 Vitest + 197 Playwright (+6) = **1,705 tests**.
- **The mobile running-indicator contract now has dedicated jsdom regression coverage** — `tests/js/unit/mobile_running_indicator.test.js` pins mount, kill-switch, visibility, count, active-exclusion, and cycle-tap behavior for the trailing chip and edge-glow overlays in `app/static/js/mobile_chrome.js`.
  - **Before:** the mobile running-indicator surface (`app/static/js/mobile_chrome.js:121+`) was covered only by manual testing and indirect Playwright checks of the tab bar. The chip's visibility rules (hidden when there are zero running non-active tabs, hidden when the body is not in `mobile-terminal-mode`, hidden entirely behind the `?ri=off` / `?ri=0` kill switch), count math (excludes the active tab even when itself running), and cycle behavior (successive taps advance through running tabs in tab-row order and wrap back to the first) had no regression pins. A refactor that accidentally dropped the active-tab exclusion, or flipped the cycle order, or read `location.search` at the wrong time and broke the kill switch, would have landed without a failing test.
  - **After:** new `tests/js/unit/mobile_running_indicator.test.js` with 9 jsdom cases pins the contract layer. The IIFE is re-loaded into a fresh `Function('window', SRC)(window)` scope per test so the module init block (including the one-shot `location.search` read for the kill switch) runs against a freshly-built harness every case — `window.history.replaceState` sets the search string before the mount runs so `?ri=off` and `?ri=0` are testable. A synchronous `requestAnimationFrame` stub collapses the rAF-coalesced `syncRunningIndicator` into one deterministic pass. Stubbed globals (`getTabs`, `getActiveTabId`, `activateTab`) replace the runtime wiring so each test can declare the exact tab set it wants to exercise. The 9 cases cover: chip + both edge-glow overlays mount when enabled, both `?ri=off` / `?ri=0` kill switches skip the mount entirely, chip hides with `u-hidden` when no running non-active tabs, count equals running non-active count (3 running → "3"), the active tab is excluded from the count even when itself running (3 running, middle active → "2"), chip tap activates the next running non-active tab in tab-row order via `activateTab(id, {focusComposer: false})`, successive taps cycle and wrap back to the first, and non-mobile body state hides the chip and deactivates the edge glows. iOS-Safari-specific behaviors (cold smooth-scroll drop, momentum-scroll destabilization from sticky/absolute children) remain out of scope — those cannot run in jsdom and are covered by the existing Playwright mobile suite.
  - **Tests:** 9 new Vitest cases in `tests/js/unit/mobile_running_indicator.test.js`. `tests/README.md` appendix gains a matching section listing each case with a one-liner, and `README.md` project structure tree gains the new test file path. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 666 Vitest (+9) + 191 Playwright = **1,699 tests**.
- **The button primitive family now has an allowlist-style contract test for template-authored UI controls** — every `<button>`, `[role="button"]`, and `<a role="button">` in `app/templates/` must either carry one of the allowed primitive classes (`btn`, `nav-item`, `close-btn`, `toggle-btn`, `kb-key`) or match a selector in a new `tests/js/fixtures/button_primitive_allowlist.json` exception fixture.
  - **Before:**
    - The button primitive family was only drift-protected on the negative side: `button_primitives.test.js` failed if retired classes (`term-action-btn`, `hud-kill-btn`, the `modal-primary-*` / `modal-secondary-*` set, etc.) reappeared in source.
    - There was nothing stopping someone from minting a brand-new class like `.hud-neo-action-btn` or `.sidebar-glow-btn` straight onto a `<button>` without ever composing the `.btn` primitive.
    - The Frontend Design System section of `ARCHITECTURE.md` documented the rule in prose — "allowed classes: `.btn` + role + tone, plus `.nav-item` / `.close-btn` / `.toggle-btn` / `.kb-key`; anything else needs an entry in the allowlist fixture" — but the fixture didn't exist and no test read it.
  - **After:**
    - New `tests/js/unit/button_primitives_allowlist.test.js` walks `app/templates/**.html`, strips Jinja delimiters (`{% %}`, `{{ }}`, `{# #}`) to whitespace so jsdom parses the static tag shape, and querySelects `button, [role="button"]` per file — which covers `<button>`, any element with `role="button"`, and `<a role="button">` in one pass.
    - For each match the test asserts one of two conditions holds: either at least one class on the element is in the allowed primitive set (`btn`, `nav-item`, `close-btn`, `toggle-btn`, `kb-key`), or the element matches at least one `exceptions[].selector` in the new fixture.
    - The fixture seeds with 22 exception entries covering deferred surfaces (desktop rail nav items and section headers, tab bar scroll arrows, terminal chrome toggles, history panel action buttons, mobile recents sheet rows, mobile hamburger menu items and sub-items, classless header/composer buttons keyed by id, permalink save-menu items keyed by `data-action` prefix, dropdown options keyed by `role="option"`, and the mobile edit bar keyed by `data-mobile-edit`).
    - Each entry carries a `note` field documenting why it's on the list so future migrations can cross-reference against the remaining backlog; the list should trend toward empty as those surfaces migrate.
    - An 8th test validates that every exception selector is syntactically parseable so a typo in the fixture fails the suite immediately rather than silently masking a real regression.
    - Scope is deliberately HTML-only plus `<a role="button">`: JS-injected buttons (the dynamic tab close button in `tabs.js`, confirmation modal action buttons built by `showConfirm()`, history row action buttons built by `_createHistoryEntry()`) are out of scope because those surfaces already bind the `.btn` / `.close-btn` primitive in their builders, and the static scan is where a stray hand-authored `<button class="my-new-widget">` would slip in.
    - The suite total is 8 new tests (7 templates in `app/templates/` × 1 test per file + 1 fixture-validity test).
  - **Tests:** 8 new Vitest cases in `tests/js/unit/button_primitives_allowlist.test.js` (one per HTML template file plus the fixture-validity case). `tests/README.md` appendix gains a matching section listing the test and a one-liner explaining the allowlist fixture. Verified as a real tripwire: temporarily removing the `.rail-nav-item` exception from the fixture produces a crisp failure naming the four rail nav buttons as violators and surfacing their `outerHTML` preview so migration work can be planned from the test output. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 657 Vitest (+8) + 191 Playwright = **1,690 tests**.
- **All app-level modals now trap focus inside their cards** — `#options-modal`, `#theme-modal`, `#faq-modal`, and `#workflows-modal` now wire `bindFocusTrap` at startup so Tab / Shift+Tab cycles inside the open modal instead of falling through to the rail, tabs, or HUD behind the backdrop.
  - **Before:**
    - Only `#confirm-host` installed `bindFocusTrap` on its card via `showConfirm()` in `app/static/js/ui_confirm.js`.
    - The four app-level modals (`#options-modal`, `#theme-modal`, `#faq-modal`, `#workflows-modal`) had no focus trap, so Tab past the last focusable could move focus into the rail, tabs, or HUD behind the backdrop.
    - The same leak existed in reverse: Shift+Tab from the first focusable could escape the modal in the other direction.
    - The gap predated the `bindFocusTrap` primitive — each open handler called `_closeMajorOverlays()` + `showXxxOverlay()` and stopped short of any focus management.
  - **After:**
    - New `setupModalFocusTraps()` in `controller.js` runs once at startup after `setupDismissibleOverlays()` and calls `bindFocusTrap(card)` on each of the four modal cards.
    - The helper's idempotent `data-focus-trap-bound="1"` marker prevents double-binding.
    - Startup-time binding works for these modals because their DOM is persistent — the card's focusable descendants do not change between opens, so a one-shot bind is equivalent to per-open rebinding.
    - When the modal is hidden, the overlay wrapper is `display: none` so the card's focusables are out of the layout tree; when the modal is open, Tab and Shift+Tab now wrap at the card boundary.
    - `ARCHITECTURE.md`'s Frontend Design System section updates its focus-trap bullet to document both patterns: per-open for `#confirm-host`, and once-at-startup for the app-level modals.
  - **Tests:** 5 new Playwright cases in `tests/js/e2e/interaction-contract.spec.js` under a new `test.describe('UI interaction contract — modal focus trap')` block. `each app-level modal card carries data-focus-trap-bound after startup wiring` asserts the `data-focus-trap-bound="1"` attribute is set on all four cards after page load — the DOM-level proof that `setupModalFocusTraps()` ran and bound each modal. Four per-modal behavioral cases (`FAQ modal wraps Tab and Shift+Tab at its card boundary`, `theme modal wraps Tab and Shift+Tab at its card boundary`, `options modal wraps Tab and Shift+Tab at its card boundary`, `workflows modal wraps Tab and Shift+Tab at its card boundary`) open each modal, tag the first and last focusable descendants of the card with `data-focustest-first` / `data-focustest-last` markers, focus the last, press Tab, assert `document.activeElement` carries the `data-focustest-first` marker, then press Shift+Tab from the first and assert it wrapped back to `data-focustest-last`. The marker pattern makes the assertions independent of per-modal focusable order so cases stay stable as modal content evolves. `tests/README.md` appendix for `interaction-contract.spec.js` gains 5 matching rows. Surfacing the contract end-to-end also uncovered a pre-existing visibility-filter gap in `bindFocusTrap`: `_isVisible()` only excluded the HTML `hidden` attribute, not `style="display:none"`, so the options modal's session-token buttons (`copy` / `rotate` / `clear` toggle between visible and `style.display = 'none'` based on token state) could be chosen as the trap's `last` focusable while not being actually focusable — Tab from the *visible* last button would not match `active === last` and focus would leak out of the card. Fixed by adding a `getComputedStyle(el).display !== 'none'` check to `_isVisible()`; works in both jsdom (inline `style.display` is reflected in computed style) and real browsers. One new `ui_focus_trap.test.js` case (`skips focusables with inline display:none (options-modal session-token buttons pattern)`) pins the regression. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 649 Vitest (+1) + 191 Playwright (+5) = **1,682 tests**.
- **Cross-cutting UI rules now live in one documented Frontend Design System reference** — the button primitive family, disclosure rules, semantic color contract, and confirmation-dialog contract now have one canonical home in `ARCHITECTURE.md`, with companion ADR pointers in `DECISIONS.md` and contributor guidance in `CONTRIBUTING.md`.
  - **Before:**
    - The button primitive family, disclosure rules, semantic color contract, and confirmation-dialog contract had no single canonical home.
    - Button primitives lived implicitly in `components.css` and `ui_pressable.js`; disclosure rules lived in MR prose; the semantic color contract was authoritative in `THEME.md` but not surfaced where UI authors would naturally look first; the confirmation-dialog contract lived in `ui_confirm.js`'s file header.
    - The practical answer to "where do I look to build a new pressable surface / modal / disclosure?" was "read the implementation history plus helper modules plus `THEME.md`."
  - **After:**
    - `ARCHITECTURE.md` now has a dedicated `## Frontend Design System` section between Front-end Architecture and Back-end Architecture.
    - That section has four focused subsections: Button Primitive Family, Disclosure Affordance Rules, Semantic Color Contract, and Confirmation Dialog Contract.
    - `DECISIONS.md` now carries four matching lightweight ADR entries under `## Frontend Decisions`, each pointing back to the corresponding `ARCHITECTURE.md` subsection rather than duplicating the full rule set.
    - `CONTRIBUTING.md` now points contributors at the new section and states that new pressable surfaces, modals, disclosures, and color decisions must follow those rules or add an explicit exception to the relevant contract test.
    - Both tables of contents (`ARCHITECTURE.md` and `DECISIONS.md`) were updated, while `THEME.md` remains the source of truth for the semantic-color contract itself.
  - **Tests:** no new tests — this ship is documentation only. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 648 Vitest + 186 Playwright = **1,676 tests** (unchanged).
- **History rows now re-run commands by default, with restore preserved as an explicit secondary action** — on both the desktop drawer and the mobile recents sheet, clicking a history row now puts the command in the composer ready for re-run instead of spawning a new tab with the old output. Full tab restore is still one tap away via the new `restore` action button.
  - **Before:** re-running a previous command was expensive on mobile. The canonical recipe was seven discrete taps: tap the recent-peek bar, tap `copy` on the target row, close the recents sheet (or wait for it to auto-hide), tap the input once to open the keyboard, tap the input again to raise the paste menu, tap `paste`, then tap the mobile `Run` button. On desktop, the row click restored the run's output into a tab — useful when you actually wanted to re-read a completed transcript, but the wrong primary action for the common case of "I want to run this again." The terminal up-arrow convention (`cmdHistory` navigation, `Ctrl+R` reverse search, rail Recent chip click) all populate the composer with a prior command so the user can inspect / edit / run it; only the history drawer's primary click diverged by doing a full tab restore instead. The divergence also meant the copy-button action slot in the history row carried the highest-friction path: copying a command to the clipboard so you could then paste it into the composer to re-run it was a one-tap replacement for the seven-tap mobile recipe, but you had to already know `copy` existed as a workaround — the row click didn't advertise it.
  - **After:**
    - `app/static/js/history.js::refreshHistoryPanel()` now treats the row click as a composer-injection path: `setComposerValue(run.command, len, len)` → `hideHistoryPanel()` → `refocusComposerAfterAction({ preventScroll: true })` → `resetCmdHistoryNav()`.
    - The old `data-action="copy"` button is replaced with `data-action="restore"`, carrying the old row-click logic verbatim: find an existing tab for the command, activate it if the tab is already open without a truncated preview, or spawn / upgrade a tab via `restoreHistoryRunIntoTab()` for the full-output case.
    - `_createHistoryEntry()` now renders the action button with text `restore`, and `_historyActionKeepsPanelOpen()` drops the `'copy'` case while preserving the `permalink` + `star` / `delete` keep-open semantics.
    - `app/static/js/mobile_chrome.js::_recentsRenderList()` now treats the sheet row click the same way, calling `global.setComposerValue(cmd, cmd.length, cmd.length)` and then `closeRecentsSheet()`.
    - The old mobile `copy` slot is replaced with a `restore` button that reuses the same `restoreHistoryRunIntoTab()` flow the desktop button now owns, with the `loading…` affordance on `.sheet-item-cmd` and the `closeRecentsSheet()` on success preserved.
    - Net mobile re-run path drops from 7 taps to 2 taps (`peek` → `row` → `Run`), or effectively 1 if the user just wants to edit first.
    - Desktop now matches the up-arrow, reverse-search, and rail Recent chip conventions: row click injects into the composer, while `restore` remains the explicit path for reopening the old output in a tab.
  - **Tests:** 1 new Vitest case in `tests/js/unit/history.test.js` plus 2 new Playwright cases and 2 updated in `tests/js/e2e/history.spec.js` + `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js`. New `clicking a history entry row injects the command into the composer and closes the panel` Vitest case mocks `setComposerValue` onto the test harness and asserts `cmdInput.value === 'ping darklab.sh'` + `historyPanel.classList.contains('open') === false` after dispatching the row click. Existing `refreshHistoryPanel copy actions fall back to execCommand...` renamed to `refreshHistoryPanel permalink action falls back to execCommand...` (copy path is gone so the test is reduced to the permalink-only fallback — clipboard fallback coverage remains intact). Existing `closes the history panel for copy / permalink but keeps it open for delete` renamed and narrowed to `closes the history panel for permalink but keeps it open for star and delete`; mobile-parallel test loses the now-obsolete copy block. The three tab-restore tests under `describe('refreshHistoryPanel restore path')` at lines 1272/1321/1367 switch from `.querySelector('.history-entry').dispatchEvent(click)` to `.querySelector('.history-entry [data-action="restore"]').dispatchEvent(click)` so they exercise the new button instead of the now-repurposed row click. New `clicking a history entry injects the command into the composer and closes the drawer` Playwright case in `history.spec.js` asserts `#cmd` carries the command after row click, drawer closes, and tab count is unchanged (a restore would spawn a new tab). New `the history restore button loads output into a tab without touching the composer` Playwright case asserts `#cmd` stays empty and the active tab's output contains the restored command. New `the history restore button switches to an existing tab instead of duplicating it` Playwright case preserves the old optimization coverage. Existing `loading a synthetic tail run from history restores the filtered transcript` switches the click target to `[data-action="restore"]`. Existing mobile `mobile recents sheet restores a previous run into the active tab` renamed to `mobile recents sheet injects the tapped command into the composer and closes` with assertions updated for the new behavior. Existing mobile `mobile history restore works from a newly created session via the mobile menu` renamed to `mobile recents sheet restore action loads the run into the active tab` and retargeted to click the new `restore` action button. Existing `mobile history copy and permalink actions keep the drawer open` narrowed to `mobile history permalink action keeps the drawer open`. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 648 Vitest (+1) + 186 Playwright (+1) = **1,676 tests**.
- **History surfaces now use alternating-row banding and clearer mobile relative-time labels** — the desktop drawer and mobile recents sheet now band rows for readability, and the mobile time cell now shows relative age (`Nm ago` / `Nh ago` / `Nd ago`) with the absolute timestamp in the tooltip. Scope is a CSS tweak on two surfaces plus a shared JS helper for the relative-time bucketing; the desktop drawer keeps its existing exact clock reading so keyboard-heavy operators can still scan for a specific "17:43" entry.
  - **Before:** the desktop drawer's `#history-list` and the mobile `#mobile-recents-list` both rendered rows against the same flat surface with only a 1px `var(--border)` bottom border between entries — on a dense list the rows ran together visually and individual commands had to be parsed out by scanning for the star-button glyph or the exit-code token at the row's end. Rows had no alternating-background affordance, so the eye had nowhere to pivot when stepping through results. On the mobile recents sheet, the `.sheet-item-time` span was *always blank*: the renderer in `mobile_chrome.js::_recentsRenderList` read `run.started_at || run.created_at` but the `/history` JSON payload returns `started` (not `started_at` or `created_at`), so both lookups resolved to `undefined` and the time span fell through to `''`. The same field-name mismatch was present in `_recentsFilter`'s `_recentsDateMatch(r.started_at, ...)` call, breaking the mobile recents sheet's date-range filter (`today` / `this week`) whenever the filter was non-`all` — the filter function returned `false` for every row because `_recentsDateMatch(undefined, ...)` fails the validity check. Desktop drawer continued to render its `startedAt.toLocaleTimeString()` reading correctly from the well-named `run.started` field; the bug was mobile-scoped to the path that diverged from the schema.
  - **After:**
    - `components.css` gains `.history-entry:nth-of-type(even)` banding using `color-mix(in srgb, var(--surface) 94%, var(--text) 6%)`, so the desktop drawer gets alternating rows without needing per-theme tokens.
    - `mobile-chrome.css` gains the matching `.recents-sheet #mobile-recents-list .sheet-item:nth-of-type(even)` rule so the mobile sheet reads identically to the desktop drawer.
    - `history.js` gains a shared `_historyRelativeTime(startedAt, now = new Date())` helper: `just now` below 45s, `Nm ago` below 60min, `Nh ago` below 24h, `Nd ago` below 7d, and a locale-aware short date (`Apr 10` / `Oct 3`) for older runs.
    - `mobile_chrome.js::_recentsRenderList` now parses `run.started` through a new `_recentsParseDate` guard, calls `_historyRelativeTime` for the visible label, and sets `timeEl.title = parsed.toLocaleString()` so the absolute moment remains one long-press or hover away.
    - The same `run.started_at` → `run.started` fix lands in `_recentsFilter`'s `_recentsDateMatch` call, restoring the mobile recents sheet's date-range filters.
    - Desktop drawer time rendering stays on `startedAt.toLocaleTimeString()` — the relative-time change is intentionally limited to the narrower, touch-oriented mobile surface.
  - **Tests:** 2 new Vitest cases in `tests/js/unit/history.test.js` + 1 new Playwright case in `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js`. New `_historyRelativeTime buckets recent diffs as just now / m / h / d and falls back to a short date` exercises the helper directly: 10s / 3min / 2h / 2d diffs map to the expected strings, 10-day-old dates fall through to a short locale date (asserted to not match `ago|just now`), and invalid inputs (non-`Date`, `new Date('invalid')`) return `''`. New `desktop history rows keep absolute clock time and no tooltip on the time span` is a regression for the surface split: it runs the desktop-mode drawer render and asserts the `.history-entry-meta span` text does not match the relative pattern and its `title` attribute stays empty, so if a future change accidentally wires the relative path into the drawer path the test fails immediately. New `mobile history rows render relative time with absolute time in the tooltip` Playwright case runs a command on the mobile layout, opens the recents sheet via the hamburger menu's `[data-menu-action="history"]`, and asserts the first row's `.sheet-item-time` matches `/just now|\d+m ago|\d+h ago/` and carries a non-empty `title` attribute — catches the field-name mismatch regression plus the relative-time wiring in one assertion. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 647 Vitest (+2) + 185 Playwright (+1) = **1,674 tests**.
- **Mobile workflows sheet no longer reopens pinned low with an unreachable grab after an interrupted drag.** Fixes a regression where the workflows bottom sheet, on its 2nd or 3rd open after any interaction with the drag handle, would render with only the header visible near the bottom of the viewport — with the grab bar and close button unresponsive, and taps visibly passing through the sheet to elements on the main UI behind it.
  - **Before:** `mobile_sheet.js::bindMobileSheet` tracked an in-flight drag via a closure `drag` variable plus inline `will-change: transform; transition: none; transform: translateY(Xpx)` styles set directly on the bound sheet element. Cleanup (`clearStyles()` + reset of `drag`) was only reached through `endDrag`, which only ran via `pointerup` / `pointercancel` fired on the grab itself. That contract held for drags that ended on the grab, but any *external* close path — the `.workflows-close` X button (routed via `bindDismissible`), a scrim tap, `_closeMajorOverlays()` triggered by a `[data-menu-action="workflows"]` on a different sheet — hid the overlay before the captured pointer released. On iOS Safari the captured element losing its compositor layer when the overlay flips to `display: none` suppressed the subsequent `pointerup`, so `endDrag` never ran, `drag` stayed set, and the inline `transform: translateY(Xpx)` (and paired `will-change`, `transition`) persisted on `#workflows-modal`. On the next open, `showWorkflowsOverlay()` toggled `.open` on `#workflows-overlay` but did not touch the inner modal's inline styles, so the modal reappeared translated by whatever `Xpx` was active at close time. As users interacted more, the residual `Xpx` grew large enough to push the content area below the viewport — only the header + grab remained visible, and the modal's layout box sat offscreen with taps hitting the main-UI elements behind. The sheet appeared "stuck low" from the user's perspective and persisted across opens because every subsequent open inherited the same leaked transform. The issue only surfaced on the workflows modal because its overlay wrapper pattern (`#workflows-overlay > #workflows-modal`) places the mobile-sheet-bound element inside a parent with the `.open` toggle, whereas `mobile-menu-sheet` and `mobile-recents-sheet` toggle `.u-hidden` directly on themselves and so never exhibit the parent-hides-child capture-loss timing.
  - **After:** `bindMobileSheet` now watches the sheet's visibility with a `MutationObserver` that fires on class/style attribute changes on the sheet itself and on its immediate parent. A shared `_isVisible(el)` helper combines `getComputedStyle(el).display !== 'none' && visibility !== 'hidden'` with an `offsetParent === null` / `getClientRects().length === 0` fallback so the check correctly reports the modal as hidden when its overlay ancestor flips to `display: none` (the precise case that previously bypassed cleanup). On every transition from visible → hidden the observer callback forcibly resets `drag = null`, removes the window-level pointer fallback listeners, and calls `clearStyles()` — so regardless of which code path hid the sheet (X button, scrim, `_closeMajorOverlays`, Escape cascade, or any future hider), inline `transform` / `transition` / `will-change` / `opacity` are scrubbed before the next open. Two defensive secondary measures land alongside the observer for robustness against unrelated edge cases: (1) `pointerdown` on the grab now calls `clearStyles()` *before* storing the new `drag` record and setting `will-change: transform; transition: none`, so any state that somehow leaks despite the observer is recovered on the user's very next touch of the handle; (2) `pointerdown` installs window-capture-phase `pointerup` / `pointercancel` listeners that route through `endDrag(e.pointerId)`, and `endDrag` removes them via a new `_removeWindowFallbacks()` helper whether it exits via cancelled, tap, or settle paths — this covers the case where a captured pointer survives the overlay's hide but routes its `pointerup` to window instead of to the (now-detached) grab. All three measures compose: the window listeners catch real-pointer edge cases, the observer catches programmatic/external close paths, and the `pointerdown` reset catches any state that escapes both. The `keydown` (Enter/Space) handler is unchanged — it never needed drag state.
  - **Tests:** one new Playwright case `workflows sheet reopens at full height after an interrupted drag` in `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js` under `test.describe('mobile menu')` reproduces the exact state-leak sequence. The test opens the workflows sheet via the hamburger menu's `[data-menu-action="workflows"]` entry, dispatches a synthetic `pointerdown` + `pointermove(+40px)` sequence on the grab to set inline `transform: translateY(40px)`, then clicks the `.workflows-close` X button while the drag is still "active" (no corresponding `pointerup` ever dispatched) — this is the exact external-close-during-active-drag path that caused the leak before the fix. After close, the test asserts `#workflows-modal`'s inline `style` attribute contains no `translateY` (scrubbed by the visibility observer). It then reopens the sheet and asserts `#workflows-modal`'s bounding box height is greater than `viewport.height * 0.5` — a regression of the leak would keep the modal short-and-low because the residual translate would push the content offscreen; the new measure fails only if the fix is broken. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 645 Vitest + 184 Playwright (+1) = **1,671 tests**.
- **Mobile sheet scrim covers the sticky header so tapping outside the sheet closes it again.** Restores the long-standing "tap outside the sheet to close" affordance for the mobile menu sheet and the mobile recents sheet, which had quietly stopped working when the mobile-terminal header gained its higher `z-index: 90` stacking context.
  - **Before:** `.menu-sheet-scrim` and `.recents-sheet-scrim` both rendered at `z-index: 50`, while `body.mobile-terminal-mode header` sits at `z-index: 90` in `mobile.css:309`. With the header DOM stacked above the scrim, tapping anywhere inside the header band (the visible strip at the top of the page when a sheet is open) hit the header element itself and the `bindDismissible` backdrop click handler on the scrim never fired. The drag handle (`.sheet-grab`) inside the sheet kept working because `mobile_sheet.js` owns its tap/drag lifecycle directly on the grab element and doesn't depend on the scrim intercepting clicks. Operators who tried the natural "tap the dimmed area above the sheet to dismiss" gesture saw nothing happen.
  - **After:** both scrims bumped to `z-index: 100` and both sheets to `z-index: 101` in `mobile-chrome.css`, lifting the scrim above the `z-index: 90` header so the dim layer actually covers the header band. Tapping anywhere outside the sheet — header included — now lands on the scrim and `bindDismissible` closes the sheet as intended. The sheet's own z-index stays one step above the scrim so sheet contents remain interactive. `z-index: 100/101` sits well below the major overlay/modal range (shortcuts overlay at 150, options/theme overlays at 320, confirm modal primitive at 340) so the bump does not change which surface wins when modals and sheets co-exist.
  - **Tests:** one new Playwright case `tapping the sticky header dismisses the mobile menu sheet` in `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js` opens the menu via the hamburger and then `page.mouse.click(40, 10)` taps inside the header's bounding box — before the fix this no-op'd because the header stacked above the scrim. The existing `clicking outside the menu closes it` case (scrim-target click) still passes and documents the canonical backdrop target. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 645 Vitest + 183 Playwright (+1) = **1,670 tests**.
- **Mobile action-row density now prioritizes high-frequency actions by moving `clear` into the hamburger menu** — the narrow mobile row now keeps only `share snapshot`, `copy`, `save ▾`, and `■ Kill`, while `clear` lives in the menu. The per-tab clear button hides on the mobile-terminal layout and a new `data-menu-action="clear"` entry in the hamburger menu routes through `dispatchMobileMenuAction()` to the same `cancelWelcome(activeTabId) + clearTab(activeTabId, { preserveRunState: true })` pair the HUD and per-tab buttons already use on desktop.
  - **Before:** the per-tab `.terminal-actions` footer (built by `tabs.js::ensureTerminalActions()` and rendered below each tab's `.output` column) shipped five control surfaces on mobile — `share snapshot`, `copy`, `save ▾`, `clear`, and the red `■ Kill` icon — plus an identical footer on every tab-pane. At narrow widths (≤390px portrait, iPhone-class) the row wrapped or squeezed each button below a comfortable text size to fit every control on a single line, with `clear` and `■ Kill` competing for the trailing slot every time a user reached for the frequent actions at the row's left. `clear` is a recovery action (wipe output while preserving run state) not an in-flow one like copy / save / share, but it carried the same row-level weight as the three actions that operators genuinely reach for mid-run. The mobile kill button had already been moved out of the action row previously (`body.mobile-terminal-mode .terminal-actions .tab-kill-btn { display: none !important }` in `mobile.css:535`), so the precedent for lifting a lower-frequency action off the row into a dedicated surface was already in place.
  - **After:** one CSS hide rule plus one menu entry plus one dispatch branch. `mobile.css` gains `body.mobile-terminal-mode .terminal-actions [data-action="clear"] { display: none !important }` sibling to the kill hide so the per-tab row on the mobile-terminal layout now shows only `share snapshot` / `copy` / `save ▾`; desktop rendering is unchanged because the rule is gated on `.mobile-terminal-mode`. `templates/index.html` gains a `<button data-menu-action="clear">` entry between `search` and `ln` in the first `.menu-group` of `#mobile-menu-sheet`, with a `⌫` icon (erase-left glyph) and the label `clear` to match the other menu items. `controller.js::dispatchMobileMenuAction()` grows a new `clear` branch between `ln` and `options` that, if `activeTabId` is set, calls `cancelWelcome(activeTabId)` followed by `clearTab(activeTabId, { preserveRunState: true })` — the exact invocation the desktop HUD clear (`shell_chrome.js:452`) and the per-tab clear handler (`tabs.js:618`) already use — then `refocusComposerAfterAction({ defer: true })` so the composer regains focus after the sheet closes. The shared `button[data-menu-action]` click handler in `controller.js:283` already hides the sheet via `hideMobileMenu()` before dispatching, so the sheet closes as part of the action path with no per-item plumbing. The clear path is now functionally identical across surfaces: the HUD clear, the per-tab desktop clear, and the mobile menu clear all route through the same `cancelWelcome + clearTab({ preserveRunState: true })` pair, so a mid-run clear on any surface wipes the output column without abandoning the live SSE stream — commands keep running and their output continues appending into the now-blank transcript.
  - **Tests:** one new Vitest case in `tests/js/unit/app.test.js` and one existing Playwright case updated in `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js`. New `clear cancels welcome, clears the active tab preserving run state, and closes the sheet` case loads `loadAppFns` with `clearTab` and `cancelWelcome` spies plus `activeTabId: 'tab-1'`, opens the sheet by removing `u-hidden`, clicks `#mobile-menu-sheet [data-menu-action="clear"]`, then asserts `cancelWelcomeSpy` was called with `'tab-1'`, `clearTabSpy` was called with `'tab-1', { preserveRunState: true }`, and the sheet carries `u-hidden` after dispatch. The existing `mobile tab action buttons still work while the keyboard is open` Playwright case in `mobile.spec.js` was updated: the direct per-tab `[data-action="clear"]` click is replaced with opening the hamburger (`#hamburger-btn`), asserting the sheet becomes visible (no longer has `u-hidden`), clicking `#mobile-menu-sheet [data-menu-action="clear"]`, and then asserting the output lines drop to zero, the mobile keyboard helper is hidden, and the sheet returns to `u-hidden` — so the test now exercises the new menu path and the keyboard-open invariant in one sequence. DOM harness in `app.test.js` also gains the matching `<button data-menu-action="clear">` between the existing `search` and `history` entries so the new case has a button to click. Visual verification: per-tab action row on 390px portrait now reads `share snapshot · copy · save ▾` with the kill button as the only trailing element, and the hamburger menu's first group reads `ln · ts · search · clear · history` with the new row rendering identically to its siblings. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 645 Vitest (+1) + 182 Playwright = **1,669 tests**.
- **Mobile search now exposes the match counter, uses a cleaner two-line layout, and steps through logical matches correctly** — the mobile search bar is easier to scan, less vertically wasteful, and no longer mis-steps across inline-element boundaries. Three layers in one ship: the counter/reflow CSS on the mobile search bar, a control-height reduction on the same surface to recover vertical viewport for the transcript, and a correctness fix in `search.js` for the nav-arrow behavior that was observed during mobile testing but affects every surface the search bar runs on.
  - **Before:**
    - `#search-count` was present in the DOM and populated by `search.js`, but `body.mobile-terminal-mode .search-count { display: none }` hid it entirely on mobile, so users got no visible match-count feedback.
    - The mobile search bar stayed on one row with `flex-wrap: nowrap`, which squeezed the input and controls together too tightly on narrow phones.
    - Control sizing was generous enough to consume a meaningful amount of vertical transcript space on already-short mobile viewports.
    - `_highlightSearchLine` treated each text-node fragment as a separate match, so logical matches that crossed inline-element boundaries were counted and navigated incorrectly.
    - `clearHighlights` never re-normalized adjacent text nodes, so repeated search / clear / re-search cycles fragmented the DOM and eventually produced per-character highlight pills.
  - **After:**
    - The mobile-only `display: none` rule is replaced with `font-size: 13px; flex: 0 0 auto`, so the counter is visible on mobile and collapses naturally when empty.
    - The mobile search bar now wraps to two rows: the input always occupies row 1, while toggles, counter, nav, and close cluster on row 2.
    - Mobile control sizing is tightened so the surface keeps the same touch semantics while returning more vertical real estate to the transcript.
    - `_highlightSearchLine(line, re, startMatchIdx)` now tags every `<mark>` with a logical `data-search-match` group id, and `runSearch` / `navigateSearch` operate on those groups instead of individual mark fragments.
    - `highlightCurrent` now lights every mark in the active group as one logical match and scrolls the first segment into view.
    - `_highlightSearchLine` normalizes cloned DOM before matching, and `clearHighlights` normalizes touched lines afterward, so repeated search cycles no longer fragment matches into separate pills.
    - Net result: mobile now shows the counter, uses a cleaner two-line layout, and both mobile and desktop search advance through logical matches rather than inline-fragment segments.
  - **Tests:** two new Vitest cases in `tests/js/unit/search.test.js` and one existing case extended. New `merges adjacent text nodes between searches so a fragmented line is not re-split per fragment` runs the known fragmentation sequence — search for `p` on a transcript containing `ping`, clear highlights, then re-search for `ping` — and asserts the result is one `<mark>` wrapping the whole word rather than multiple per-fragment marks. New `navigates by logical match across inline-element boundaries` asserts a two-line transcript with `<span class="line-prefix">$</span>curl <span class="line-host">localhost</span>` pattern produces four DOM marks but counter reads `1 / 2`, and stepping with `navigateSearch(1)` / `navigateSearch(-1)` cycles through the two logical matches rather than the four segments. Existing case `highlights mixed-content lines without flattening helper markup` extended to assert the two DOM marks share a `data-search-match` attribute value and the counter reads `1 / 1`. The three mobile-search CSS changes (display replaced with sizing, input flex override, wrap rule flip) have no new automated coverage — `search.spec.js` Playwright coverage continues to pass since `#search-count`'s textContent contract is unchanged. Visual verification: at 390px, 360px, and 320px portrait the input occupies row 1 and all four controls cluster on row 2 with the close button right-aligned; counter renders inline with the toggles on the second row when a match count is present (`1 / 42`, `123 / 4567`) and collapses to zero width when the input is empty with no leftover gap; the shorter 28–32px control heights give the terminal transcript an extra row of visible output on a 390×844 viewport; repeated search / clear / re-search cycles on a `ping` transcript keep each word-wide match rendering as a single amber pill, not per-character pills. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 644 Vitest (+2) + 182 Playwright = **1,668 tests**.
- **Desktop toolbar and discoverability polish improves autocomplete, reverse-search, rail clarity, and starred-command signaling** — a set of tightly-scoped chrome refinements make selection state, navigation cues, and star grouping easier to read without changing the underlying behavior. Scope is a handful of narrowly-scoped tweaks on the existing chrome — no new surfaces, no behavioral changes to how autocomplete / reverse-search / the rail / the history drawer work (the rail's starred-first ordering simply mirrors what the history drawer already does, against the same server-backed star set), and the `.dot-r` / `.dot-y` / `.dot-g` classes plus their `--theme-window-btn-*` tokens are intentionally preserved because the theme-card preview chrome in the theme picker (`app.js:1459`) still renders a mini terminal frame with those dots.
  - **Before:**
    - The autocomplete dropdown's active row changed text color but had no background change, so selection state was too subtle on dense lists.
    - Reverse-i-search highlighted matches with green text alone, which became hard to distinguish once the whole active row also turned green.
    - The collapsed rail used undersized glyphs and weak muted coloring for icon-only navigation, so the collapsed state read as less interactive than it should.
    - The rail collapse button never updated its tooltip or `aria-label` when switching between expanded and collapsed states.
    - The search-prev and search-next buttons had no `type`, `aria-label`, or `title`, making them the only unlabeled controls in the search row.
    - History star buttons had `aria-label` but no tooltip text explaining that starring pins a command to the top.
    - The desktop tabbar still carried decorative macOS-style traffic lights that consumed space without conveying app state.
    - The rail Recent section preserved raw recency order but not starred-first ordering, so pinned commands lost their strongest affordance on the primary nav surface.
  - **After:**
    - `.ac-item.ac-active` now gets a neutral hover-band background so the active autocomplete row is easier to track.
    - `.hist-search-match` now gets a soft tinted capsule background, radius, and padding so the matched substring stays legible even on an active green row.
    - Collapsed rail glyphs are larger, stronger, and spaced more generously, and collapsed nav items now pick up the same accent-on-hover feel as the rest of the chrome.
    - `shell_chrome.js::applyCollapsed()` now updates both the `title` and `aria-label` on `railCollapseBtn` so the control always advertises the correct action.
    - Search-nav buttons now declare `type="button"`, `aria-label`, and shortcut-aware `title` text (`Shift+Enter` / `Enter`) to match the rest of the surface.
    - History and mobile-recents star buttons now expose descriptive tooltip text explaining the pin-to-top behavior.
    - The decorative tabbar traffic lights are removed from the desktop strip, while the underlying theme tokens remain because the theme-picker previews still use them.
    - `renderRailRecent()` now partitions rows into starred-first then unstarred groups, preserves recency within each partition, and marks starred rows with a 2px amber left stripe so pinned commands stand out without adding a glyph.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — the changes are a CSS tweak pair (one new rule on `.ac-item.ac-active`, one background + radius bump on `.hist-search-match`), template attribute additions (no id / selector changes), a glyph-size rule in the collapsed-rail media block, two `setAttribute` calls in `applyCollapsed()`, descriptive text on existing `aria-label` / new `title` on two star-button renderers, a pure deletion of one `<div>` + three CSS rules, plus a starred-first partition in `renderRailRecent()` that reuses the existing `_getStarred()` helper and two CSS rules on `.rail-item` / `.rail-item.starred` for the amber stripe + padding shift. Existing e2e and unit coverage passes unchanged — a repo-wide grep for the retired class (`tabbar-traffic-lights`) and the retired title (`"Collapse sidebar"` as a static string) returns zero hits outside of CHANGELOG and release-notes historical entries, and the existing `shell_chrome.test.js` rail coverage continues to pass since `renderRailRecent()` still receives and renders every `items` entry — just in a reordered sequence with a new class on starred rows. Visual verification: autocomplete exercised under a long suggestion list; reverse-i-search (Ctrl+R) exercised with a multi-character query against both active and inactive rows; rail collapsed and expanded across all 17 themes; hover tooltips confirmed on the two search-nav buttons and on both star-button surfaces; tabbar left edge now starts immediately at the `◀` scroll button with no leading dots; starring a command from the history drawer was observed to re-order the Recent rail with the amber stripe painting on the flagged row, and unstarring moved it back to chronological position. Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 642 Vitest + 182 Playwright = **1,666 tests** (unchanged).
- **The diagnostics page now separates Activity from Outcomes, shows freshness, and treats config booleans as neutral metadata** — `/diag` is easier to scan and semantically cleaner without changing its underlying data model. Scope is three narrowly-scoped tweaks: section structure, a freshness affordance, and a color-semantics correction — no new diagnostic data, no backend query changes, and no change to the JSON-format response (`?format=json` still returns the same `data` shape).
  - **Before:**
    - The diagnostics page mixed time-window activity counts and run outcomes into one `Activity` card, forcing readers to decode two different axes under one heading.
    - The page had no visible freshness signal, so a stale open tab looked the same as a newly rendered one.
    - Config booleans rendered `true` values in green, which diluted the meaning of green as a live success/status signal.
  - **After:**
    - The old `Activity` card is split into two sibling sections: `Activity` for time-window counts and `Outcomes` for success / failed / incomplete counts.
    - A new `diag-topbar` wraps the existing header plus a sibling `diag-status-bar`, so desktop can show freshness/status beside the app name while mobile can stack the same content without fighting sticky-header layout rules.
    - The status bar now shows `Generated at ...` plus an `Auto-refresh (10s)` toggle that persists in `localStorage` and reloads the page on a one-shot timer when enabled.
    - The header itself stays structurally simple, avoiding the earlier regressions caused by putting multi-row status content directly inside the sticky header element.
    - Config-card `true` values now render as neutral text instead of green, reserving green for live verified status rows such as Database, Redis, and Vendor Assets.
    - The diagnostics page title drops its stale bordered-box chrome and now matches the plain glowing title treatment used on other official surfaces.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — the change is a template split + inline JS + two CSS rule edits with no new behavioral primitive. Existing `/diag` route coverage in `tests/py/test_routes.py` and diagnostics allowlist coverage in `tests/py/test_backend_modules.py` pass unchanged since the `data` dict and `?format=json` response shape are untouched. Visual verification: the split card renders at desktop (`Activity` and `Outcomes` side-by-side under Config) and at ≤760px (stacked 2-col); generated-at timestamp appears under the header, auto-refresh toggle persists across reloads via localStorage, un-toggling during a scheduled reload cancels the next refresh (cleared via `clearTimeout`); config `true` values now read as neutral white on all 17 themes, matching `false`'s dim treatment with only a color-weight difference (true: `var(--text)`, false: `var(--muted)`). Net suite delta: 842 pytest + 642 Vitest + 182 Playwright = 1,666 tests (unchanged).
- **Permalink prompt-echo lines now use the configured `prompt_prefix` instead of a bare `$`** — permalink pages now match the live shell's prompt identity. Scope is intentionally narrow: the one remaining drift between the live shell's prompt identity and the prompt rendered on history / snapshot permalinks — no changes to the JS export pipeline (already shared across live shell, HTML export, PDF export, and permalink.js via `output.js::_outputPromptPrefix()` + `export_html.js::renderExportPromptEcho()`), no changes to the permalink template or the `<title>` tag.
  - **Before:** `_normalize_permalink_lines` in `app/permalinks.py` synthesized a prompt-echo line for history snapshots / share pages that did not already carry one — both the structured-snapshot branch (line 90) and the unstructured-content branch (line 103) hardcoded `f"$ {label}"`. The `/config` endpoint and the live shell template both source the prompt identity from `CFG["prompt_prefix"]` (default `anon@darklab:~$`), but the permalink path ignored it, so the same run rendered as `anon@darklab:~$ ls -la` in the live shell and as the reduced `$ ls -la` on its permalink. This was the only server-side drift — the JS side was already unified: `output.js::_outputPromptPrefix()` reads the DOM `.prompt-prefix` (or falls back to `APP_CONFIG.prompt_prefix`) and stores the full prefix into `rawLine.text`, which both `export_html.js::renderExportPromptEcho()` and `export_pdf.js`'s prompt-echo branch consume by splitting on the first space to colourize the prefix.
  - **After:** new `_prompt_echo_text(label)` helper in `permalinks.py` is the single server-side source of truth for synthesized prompt-echo text — reads `CFG["prompt_prefix"]`, strips surrounding whitespace, falls back to `$` when the prefix is empty or missing, and returns `f"{prefix} {label}".rstrip()` so an empty label yields `anon@darklab:~$` rather than `anon@darklab:~$ ` with a trailing space. Both hardcoded `f"$ {label}"` sites in `_normalize_permalink_lines` call the helper instead, so permalink prompt echoes now match the live shell across default and custom `prompt_prefix` values. Scope is intentionally limited to permalinks: `app/blueprints/history.py:316` still uses `f"$ {run['command']}"` for the HTML `<title>` tag, which is kept short-form by convention since browser tabs render abbreviated titles and the `<title>` is not a visible-prompt surface — leaving this one out keeps the change a single-concept ship. The JS-side helpers `_outputPromptPrefix()` and `renderExportPromptEcho()` keep their current names; a rename to a common `getPromptPrefix()` vocabulary was considered but the two helpers sit on different layers (live-shell prompt render vs export text renderer) and renaming them would churn tests and capture selectors without reducing drift. Per `project_synthetic_prompt` memory, the prompt is synthetic cosmetic chrome (not session-derived), so surfacing the full prefix on permalinks is consistent with product intent and raises no redaction concern.
  - **Tests:** 6 new pytest cases in `tests/py/test_backend_modules.py`. New `TestPromptEchoText` suite covers the helper directly — `test_uses_configured_prompt_prefix` (configured prefix renders on the echo), `test_falls_back_to_dollar_when_prefix_missing` (empty/missing config falls back to `$`), `test_strips_trailing_space_when_label_empty` (no trailing space when label is empty). New `TestNormalizePermalinkLinesPromptEcho` suite covers the integration path — `test_unstructured_content_uses_configured_prefix` (string-list content synthesizes the echo with the configured prefix), `test_structured_snapshot_without_echo_gets_configured_prefix` (dict-list snapshots without an existing echo get one synthesized with the configured prefix), `test_structured_snapshot_with_existing_echo_is_preserved` (existing echo lines survive verbatim — normalizer does not double-prepend). Net suite delta: 842 pytest (+6) + 642 Vitest + 182 Playwright = **1,666 tests**. Visual verification: history permalinks and share snapshots loaded under a custom `prompt_prefix` render the configured prefix on the prompt-echo line matching the live shell; default-config render unchanged from the live shell side.
- **Save-menu copy clarity rewords `txt / html / pdf` into descriptive format labels and tightens the visual attachment between trigger and menu** — the three save-menu surfaces (desktop HUD, per-tab, and permalink page) now read more clearly without changing the underlying save actions, file-extension wiring, or `data-action` hooks.
  - **Before:**
    - All three save menus rendered the bare labels `txt` / `html` / `pdf` — format names only, with no descriptive wording or `.ext` hint.
    - The menus floated 4px off the trigger button, which made them read as detached popovers rather than extensions of the button.
    - Menu `min-width` was tuned only for the short 3–4 character labels.
    - The chevron rendered only on `.save-menu-wrap > button`, so the desktop HUD save button had no dropdown indicator at all, and the permalink/mobile direction cue did not match the actual menu-open direction.
  - **After:**
    - Labels now render as `Plain text (.txt)` / `Styled HTML (.html)` / `PDF document (.pdf)` across all three call-sites.
    - `data-action` attributes (`save-txt` / `save-html` / `save-pdf`) are unchanged, so existing selectors and tests still bind to the same actions.
    - The attachment cue is tightened by changing the menu offsets from `calc(100% + 4px)` to `calc(100% - 1px)`, creating a shared border edge between trigger and menu.
    - Border radii are trimmed on the edge that meets the trigger so the menu reads as an extension of the button rather than a separate rounded panel.
    - `min-width` is bumped to 160px on both shell and HUD variants to accommodate the longer labels without wrapping.
    - The chevron selector now includes `.hud-save-wrap > button`, and the indicator is redrawn so its orientation matches whether the menu opens upward or downward.
    - The HUD save button's `title` attr stays as `"Save tab output (txt / html / pdf)"` because the short parenthetical still works well as a pre-open hover hint.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — the change is a copy + CSS tweak with no new behavior. Existing Playwright coverage in `tests/js/e2e/output.spec.js`, `share.spec.js`, `interaction-contract.spec.js`, and both capture specs selects on stable `data-action` attributes (`[data-action="save-txt"]`, `[data-action="save-html"]`, `[data-action="save-pdf"]`, `[data-action="save-menu"]`) that did not change; the two `share.spec.js` cases using `:has-text("txt")` / `:has-text("html")` continue to match via case-insensitive substring against the new labels (`.txt` and `.html` both appear literally in the new copy). Visual verification: HUD save menu, per-tab save menu, and permalink save menu all opened across desktop and mobile widths — menu reads as attached to trigger (shared 1px border edge, flat-on-trigger-side corners) and long labels fit without wrapping. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 642 Vitest + 182 Playwright = 1,660 tests (unchanged).
- **Workflow modal usability adds a per-step run affordance and converges the step row onto a consistent two-row grid** — `#workflows-overlay` now supports both "load into prompt" and direct per-step execution without changing the card headers, modal shell, or underlying workflows catalog. Each step gets its own ▶ button; there is no bulk-run affordance because the catalog's commands are examples meant to be reviewed and adapted, not templated inputs.
  - **Before:**
    - `renderWorkflowItems` in `app.js` built each step as a flex-row `.workflow-step` with the counter, command chip, and note all living as inline-level children of the same `<li>`.
    - Because the chip grew to fit its text, the note's horizontal start position shifted step by step, so the notes column zig-zagged down the card.
    - Users had only one interaction path per step: clicking the chip loaded the command into the composer and closed the modal, leaving the user to press Enter separately.
    - There was no direct run path for users who wanted to execute the canned example as-is.
  - **After:**
    - `.workflow-step` moves from a flex row to a 2-column × 2-row CSS grid so the counter, main action row, and note align consistently.
    - A new `<div class="workflow-step-main">` holds the chip and the new run button inline, while `.workflow-step-note` moves to its own second-row cell so all notes begin at the same x-coordinate.
    - The new run affordance is a `<button class="btn btn-ghost btn-compact btn-icon-only workflow-step-run">▶</button>` with `data-workflow-step-cmd="${cmd}"` and `aria-label="Run: ${cmd}"`.
    - New `activateWorkflowStepRun(cmd)` closes major overlays and then calls `submitComposerCommand(cmd, { dismissKeyboard: true })`, so a step can be run in one gesture without a stop through the composer.
    - The run button is wired through `bindPressable` in `wireWorkflowStepRunButtons(root)`, keeping click and keyboard activation on the shared primitive path.
    - Chip behavior is intentionally unchanged: users who want to inspect or edit before running still use the chip path.
    - Obsolete mobile flex-wrap overrides are removed because the grid layout now handles narrow-width wrapping natively.
  - **Tests:** 3 new Playwright cases under `test.describe('workflows modal')` in `tests/js/e2e/ui.spec.js`. First case asserts DOM structure — chip presence, run button presence, button text is `▶`, `data-workflow-step-cmd` is non-empty, `aria-label` is `Run: ${cmd}`. Second case asserts the grid layout contract — computed `display` is `grid`, first child is `.workflow-step-main`, second child is `.workflow-step-note` — so a future refactor can't silently revert the two-row layout without a failing test. Third case asserts end-to-end click-to-run — opening workflows via `Alt+G`, clicking the first step's run button, overlay closes, body content eventually contains the command text. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 642 Vitest + 182 Playwright = **1,660 tests**. Visual verification: all built-in workflow cards open via the rail and via `Alt+G`; step counter, chip, and note columns align consistently down each card; ▶ button activates via mouse, Enter, and Space and closes the modal before submitting the command.
- **Compact dialog spacing now tightens body-to-actions rhythm, adds a narrow-width treatment, and wires a shared focus trap into every confirm modal** — the `.modal-card-compact` family used by all five `showConfirm` surfaces now reads more cleanly and keeps keyboard focus where it belongs.
  - **Before:** `.modal-copy { margin-bottom: 20px }` produced a larger body-to-actions gap than the `.modal-card-compact { padding: 18px 20px }` card's bottom padding of 18px, so action buttons read as floating mid-card rather than anchored to the bottom edge. The optional `.modal-confirm-content` slot — empty on three of the five surfaces (kill, history delete, session-token migrate) and populated on the other two (share redaction inline, session-token set with an `<input>` + `.modal-inline-field` + error span) — had no rule for the empty case, so even without children it occupied a 0-height flex slot that sat between body and actions; not visually broken but the slot's presence was reserved rather than collapsed. When the slot *was* populated (session-token set), the stacked margins of `.modal-copy` (20px) + `.modal-inline-field` (18px) compounded to a 38px band between body and actions, inconsistent with the no-content 20px case. Narrow-width (<=480px) had only `.modal-actions-wrap { gap: 6px }` — the card itself still shipped with desktop padding (18px/20px) and body margin (20px), so on 320px-wide screens the compact modal felt loose rather than compact. Separately on the behavioral side: `ui_confirm.js` focused Cancel on open but installed no Tab-boundary trap, so Tab from the last action button (e.g. Kill in the kill-confirm) fell through to the document and started cycling into rail / tab / HUD buttons behind the backdrop — many Tabs later the user could ghost-activate chrome buttons they could not see. And the history-clear and history-row-delete confirms opened from mouse clicks, so their programmatic `focusTarget.focus()` did not match `:focus-visible` (Chrome / Firefox heuristic — `:focus-visible` suppresses the ring on mouse-driven focus), leaving Cancel focused but with no visible outline; users had no signal which button would activate on Enter. The history-row trash icon further compounded this: its `bindPressable` onActivate called `confirmHistAction(...)` then `hideHistoryPanel()`, and `hideHistoryPanel` calls `refocusComposerAfterAction` — so the modal focused Cancel, then hideHistoryPanel yanked focus to the composer, then `bindPressable._afterActivate` yanked it again, landing focus outside the modal's focus-trap target and leaving Tab with nothing to trap.
  - **After (spacing, pure CSS):**
    - `.modal-copy` margin-bottom trims from 20px to 16px so actions anchor more naturally to the card's bottom padding.
    - `.modal-inline-field` margin-bottom trims from 18px to 14px so field-to-actions spacing is tighter than body-to-actions spacing.
    - New `.modal-confirm-content:empty { display: none; }` collapses the slot entirely when unused.
    - New narrow-width (<=480px) rules tighten compact-card padding and inner spacing to match the already-tightened action-row gap on mobile widths.
    - Action alignment stays intentionally unchanged; this ship tightens rhythm and spacing, not justification.
  - **After (focus-trap + visible-focus bundle):**
    - New `app/static/js/ui_focus_trap.js` primitive provides `bindFocusTrap(container)`, which wraps Tab / Shift+Tab at the container boundary and is idempotent via `data-focus-trap-bound`.
    - `ui_confirm.js` installs that trap on the active `_card` and disposes it during `_cleanup`; `templates/index.html` now loads the new script between `ui_dismissible.js` and `ui_confirm.js`.
    - A scoped `#confirm-host .btn:focus` rule forces a visible green outline onto the default-focused Cancel button even when the modal was opened by mouse and `:focus-visible` would otherwise suppress the ring.
    - The history-row delete path now avoids yanking focus back to the composer before the confirm modal can own it: the eager `hideHistoryPanel()` call is removed, and `ui_pressable.js` skips its post-activate refocus path whenever `onActivate` opened a confirm modal.
  - **Scope note:** at this point in the rollout, the focus trap lived only in `ui_confirm.js`. Options, theme picker, FAQ, workflows, and save menu overlays remained un-trapped until the later modal parity pass because their Tab-escape cost was lower and rolling them onto the primitive cleanly required a separate pass through each dismissible's open/close lifecycle.
  - **Tests:** nine new Vitest cases. New file `tests/js/unit/ui_focus_trap.test.js` covers the primitive directly — wrap forward (Tab from last → first), wrap backward (Shift+Tab from first → last), middle-of-list passthrough (no `preventDefault`), no-focusables no-op, idempotent re-bind returns `null`, `dispose` removes the handler and clears the bound flag, skips hidden focusables. `ui_confirm.test.js` gained two cases asserting that an open confirm traps Tab from the last action and Shift+Tab from the first. `ui_pressable.test.js` gained one case asserting the modal-open guard — when `window.isConfirmOpen() === true`, `_afterActivate` does not call `refocusComposerAfterAction`. `history.test.js` — the two existing cases (`closes the history panel when a history action button is clicked`, `keeps common history actions open on mobile and only closes for delete`) were renamed and flipped to assert the new invariant: the history panel stays open for all row actions (copy and permalink still close on desktop; delete keeps the panel open on both desktop and mobile since the confirm modal overlays it). Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 642 Vitest + 179 Playwright = 1,657 tests. Visual verification: all five compact-modal surfaces (kill via HUD Kill while `sleep 30` runs; history row delete + clear all + clear non-favorites; share redaction; session-token set / migrate) opened via mouse and via keyboard — Cancel ships with a visible green focus ring, Tab and Shift+Tab cycle within the modal's action row and never escape to the rail / tabs / HUD behind the backdrop, Enter activates the focused action. The `:empty` rule inspected via DevTools on the three no-content surfaces confirms the slot collapses to `display: none`.
- **Desktop HUD status-bar wording now renames `RUNS` to `TABS` and dims `LAST EXIT` while the active tab is running** — this is a narrow HUD semantics and freshness update, with no new pills, no removals, and no layout change.
  - **Before:** the desktop HUD carried a pill labelled `RUNS` that rendered as `RUNS 1 / 2` — which read as "1 of 2 total runs" (lifetime count) but actually counted tabs (`running / total` derived from `global.tabs`). Numerator/denominator ambiguity: readers had to guess whether `/ 2` meant "two remaining" or "two total"; the label implied an historical counter but the number was point-in-time. Separately, the adjacent `LAST EXIT` pill painted its exit code in full-intensity green (`0`) or red (non-zero / `KILLED`) during an active run, even though the prior run's exit is stale context once a new run is in flight — full-intensity semantic color on stale metadata violated the semantic-color contract (stale metadata = muted).
  - **After:** the pill renamed to `TABS` (html `id="hud-tabs"`, ref `hudTabsEl`, render fn `_renderTabs` in `shell_chrome.js`). Format dropped the `running / total` fraction in favor of `${total} · ${running} active` when any tab is running (e.g. `TABS 2 · 1 active`) and the bare count `${total}` when no tabs are running (e.g. `TABS 2`). Color semantics unchanged — amber when any tab is running, muted otherwise. `LAST EXIT` gains an active-run awareness: `_renderLastExit` reads `global.tabs` + `global.activeTabId` on each render; when the active tab's `.st === 'running'`, the exit color is forced to `hud-muted` regardless of the stored value, while the text value stays in place (still shows `0` / `3` / `KILLED` from the prior run). Re-renders trigger on four wrappers in total: the existing `setTabStatus` wrapper (which already drove `_renderTabs`, now also drives `_renderLastExit`), a new `activateTab` wrapper so tab switches re-evaluate the dim state (otherwise a user leaving a running tab for an idle one would see `LAST EXIT` stay dim until the next status transition), and new `createTab` / `closeTab` wrappers so `TABS` reflects opens and closes immediately — neither `setTabStatus` nor `activateTab` fires on open/close, so without these wrappers the pill would stay stale until the next command ran in any tab. Per the semantic-color contract, stale metadata = muted; the value is preserved so the viewer can still reference the prior exit, but the pill no longer competes with the active run's status pill for attention.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — this is a label rename + render-format tweak + a one-branch color-gate addition, no new behavioral primitive. A repo-wide grep for `hud-runs` / `hudRuns` / `_renderRuns` returns zero hits (besides the decision text in `TODO.md:179`), confirming the rename is complete across `index.html`, `shell_chrome.js`, and nothing else. Existing Playwright and Vitest coverage does not assert the old id or label and passes unchanged. Visual verification: HUD exercised at all three states (no tabs, tabs with none running, tabs with one or more running) and on the active-tab-running + tab-switch paths; `TABS` pill renders the new format and `LAST EXIT` dims to muted only while the active tab is running, un-dims on completion and on switching to an idle tab. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 632 Vitest + 179 Playwright = 1,647 tests (unchanged).
- **Snapshot metadata hierarchy now promotes the expiry line above the run-meta row** — this is a narrow tonal and weight polish pass on the existing permalink header only, with no new fields, server-side changes, or DOM elements.
  - **Before:** the permalink header's four rows — `.export-title` (20px green glow), `.export-meta` (label + created, 10px muted uppercase), `.export-run-meta` (exit badge + duration/lines/version, 10px mixed semantic/muted uppercase), and `.permalink-expiry` (10px amber uppercase) — shared identical type treatment from row 2 onward: `font-size: 10px; letter-spacing: 1.5px; text-transform: uppercase`. Color was the only differentiator, so `.permalink-expiry` (the one row the viewer should actually act on — "this page expires in N hours") read at the same visual weight as the secondary metadata. Hierarchy was color-only; weight hierarchy was flat.
  - **After:** `.permalink-expiry` bumped to `font-size: 11px; font-weight: 700` — both values already in the app's existing vocabulary (11px shared with `shell.css:563`, 700 shared with `.meta-badge` and other uppercase-eyebrow styles across `base.css` / `components.css` / `shell.css`). Color stays `var(--amber)` per the semantic contract (expiring = amber, not `--text`). Run-meta items intentionally untouched: they already use `var(--muted)` which is the app's canonical dim convention — inventing an `opacity: 0.75` second-tier dim would have been a one-off that drifted from the shared muted token. Net result is three weight tiers in the header instead of a flat two: title (20px/300) → created + exit badge + run-meta (10px/400–700 depending on semantic role) → expiry (11px/700). The change is one CSS rule in `components.css` scoped to `body.permalink-page`; no markup or JS touched, no impact on standalone HTML exports (which omit the expiry row) or diagnostics (which doesn't carry a permalink expiry).
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — the change is a two-property CSS bump with no new behavior. Existing permalink e2e coverage (`tests/js/e2e/permalink.spec.js`) passes unchanged. Visual verification: expiry row now reads as the most prominent metadata line below the title, amber color against the muted run-meta row above it, across all 17 themes. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 632 Vitest + 179 Playwright = 1,647 tests (unchanged).
- **The rail collapsed state now communicates available navigation more clearly** — there is no auto-switch to the skinny icon rail when both sections collapse; this is a convergence on the shared disclosure primitive, a missing-count fix, a layout correction so both collapsed sections stack at the top of the split area instead of one-at-top / one-at-bottom, and a glyph-alignment compensation on the workflow drill chevrons.
  - **Before:** section chevs (▸ rotating to ▾) lived on a bespoke `.rail-section-chev` class in `shell-chrome.css` that duplicated the shared `.disclosure-chev` primitive in `components.css` — same glyph, same 90° rotation, but keyed off a `.closed` class via `.rail-section:not(.closed) .rail-section-chev { transform: rotate(90deg); }` instead of the primitive's `[aria-expanded="true"]` selector, and sized 18px vs the primitive's 24px. Drift. When both sections were collapsed, a `.rail-spacer` element (displayed via `.rail-split-area.workflows-closed .rail-spacer { display: block }`) pushed the Workflows header to the bottom of the split-area, leaving a large empty vertical void between the two section headers — inconsistent with every standard sidebar UI (VS Code, JetBrains, Finder sidebars) where collapsed sections stack toward the top. The Workflows section header lacked a count element, so when closed it showed bare `WORKFLOWS` with no "N items hidden, click to expand" signal, while Recent showed `RECENT 12` — asymmetric. Chev glyphs on the section headers (▸/▾) and on the `.drill-chev` › codepoint used for workflow rows both sat off their labels' visual centerlines, since the ▸ codepoint renders in the upper half of its em-box and the › codepoint renders in the lower half — neither had a compensation at the rail surface.
  - **After:** both section chevs now use the shared `.disclosure-chev` primitive from `components.css`, with rotation driven by the primitive's `[aria-expanded="true"]` selector that `bindDisclosure` already writes on the header `<button>`. A surface-scoped `.rail-section-header .disclosure-chev { font-size: 18px; width: 14px; opacity: 0.9; transform: translateY(2px); }` rule keeps the rail's tighter information density and pulls the glyph onto the uppercase label's visual centerline; the paired `.rail-section-header[aria-expanded="true"] .disclosure-chev { transform: translateY(2px) rotate(90deg); }` composes the nudge with the primitive's rotation so the offset survives both states. The bespoke `.rail-section-chev` class and its `.closed`-keyed rotation rule are deleted. `.rail-spacer` element (`#rail-spacer` in `index.html`) and its two CSS rules are deleted; sections now collapse upward — when both are closed, both headers stack at the top of the split-area. Recent-open + Workflows-closed still sits the Workflows header at the bottom naturally (Recent's default `flex: 1 1 auto` fills the remaining space), so the only behavioral change is in the both-closed case. The `.rail-split-area.workflows-closed .rail-section-workflows { border-top: 1px solid var(--border); }` separator stays as a visual demarcation between the collapsed headers. Workflows header gained a `<span class="rail-section-count" id="rail-workflows-count">` element, populated from `allWorkflows.length` on every `renderRailWorkflows` call in `shell_chrome.js`. A surface-scoped `.rail-section-workflows .rail-item .drill-chev { transform: translateY(-4px); }` rule pulls the › glyph up onto the first-line visual midline without disturbing the two-line wrap behavior (`align-items: flex-start` is kept on `.rail-section-workflows .rail-item` so the chev still pins to the first line when a long workflow title wraps via `.line-clamp-2`).
