  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — the change is markup + CSS + one JS wire-up (`railWorkflowsCount.textContent = String(allWorkflows.length)` in `renderRailWorkflows`), no new behavioral logic worth unit-covering. Existing e2e specs (`tests/js/e2e/ui-capture.desktop.capture.js`, `tests/js/e2e/interaction-contract.spec.js`) preserve their `#rail-section-workflows` + `.closed` class assertions and continue to pass. A repo-wide grep for `rail-spacer`, `railSpacer`, and `rail-section-chev` returns zero hits, confirming the delete is complete across templates, CSS, and JS. Visual verification: rail exercised under `docker compose up` at all four state combinations (both open, Recent-only open, Workflows-only open, both closed); glyph centerlines now read as aligned on the section headers and on the workflow drill rows; workflow count updates live when workflows are added/removed. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 632 Vitest + 179 Playwright = 1,647 tests (unchanged).
- **Themed native desktop form controls now power the Options modal, with `.form-*` class names pinned for future reuse** — only the Options modal (3× `<select>`, 2× `<input type="checkbox">`) and the dynamically-built share-redaction "remember this choice" checkbox consume the new class names today, but the primitives are ready for broader reuse. `<select>` gains a themed closed-state arrow so it looks app-native rather than browser-native across 17 themes, and `<checkbox>` / `<radio>` gain explicit size, hover, and `:focus-visible` ring states. The `.form-check input[type="radio"]` rule ships with no caller yet, pinning the primitive shape so the first radio-backed surface inherits it without re-derivation. Mobile keeps native rendering.
  - **Before:** `.options-select`, `.options-choice`, and `.options-fieldset` were Options-modal-scoped one-offs. The `<select>` trigger rendered with each browser's native arrow — chevron-down in Chrome, stepper in Safari, whatever Firefox picked — so the closed state looked browser-native instead of theme-native across 17 themes. Checkbox / radio had `accent-color: var(--green)` only; no explicit sizing (native UA default, ~13px on Chrome, ~15px on Safari), no visible focus ring (relied on native UA focus chrome that varies by browser and gets suppressed entirely under `appearance: none`), no hover state on the wrapper label. Radio had zero styling because no caller existed yet, so the first radio-backed surface would have had to re-derive the primitive mid-build. Theme token `options_select_bg` mapped to `--theme-options-select-bg` and drove only the select's background — the name implied Options-scope even though the class could reasonably live on any themed select.
  - **After:** three generic primitives in `shell.css` — `.form-fieldset` (flex column wrapper, 10px gap), `.form-check` (label wrapping `<input type="checkbox|radio"> + <span>`), and `.form-select` (themed `<select>` with `appearance: none`). The select arrow is drawn in pure CSS via two overlapping `linear-gradient()` background images that form a ▾ in `var(--text)` color — no SVG data URIs (would have required hardcoded arrow color or per-theme variants), and the themed background override in `body .form-select` is explicitly `background-color: var(--theme-form-control-bg)` (not the `background` shorthand) so the arrow gradient survives the theme-layer override. Checkbox / radio get explicit 14×14 sizing, `cursor: pointer`, the canonical `green-dim outline + 3px green-glow box-shadow` focus ring shared with the button primitive, and a subtle hover on the wrapper label (muted → text color) so hovering feels responsive without touching the native input chrome. Radio support is pinned in the primitive even though no caller exists yet; when the first radio-backed surface lands it inherits the primitive with no re-derivation. Theme token consolidated: `options_select_bg` renamed to `form_control_bg` in all 17 theme YAMLs + both `.yaml.example` files + `_THEME_CSS_ORDER` / bootstrap-defaults in `app/config.py` + `scripts/generate_theme_examples.py` + the `THEME.md` token-reference row; per-theme value unchanged (pure rename). `--theme-options-select-bg` → `--theme-form-control-bg` in `base.css`. The proposed `--theme-form-control-accent` was dropped because `var(--green)` is already per-theme and already audited for WCAG AA across every shipped theme — a separate accent token would be pure duplication. The three `<select>` (`options-ts-select`, `options-welcome-select`, `options-share-redaction-select`) and two `<checkbox>` (`options-ln-toggle`, `options-notify-toggle`) in the Options modal migrated to the new class names, plus the dynamic `_buildShareRedactionRememberField()` helper in `app.js` that builds a checkbox inside a confirmation modal. The mobile padding rule (`body.mobile-terminal-mode .options-choice`) in `mobile.css` renamed alongside; no other mobile behavior changed because mobile still keeps native rendering.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — this is a rename + styling change with no new behavioral primitive, and the Options modal's runtime wiring (listeners, persistence, dispatch) is unchanged, so existing `app.test.js` / `options.test.js` coverage suffices. A fresh repo-wide `grep` for `options-select|options-choice|options-fieldset|options_select_bg|--theme-options-select-bg` returns zero hits, confirming the rename is complete and nothing in tests/docs still references the old names. Visual verification: the existing theme capture pack covers the Options modal across all 17 themes; the chevron and checkbox/radio states render identically post-rename except for the new `:hover` border-brighten on selects and the new `:focus-visible` ring on checks/radios. Net suite delta: 836 pytest + 632 Vitest + 179 Playwright = 1,647 tests (unchanged).
- **A shared confirmation-dialog primitive now replaces every bespoke confirm modal** — every destructive or mode-switching confirmation in the shell now resolves through a single declarative helper instead of its own bespoke markup, show/hide helpers, backdrop wiring, and dispatcher entries.
  - **Before:** five confirmation surfaces (`#kill-overlay`, `#hist-del-overlay`, `#share-redaction-overlay`, `#session-token-set-overlay`, `#session-token-migrate-overlay`) each hand-rolled their own markup, `showXxxOverlay` / `hideXxxOverlay` / `isXxxOverlayOpen` helpers, `bindDismissible` registration, `bindMobileSheet` registration, affirmative-button listener, composer-refocus dance, and — in the case of kill — a dedicated Enter-to-confirm keydown branch in `controller.js`. Escape and backdrop paths were re-implemented per surface with slightly different semantics. Two legacy theme tokens (`kill_modal_bg`, `hist_del_modal_bg`) shipped in all 17 theme YAMLs but only one (`--theme-confirm-modal-bg`) actually reached the DOM after the kill pilot, so light-theme confirm modals rendered dark regardless of the theme's palette.
  - **After:** one declarative primitive `showConfirm({body, content, tone, actions, defaultFocus}) → Promise<actionId | null>` in `app/static/js/ui_confirm.js`, backed by a single pre-minted `#confirm-host` node that all five surfaces reuse. `content` accepts a `Node` or array-of-`Node`s for callers that need their own input fields or inline error elements (session-token set ships an `<input>` + `<span class="input-err">`); `onActivate` on an action returns truthy/undefined to close or falsy to keep the modal open so async validation (session-token format check + `/session/token/verify` fail-closed call) can gate resolution inline; `defaultFocus` accepts a `Node` (wins literally), a string (looks up by action id), or falls back to the `role: 'cancel'` button so Enter routes to the safe action via the browser's native button activation; buttons stack when `actions.length >= 3` or viewport matches `(max-width: 480px)`. Migrated in this ship: `#hist-del-overlay` (single-delete, bulk delete-all, delete-non-favorites); `#share-redaction-overlay` (cancel / raw / redacted, respects the persisted share-redaction preference and short-circuits before ever opening when set); `#session-token-set-overlay` (input + error slot + async verify gating); `#session-token-migrate-overlay` (skip / yes-migrate). Commit 1's kill pilot stays on the same primitive. Dead markup, CSS, and JS deleted: four overlay divs in `index.html`; eight `showXxxOverlay` / `hideXxxOverlay` / `isXxxOverlayOpen` functions plus their dom refs; four `setupDismissibleOverlays` registrations collapsed into the single `#confirm-host` registration; four `bindMobileSheet` calls similarly collapsed; seven `#hist-del-modal` / `#share-redaction-modal` / `#session-token-set-modal` / `#session-token-migrate-modal` selectors in `shell.css` and `mobile.css`. Theme tokens consolidated: `kill_modal_bg` + `hist_del_modal_bg` removed from all 17 theme YAMLs, both `.yaml.example` files, and the `_THEME_CSS_ORDER` / bootstrap-defaults lists in `app/config.py`; replaced by a single `confirm_modal_bg` that maps to `--theme-confirm-modal-bg` and drives `.modal-card-compact`. This also fixes a latent commit-1 regression where confirm modals rendered dark (`#141414`) on light themes because `--theme-confirm-modal-bg` had only a base-layer fallback — every theme now carries its own `confirm_modal_bg`, and the "Semantic Color Contract" and token reference in `THEME.md` dropped to a single row. `#confirm-host { z-index: 340 }` in `shell.css` keeps the dialog above `#options-overlay` (z-index 320) even with the primitive sharing the default `.modal-overlay` stacking context.
  - **Tests:** 12 new Vitest cases extend `tests/js/unit/ui_confirm.test.js` to 39 (was 27): 5 in `content slot` (single Node, array of Nodes, non-Node items skipped, clears on resolve, clears stale content between opens), 6 in `onActivate gating` (sync-false keeps open, sync-true closes, async-pending keeps open, async-truthy closes, sync-throw keeps open, async-reject keeps open), 1 in `defaultFocus Node` (explicit Node wins over role:cancel). `tests/js/unit/app.test.js` loses the two obsolete `wires the history delete modal…` / `wires the share redaction modal…` suites and gains one `routes hist-clear-all through confirmHistAction` case to assert the toolbar button still triggers the shared prompt. `tests/js/unit/history.test.js` replaces dead `hist-del-*` fixtures with a `#confirm-host` template matching production. E2E migrations: `history.spec.js`, `failure-paths.spec.js`, `shortcuts.spec.js`, `helpers.js`, and both capture specs retarget the old per-modal selectors onto `#confirm-host [data-confirm-action-id="…"]` (ids: `one` / `cancel` / `nonfav` / `all` for hist-del; `cancel` / `raw` / `redacted` for share-redaction; `cancel` / `apply` for session-token-set; `skip` / `yes` for session-token-migrate). The `ui_confirm.js` header comment was rewritten to describe the primitive's current contract rather than list the replaced helper family. Net suite delta: 632 Vitest (+11), 836 pytest, 179 Playwright = 1,647 tests.
- **A shared button primitive system now drives the shell's high-value CTA surfaces** — confirmations, desktop HUD actions, search toggles, tab actions, and per-surface close buttons now build on one composable vocabulary instead of re-deriving chrome per surface. A few lower-priority button-like surfaces remain intentionally deferred in the backlog — `rail-nav-item` (5 instances on the desktop rail), `rail-collapse-btn`, `tabs-scroll-btn` (×2), `chrome-btn` (×3 on the terminal chrome toolbar), `history-action-btn` (3 template sites plus 3 JS-generated buttons per history row in `history.js`), and `sheet-clear-btn`.
  - **Before:** button visuals were scattered across ~10 surface-scoped class families (`.term-action-btn`, `.hud-action-btn`, `.hud-kill-btn`, `.tab-kill-btn-danger`, `.modal-primary*`, `.modal-secondary*`, `.search-toggle`, plus per-surface close buttons `.faq-close`/`.options-close`/`.theme-close`/`.shortcuts-close`/`.workflows-close`/`.history-panel-close`/`.search-close-btn`/`.sheet-close`) that each re-derived padding, border, radius, hover, and disabled semantics. Confirmation modals mixed `.modal-primary-danger` / `.modal-primary-warning` / `.modal-primary-accent` without a contract; the desktop HUD had no hover effect on share-snapshot / copy / save / clear because the old `.hud-action-btn` rule had no `:hover` branch. Search case/regex toggles used a bespoke `.active` class instead of `aria-pressed`, so the pressed state was invisible to assistive tech.
  - **After:** five composable primitives in `components.css` — `.btn` (role × tone × size × state), `.nav-item`, `.close-btn`, `.toggle-btn`, `.kb-key`. Role is one of `primary | secondary | ghost | destructive`; tone is one of `accent | warning | danger`; size is `default | compact`; state reads through `aria-disabled` / `aria-busy` / `aria-pressed` instead of per-surface `.active` / `.is-*` classes. A local custom property `--_tone` flows through roles so tone overrides don't require long `:is()` selectors. Semantic tone upgrades: reversible destructive (`hist-del` confirm, session-token rotate) ships `btn-warning` (amber on hover), irreversible destructive (session-token clear, kill confirm) ships `btn-destructive` (red tint at rest). Migrated: five confirmation modals (kill, hist-del, share-redaction, session-token-set, session-token-migrate); options session-token row; permalink/permalink_error/diag templates; all eight overlay close buttons (now `close-btn` + kept surface class as a JS hook); search case/regex toggles now `toggle-btn` driven by `aria-pressed`; `tabs.js::_createTabActionButton` and the `saveBtn`; `shell_chrome.js::_makeHudBtn` (desktop HUD Kill / share snapshot / copy / save / clear). Retired CSS families: `.modal-primary*`, `.modal-secondary*`, `.term-action-btn`, `.hud-action-btn`, `.hud-kill-btn`, `.tab-kill-btn-danger`, `.search-toggle` / `.search-toggle:hover` / `.search-toggle.active`, `body .star-btn.starred`. The shared `.u-hidden` escape hatch needed a scoped override for the primitives (`.btn.u-hidden, .nav-item.u-hidden, .close-btn.u-hidden, .toggle-btn.u-hidden { display: none }`) because the primitive's `display: inline-flex` beats a single-class `display: none` by CSS load order; the earlier `!important` shortcut was reverted after it stomped inline `style.display='flex'` set by `showModalOverlay()` and hid the kill confirmation modal entirely. `.tab-close` is an intentional exception — its circular chrome, per-theme tokens, and parent-hover opacity reveal don't fit the primitive model and the class is documented as the single permanent surface outside the primitive family. Test selectors updated: the Playwright kill-path specs (`kill.spec.js`, `runner-stall.spec.js`, `ui-capture.desktop.capture.js`) moved from the retired `.hud-kill-btn` class selector to the stable `#hud-actions [data-action="kill"]` data-attribute selector, and `test_routes.py` rewrote its rendered-HTML assertion for the `/diag` back button from the old `term-action-btn diag-back-btn` class string to `btn btn-secondary btn-compact diag-back-btn`.
  - **Tests:** one new regression-guard test file `tests/js/unit/button_primitives.test.js` with 12 cases — scans `app/static/css`, `app/static/js`, and `app/templates` and fails if any retired class name (`term-action-btn`, `hud-kill-btn`, `hud-action-btn`, `tab-kill-btn-danger`, `modal-primary`, `modal-primary-danger`, `modal-primary-warning`, `modal-primary-accent`, `modal-secondary`, `modal-secondary-warning`, `modal-secondary-neutral`, `search-toggle`) reappears in app source. Token-boundary matching (negative lookbehind/lookahead on `[\w-]`) keeps the `.search-toggles` wrapper and `#search-toggle-btn` id valid while catching any future reintroduction of the bare `.search-toggle` class. Visual verification: all five confirmation modals, the options session-token row, search toggles, desktop HUD, and per-tab mobile terminal actions re-rendered and interacted with across all 17 themes. Net suite delta: 596 Vitest (+12), 836 pytest, 179 Playwright all pass.
- **The semantic color contract is now explicit and enforced across the theme system** — warning, destructive, success, and neutral metadata colors now have a documented contract and corrected consumers.
  - **Before:** semantic color usage was conventional, not contractual. `--amber` was reached for whenever something was "notable" — snapshot-not-found headings, `faq-a code` inline code, `allowed-chip` labels, diag config `false`/`null` values, diag `failed` outcome counts — blurring the line between "warning" and "neutral metadata" and between "warning" and "error". Five themes also shipped a `--green` token that wasn't actually green: `charcoal_amber` and `ember_obsidian` used warm amber-ochre hues that collided with `--amber` (Δhue < 10°), while `charcoal_steel` / `charcoal_violet` / `cobalt_obsidian` overloaded `--green` with the theme's primary accent (blue / violet / cobalt-blue) so "diag-ok" dots rendered in the accent hue rather than reading as green.
  - **After:** codified four-color contract lifted into a new "Semantic Color Contract" section in `THEME.md` — `yellow = caution / reversible destructive / expiring / in-progress`, `red = destructive / kill / error / irreversible`, `green = completed success / enabled / current-focus`, `dim = neutral metadata`, plus three named exceptions (starred items, search-hit highlights, macOS-style window-control minimize button). Code-level violations fixed: `components.css` permalink snapshot-not-found heading moved from `--amber` to `--red` (it's an error, not a caution); `shell.css` `.faq-a code` moved from `--amber` to `--text` and `.allowed-chip` from `--amber` to `--muted` (both are neutral metadata, not cautions); `diag.html` config rows for `none`/`false` values swapped `diag-warn` for a new `diag-muted` class (also new `.diag-muted { color: var(--muted); }` in `diag.css`) and the `outcomes.failed` count moved from `diag-warn` to `diag-fail` (it's an error, not a caution). Theme-level green restored: `charcoal_amber` / `ember_obsidian` / `charcoal_steel` / `charcoal_violet` / `cobalt_obsidian` converge on `green: #6bb36a` (muted sage) with paired `green_dim: #4a7c4a` and a matching `green_glow` (per-theme opacity preserved). Theme chrome identity (toolbar / tab / chip hardcoded hexes) stays on each theme's accent palette, so the warm amber identity of `charcoal_amber` / `ember_obsidian` and the blue / violet accents of the three obsidians persist; only consumers of `var(--green)` (diag OK dots, completion indicators, welcome ASCII glow, macOS-style maximize button) shift to a true green. Audit: `hue(--green) ∈ [89°, 162°]` and `|hue(--green) − hue(--amber)| > 60°` in all 17 shipped themes.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — rule enforcement is by inspection and by the `test_docs.py` contract suite (still 21/21). Visual verification: diag page reloaded under all 17 themes; OK dots render green and distinct from amber / red / muted values in every theme.
- **Trust, clarity, and consistency pass across rail, disclosures, and mobile running-state signaling** — the first UI review bundle tackled the highest-signal "I can't tell what's happening / what this does / what's selected" issues in one pass so later polish could build on shared primitives.
  - **Rail workflow titles wrap to two lines instead of truncating mid-word.**
    - **Before:** the desktop rail's `Workflows` rows ran the workflow title through `text-overflow: ellipsis`, which clipped names like `Common nmap port scans` after the first word and made the whole list read as broken.
    - **After:** decision recorded in `TODO.md` was to wrap to two lines and truncate beyond. New shared utility `.line-clamp-2` in `base.css` (`-webkit-line-clamp: 2` + `word-break: break-word`) is applied to `.rail-item-text` in the workflows section via `shell_chrome.js::renderRailWorkflows`. `.rail-section-workflows .rail-item` switches to `align-items: flex-start; white-space: normal` so a wrapped title doesn't push the row's drill chev off-baseline; `min-width: 0` on `.rail-item-text` lets the wrap actually engage inside the flex parent. Hover tooltip (`title=`) now contains both the full title and the description on separate lines so titles cut off after line two stay discoverable. Recent rows are intentionally untouched — they are short by construction (command names) and were not part of the reported readability problem.
    - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified visually across the desktop rail at narrow and wide widths with built-in workflow names.
  - **Theme picker has a single shared selected-card visual on desktop and mobile.**
    - **Before:** the desktop theme cards used a custom `.theme-card-active` rule with a thin border and 1px ring that read as "hovered" rather than "selected"; `:hover` and `:focus-visible` rules on the same element overrode it as soon as the user moused or tabbed back onto the card.
    - **After:** decision recorded in `TODO.md` was visual treatment alone, no `active` badge. New `.is-selected-card` primitive in `components.css` (bright `--green` border + 2px green-glow ring + soft halo + theme-aware drop shadow) lives at the component layer so future selectable surfaces (workflow / preset pickers) can adopt the same visual without re-deriving it. `.theme-card-active` is retained on the DOM for back-compat with anything that might query it but no longer carries the visual; `:hover:not(.is-selected-card)` and `:focus-visible:not(.is-selected-card)` guards added to `.theme-card` rules in `shell.css` so the selected visual wins when the user hovers or tabs back. `syncThemeSelectionControls` in `app.js` toggles both classes in lockstep across desktop and mobile theme cards (any node with `[data-theme-name]`), so the shared primitive is now applied on mobile as well — mobile's existing strong selected visual remained visually dominant, so no mobile-specific style tweak was needed on top of the shared primitive.
    - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified visually across all 17 themes in the desktop and mobile theme pickers.
  - **Disclosure language follows behaviour, not visual hierarchy.**
    - **Before:** rail headers, mobile menu rows, and recents-sheet filter affordances mixed expand-collapse, drill-in, and dropdown chev shapes inconsistently — users couldn't infer "this expands inline" vs "this opens a sheet" vs "this opens a dropdown" from the affordance alone.
    - **After:** codified meta-rule — `▸/▾` for inline expand/collapse, `›` for navigation/drill-in (sheet, modal, panel), rotating `▾` only for true dropdown/popover triggers, no glyph on toggle rows (the on/off label is the affordance). Two new shared glyph primitives in `components.css`: `.disclosure-chev` (rotating `▸` that flips to `▾` via `[aria-expanded="true"] .disclosure-chev`) and `.drill-chev` (static `›`). Applied across surfaces: rail `Recent` / `Workflows` section chevs scaled up (`width: 14px`, `font-size: 18px`) so the rotation is legible; rail workflow rows tagged `.drill-chev`; mobile menu drill rows (`search`, `history`, `workflows`, `options`, `theme`, `FAQ`, `diag`) now use `.menu-item-chev.drill-chev` with `›`; mobile menu `timestamps` row swapped its drill `›` for the rotating `.disclosure-chev` `▸` because it actually expands an inline submenu; mobile menu `line numbers` row dropped its glyph entirely (the `off`/`on` label is the affordance); recents-sheet `filters` toggle gained the rotating `.disclosure-chev` (with a 2px translateY on the surface to align the `▸` codepoint to the row centerline); recents-sheet exit/date dropdown carets switched from `⌄` to `▾`. Mobile-chrome's per-element rotation rule for `.menu-item-expander` retired because the primitive owns it now.
    - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified visually across rail, mobile menu sheet, and recents sheet open/closed states.
  - **Mobile non-active running-state indicator.**
    - **Before:** mobile's status pill only ever reflects the active tab, so a long-running scan on a backgrounded tab was invisible from the system chrome until the user manually switched to it.
    - **After:** trailing-edge tab-bar chip showing the count of running non-active tabs (cycle through them on tap, in tab-row order), plus left/right amber edge glows that pulse when a running tab is currently scrolled off-screen. New module section in `mobile_chrome.js` mounts both surfaces idempotently. Chip is a natural flex child appended after `.tabs-bar` so the flex layout reserves its space; styled in `mobile.css` using `color-mix(in srgb, var(--amber) 12%, var(--theme-panel-alt-bg))` so it tracks the same `--amber` token as `.status-pill.running` / `.tab-status.running`. Chip tap activates the next running tab via `window.activateTab(id, { focusComposer: false })` and then assigns `tabsBarEl.scrollLeft` directly to centre the newly-active tab — `scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' })` and `scrollTo({ behavior: 'smooth' })` are both silently dropped by iOS Safari on the first call to a cold (never-scrolled) horizontal container, so direct `scrollLeft` assignment is the only path that reliably works on the first tap (this iOS quirk is now recorded in `feedback_ios_smooth_scroll_cold.md`). Edge glows are `position: fixed` overlays parented to `document.body` rather than children of `.tabs-bar`; the JS computes their coordinates from `tabsBarEl.getBoundingClientRect()` on every sync, because empirically (confirmed 2026-04-19) `position: sticky` inside a horizontal `display: flex; overflow-x: auto` container and `position: absolute` children of a `position: relative` flex parent both destabilise iOS Safari momentum scroll on `.tabs-bar`. Resync triggers: rAF-coalesced `MutationObserver` on `.tabs-bar` (attribute-filter `class` for tab status changes; childList for tab add/remove), `window.resize`, and a 120ms-debounced `.tabs-bar` scroll listener that updates edge-glow direction once the finger lifts. The pre-existing pull-to-refresh `touchmove` guard in `mobile_chrome.js` was tightened in the same change to bail out for predominantly-horizontal gestures (`Math.abs(dx) >= Math.abs(dy)`) — without that bail, the guard's vertical-axis-only ancestor walk skipped `.tabs-bar` (which has `overflow-y: hidden`) and `preventDefault`'d the touchmove, blocking horizontal tab-bar scroll roughly 90% of the time; the rule is now recorded in `feedback_overscroll_behavior_inert.md` as the critical gotcha. Kill switch: append `?ri=off` (or `?ri=0`) to skip mounting the chip and observers entirely. The mobile header status pill is intentionally untouched — it remains the canonical run-state surface for the active tab.
    - **Tests:** no new automated cases — these surfaces are iOS-Safari-specific (the smooth-scroll cold-container bug doesn't reproduce in Chromium-based Playwright). Verified manually on iOS Safari that chip-tap activation + scroll-to-centre works on the first tap (cold container) and on subsequent taps (warm), edge glows hide/show on the correct side, `?ri=off` cleanly skips both surfaces, and horizontal tab-bar scroll works reliably after the touchmove-guard fix.
- **UI Interaction Helper Refactor — ~80 hand-rolled UI interaction sites across `app/static/js` now flow through a shared helper family** so that focus restoration, pressed/highlight cleanup, disclosures, dismissibles, and ambient outside-click dismissal behave consistently instead of being re-implemented per control. Resolves the `Interaction state does not reset consistently after chrome actions` known issue in `TODO.md`. Every helper in the family follows the `bindMobileSheet()` prior-art shape: one function, element + options bag, asserts its preconditions, idempotent via a `data-*-bound` guard, returns a disposable handle. Composition order: `bindPressable` → `bindDisclosure` (composes pressable) → `bindDismissible` (composes pressable for close buttons) → `bindOutsideClickClose` (ambient companion to dismissible).
  - **Post-action composer refocus now runs through `refocusComposerAfterAction()` in `ui_helpers.js`.** The previously-existing helper already handled the mobile-skip / `preventScroll` / `getVisibleComposerInput` decisions that most call sites were silently missing; it gained a `{ defer: true }` option to preserve the retired `refocusTerminalInput()`'s `setTimeout(0)` semantics (chrome-close paths that need to let a pending blur finish before re-focusing can opt in without regressions), and `preventScroll` now defaults to `true` (legacy `refocusTerminalInput` used `false`), removing scroll-into-view jank when chrome surfaces close.
    - Retired paths: `refocusTerminalInput()` in `app.js`, `refocusTabsTerminalInput()` in `tabs.js`, `focusComposerInputAfterRun()` in `runner.js`, bare `focusAnyComposerInput()` calls across seven files, raw `cmdInput.focus()` fallbacks, `setTimeout(0)`-wrapped variations.
    - Migrated ~46 call sites: 20 in `controller.js`, 6 in `app.js`, 6 in `tabs.js` (incl. removing the local `refocusTabsTerminalInput` wrapper), 5 in `welcome.js`, 3 in `runner.js` (incl. removing local `focusComposerInputAfterRun`), 2 in `autocomplete.js`, 2 in `controller.js` keypress-redirect paths, 1 in `shell_chrome.js`, 1 in `history.js`, and the raw `cmdInput.focus()` fallback in `ui_helpers.js`'s `hideSearchBar`.
    - Intentionally left alone: two bare `focusAnyComposerInput({ preventScroll: true })` sites inside `performMobileEditAction` in `app.js` — they must force focus onto the *mobile* composer specifically, the opposite of the chrome-action semantics the canonical helper encodes.
    - Test harness: `tests/js/unit/app.test.js` export list and the `does not programmatically focus the mobile composer` case now reference `refocusComposerAfterAction({ defer: true })` instead of the removed `refocusTerminalInput`.
    - Net suite delta: 475/475 Vitest, 731/731 pytest, 169/169 Playwright all pass — no count change, no behaviour regressions.
  - **Pressable controls now share one activation contract via `bindPressable(el, { onActivate, refocusComposer, preventFocusTheft, preventScroll, defer, clearPressStyle })` in `app/static/js/ui_pressable.js`.** It replaces 9 hand-rolled activation paths and is idempotent via `data-pressable-bound`.
    - Contract: click always activates; `Enter`/`Space` activate only on non-`<button>` elements so native buttons don't double-fire (the browser already dispatches click for Enter/Space on real buttons); `el.blur()` clears native `:focus` styling when the element owns focus; `clearPressStyle` opt-in toggles `data-pressable-clearing="1"` for one animation frame so per-surface CSS can un-style sticky `:hover`/`:active`/`.is-pressed` residue on `role="button"` divs that cannot be blurred; `preventFocusTheft` binds `pointerdown`+`preventDefault` on primary-button/primary-touch contacts only (multi-touch and right-click pass through); after activation the canonical `refocusComposerAfterAction({ preventScroll, defer })` runs unless `refocusComposer: false` (opt-out used by disclosure triggers so a just-opened dropdown keeps user attention).
    - Migrated: the four `setTimeout(() => btn.blur(), 0)` call sites (`history.js` copy/permalink/delete rows, `tabs.js` save-menu items with its `save-menu` disclosure opt-out); `_makeHudBtn` factory in `shell_chrome.js` (Kill, share snapshot, copy, save, clear, plus save-menu items inside the HUD dropdown); `_recentsMakeAction` factory in `mobile_chrome.js` and the recents-sheet `role="button"` star element; `mobile-recent-peek` pull-up tile; desktop rail Recent and Workflows section headers; FAQ question toggles in `app.js` (the concrete `role="button"` div bug behind the refactor); three welcome-command activation sites in `welcome.js` (live `cmdText`, finalized `boundCmdText`, try-this-first badge).
    - Test coverage: new `tests/js/unit/ui_pressable.test.js` with 20 cases — click + keyboard activation for native and non-native buttons, no-double-fire guarantee for native buttons, idempotent re-bind, blur-after-activate, refocus defaults and opt-out, defer and preventScroll pass-through, `preventFocusTheft` primary-vs-secondary pointer semantics, `clearPressStyle` double-`requestAnimationFrame` lifecycle, missing-el / missing-onActivate / missing-refocus-helper guard paths.
    - Test harness: `tests/js/unit/helpers/extract.js` extended to bundle `ui_pressable.js` into every `fromDomScript`/`fromDomScripts` context so downstream module tests see `bindPressable` as a global without per-test wiring; `app/templates/index.html` loads `ui_pressable.js` immediately after `ui_helpers.js`.
    - Net suite delta: 495 Vitest (+20), 833 pytest, 171 Playwright all pass.
  - **Expandable and collapsible controls now share one disclosure contract via `bindDisclosure(trigger, { panel, openClass, hiddenClass, initialOpen, onToggle, stopPropagation, ...pressableOpts })` in `app/static/js/ui_disclosure.js`.** It replaces 5 hand-rolled expand/collapse paths and composes `bindPressable` (the pressable owns click + `Enter`/`Space` + blur + optional refocus; the disclosure owns `aria-expanded` sync + panel class lifecycle + `onToggle` emission). Idempotent via `data-disclosure-bound`.
    - Contract: `aria-expanded` stays in sync with the open flag on every state change; `openClass` toggles on the panel when open (default `'open'`, pass `null` to disable); `hiddenClass` inverse-toggles when closed (for `u-hidden`-style panels); `panel: null` lets the caller own class mutation entirely (used by rail sections where `applySectionsState()` is the sole writer of `.closed`); `onToggle(open, { trigger, panel })` fires on user transitions and on imperative `open()` / `close()` / `toggle()` calls that actually change state, but is deliberately suppressed on the initial sync so binding doesn't trigger side effects; returned handle exposes `isOpen() / open() / close() / toggle()` for imperative coordination (e.g. `tsDisclosure.close()` inside `openMenuSheet()` so the sheet always opens with the submenu collapsed); `stopPropagation: true` opts into `e.stopPropagation()` on the activation event so disclosures can coexist with ambient outside-click dismissal.
    - Migrated: FAQ question toggles in `app.js` (5 aria-only wirings removed; handles collected so `faqHandles[0].open()` replaces the hand-rolled `faq-open` class + aria-expanded on the first item); desktop rail Recent / Workflows section headers in `shell_chrome.js` (`panel: null, openClass: null` so the helper only syncs aria-expanded while `onToggle(open)` updates `ui.recentOpen` / `ui.workflowsOpen`, writes prefs, and calls `applySectionsState()`); mobile timestamps sub-menu in `mobile_chrome.js` (`hiddenClass: 'u-hidden'`); mobile recents advanced filters toggle in `mobile_chrome.js` (`hiddenClass: 'u-hidden'`; `onToggle` closes the recents filter dropdowns on collapse and re-syncs the filter UI). `controller.js` dispatcher for `ts-toggle` simplified to a targeted no-op preserving only "don't close the sheet on ts-toggle" — the disclosure in `mobile_chrome.js` now owns the aria + submenu visibility via the pressable's own click handler.
    - Save-menu dropdowns at `tabs.js:621`, `permalink.js:115`, and `shell_chrome.js:383–384` intentionally waited for the outside-click helper so one migration could fix their disclosure state and dismissal coupling in a single pass.
    - Test coverage: new `tests/js/unit/ui_disclosure.test.js` with 23 cases — initial aria state, custom `openClass`, `hiddenClass` inverse, `panel: null` caller-owns-visibility semantics, `onToggle` emit-only-on-transitions invariant, handle `isOpen` / `open` / `close` / `toggle` idempotency, `data-disclosure-bound` guard, `stopPropagation` opt-in, null guards (missing trigger / opts / `bindPressable`), `refocusComposer` forwarding, `clearPressStyle` forwarding, `Enter` / `Space` activation via the underlying pressable. The `app.test.js` `ts-toggle does not close the mobile sheet` case was rewritten to assert only the controller dispatcher's remaining contract (sheet does not close on ts-toggle); submenu toggle behaviour is now covered in `ui_disclosure.test.js`.
    - Test harness: `tests/js/unit/helpers/extract.js` extended to concatenate `ui_disclosure.js` after `ui_pressable.js` into every `fromDomScript`/`fromDomScripts` bundle; `index.html` loads `ui_disclosure.js` immediately after `ui_pressable.js`.
    - Net suite delta: 518 Vitest (+23), 836 pytest, 171 Playwright all pass.
  - **Dismissible overlays and sheets now share one close contract via `bindDismissible(el, { level, onClose, closeButtons, closeOnBackdrop, backdropEl, stopPropagation })` + `closeTopmostDismissible()` in `app/static/js/ui_dismissible.js`.** It replaces 11 hand-rolled modal/sheet dismissal paths and unifies the Escape cascade. Composes `bindPressable` for each close button (falls back to a plain click listener when the button is already pressable-bound so disclosure-backed close buttons don't double-bind); registers the surface with a shared level-priority dispatcher so a single `closeTopmostDismissible()` call replaces the hand-rolled Escape if-chain in `controller.js`. Idempotent via `data-dismissible-bound`.
    - Contract: `level` is one of `'modal' | 'sheet' | 'panel'` with priority `modal > sheet > panel`; within a level, the most recently registered open surface wins; `isOpen()` defaults to `!el.hidden && !el.classList.contains('u-hidden')` but callers can override for surfaces with bespoke visibility (e.g. history drawer's `.open` class); `closeButtons` accepts a single element or an array; `closeOnBackdrop` defaults to `true` with the default backdrop being the surface itself (click lands on `e.target === el`); sheets with a detached scrim pass `backdropEl: <scrim>` so clicks on the scrim dismiss but clicks inside the sheet body don't; passing `closeOnBackdrop: false` or `backdropEl: null` disables backdrop-click entirely (used by the history drawer because it's a side panel, not a modal).
    - Migrated: nine overlays registered through a new `setupDismissibleOverlays()` in `controller.js` (workflows, faq, theme, options, shortcuts as `level: 'modal'`; historyPanel as `level: 'panel'` with `closeOnBackdrop: false`; killOverlay, histDelOverlay, shareRedactionOverlay as `level: 'modal'`); two mobile bottom sheets in `mobile_chrome.js` (menu sheet + recents sheet, both `level: 'sheet'` with their scrim passed as `backdropEl`).
    - Removed: eight standalone backdrop-click handlers and eight standalone close-button handlers from `controller.js`; two separate click handlers on the menu-sheet scrim / close button and two on the recents-sheet scrim / close button collapsed into their `bindDismissible` registrations in `mobile_chrome.js`; redundant document-level Escape-close handler for mobile sheets in `mobile_chrome.js` removed because the unified dispatcher owns it.
    - Escape handling after the collapse: `controller.js` keydown cascade (lines ~800–832 pre-refactor) is now a short `closeTopmostDismissible()` call. Escape on any dismissible surface dispatches through the registry; the kill-overlay Enter-confirm remains separate (Enter isn't a dismissal); the panels-open gate still swallows non-chrome keys except Escape (so Alt+H still toggles the history panel via `handleChromeShortcut`); the "hide search bar on Escape" path still fires as a secondary fallback because the search bar is not a dismissible. `historyPanel`'s `onClose` preserves the prior `resetHistoryMobileFilters() + hideHistoryPanel()` sequence; `histDelOverlay`'s `onClose` preserves `hideHistoryDeleteOverlay() + pendingHistAction = null`.
    - Test coverage: new `tests/js/unit/ui_dismissible.test.js` with 29 cases — guard paths (missing `el` / missing `onClose` / invalid `level` / duplicate bind), backdrop-click semantics for default / `backdropEl`-override / `closeOnBackdrop: false`, close-button single vs. array vs. already-pressable-bound fallback, handle API (`isOpen() / close() / dispose()`), `closeTopmostDismissible()` dispatcher priority rules (modal beats sheet beats panel; within-level most-recent-open wins; closed surfaces are skipped; registry stays consistent across `dispose()` calls).
    - Test harness: `tests/js/unit/helpers/extract.js` extended to concatenate `ui_dismissible.js` after `ui_disclosure.js` into every `fromDomScript`/`fromDomScripts` bundle so downstream module tests see `bindDismissible` and `closeTopmostDismissible` as globals.
    - Net suite delta: 547 Vitest (+29), 836 pytest, 171 Playwright all pass.
  - **Ambient outside-click dismissal now shares one helper via `bindOutsideClickClose(panel, { triggers, isOpen, onClose, exemptSelectors, scope })` in `app/static/js/ui_outside_click.js`.** It replaces 6 hand-rolled document-level outside-click handlers and encodes the trigger-exemption contract. `bindDismissible` owns scrim/modal-click dismissal for backed surfaces; `bindOutsideClickClose` owns document-level (or scope-overridden) click dismissal for unbacked panels where the trigger sits outside the dismissible surface. Null-guards its preconditions and returns a `{ dispose }` handle.
    - Contract: `panel` may be `null` for sibling-set cases (multiple peer dropdowns sharing a parent — e.g. the two recents filter dropdowns on mobile), in which case containment is decided purely by `triggers` / `exemptSelectors`; `triggers` accepts a single element or array and is matched via `.contains()` (clicks anywhere inside a trigger do not close); `exemptSelectors` is matched via `.closest()` against the click target (clicks landing on or inside any matching ancestor do not close — used for `.hist-chip-overflow` + `[data-action="history"]` on the history panel, `.ac-dropdown` + `#mobile-composer` for autocomplete, `[data-recents-dropdown]` for the recents filter dropdowns); `scope` defaults to `document` but accepts any element (the recents sheet passes itself so only sheet-scoped clicks are evaluated); the handler short-circuits when `isOpen()` returns false so a no-op close is never triggered. Trigger exemption explicitly replaces the hand-rolled `e.stopPropagation()` pattern that every pre-refactor outside-click site used — trigger clicks now flow naturally, and the helper recognises them as part of the surface rather than "outside" clicks.
    - Migrated (six sites): the three near-identical save-menu dropdowns (`tabs.js` per-tab save-menu inside `_createTabPanel`, `shell_chrome.js` HUD save-menu, `permalink.js` save-menu) each collapse a hand-rolled document click listener plus a hand-rolled `e.stopPropagation()` on the trigger into one `bindOutsideClickClose` call with `triggers: saveBtn`; `controller.js` global-dismiss block (three stacked document click listeners for autocomplete, history panel, and mobile menu) collapses to two `bindOutsideClickClose` calls — history panel with `triggers: histBtn` + `exemptSelectors: ['.hist-chip-overflow', '[data-action="history"]']`, autocomplete anchored on `shellPromptWrap` with `exemptSelectors: ['.ac-dropdown', '#mobile-composer']` — with the mobile-menu outside-click deliberately removed as redundant now that the dismissible scrim covers the viewport and handles dismissal there; `mobile_chrome.js` recents filter dropdowns (two sibling dropdowns on one sheet) collapse to a single `bindOutsideClickClose(null, { scope: recentsSheet, exemptSelectors: ['[data-recents-dropdown]'], ... })` with `panel: null` because there is no single containing element — the sibling set is defined entirely by exemption.
    - Removed: three document click handlers in `tabs.js` / `shell_chrome.js` / `permalink.js`; three `e.stopPropagation()` calls on save-menu triggers; three-block Global click block in `controller.js`; `recentsSheet.addEventListener('click', ...)` handler and two `e.stopPropagation()` calls on recents dropdown triggers and option clicks in `mobile_chrome.js`.
    - Post-action close semantics: the old document-level listener in `tabs.js` unconditionally removed `open` on any click (including clicks inside the menu on save-txt/save-html/save-pdf option buttons), so the menu auto-closed after each action; the outside-click helper intentionally does not fire on inside clicks, so `permalink.js` and `tabs.js` now explicitly call `wrap.classList.remove('open')` inside their data-action dispatchers after a save action — matching the explicit `saveWrap.classList.remove('open')` that `shell_chrome.js` already did per-option.
    - Test coverage: new `tests/js/unit/ui_outside_click.test.js` with 19 cases — guard paths (`panel: null` accepted, missing `opts` / `isOpen` / `onClose` each return `null`, handle exposes `dispose`), outside-click dismissal (closes outside, skips inside, skips on element itself, respects `isOpen`), trigger exemption (single, array, nested via `.contains()`, falsy entries ignored), exempt selectors (single, nested via `.closest()`, array), scope override, handle `dispose()` on document and scope-override paths.
    - Test harness: `tests/js/unit/helpers/extract.js` extended with `UI_OUTSIDE_CLICK_SRC` bundled after `UI_DISMISSIBLE_SRC` in both `fromDomScript` and `fromDomScripts`; both templates (`index.html` and `permalink_base.html`) load `ui_outside_click.js` after `ui_dismissible.js`.
    - Net suite delta: 566 Vitest (+19), 836 pytest, 171 Playwright all pass.
  - **Direct focus and blur calls are now narrowed to shared DOM helpers via `focusElement(el, { preventScroll })` and `blurActiveElement()` in `app/static/js/ui_helpers.js`.** `focusElement` collapses the repeated `try { el.focus({ preventScroll: true }) } catch (_) { el.focus() }` pattern into one helper (the try/catch fallback covers engines that reject the options arg), null-guards non-focusable targets, and returns a bool; `blurActiveElement` blurs `document.activeElement` if it is blurrable, returning a bool so call sites can branch cleanly. `focusComposerInput` was refactored to delegate to `focusElement`, eliminating the duplicate try/catch block inside the helper module itself.
    - Migrated: two `searchInput.focus()` sites in `controller.js` (rail action dispatcher + search toggle); session-token-set modal's `input.focus()` in `controller.js`; tab-rename input focus in `tabs.js:1085`; history-filter root-input `focus({ preventScroll: true })` in `history.js:149`; both theme-selector focus targets in `app.js:546–562` (selected card then fallback to themeSelect); `_blurActiveElement()` local in `tabs.js` plus its two call sites in `createTab` and `closeTab`; `chip.blur()` in `history.js:478`.
    - Removed: `focusCommandInputFromGesture` in `app.js` had a dead defensive fallback (`typeof focusComposerInput !== 'function'` branch) that re-implemented the same try/catch in place — `ui_helpers.js` always loads before `app.js`.
    - Intentionally left alone: only two direct focus/blur calls remain outside helper internals — `utils.js:83` (hidden textarea inside the clipboard `execCommand('copy')` fallback; single-shot, self-contained) and `ui_pressable.js:55` (helper-internal blur after activation).
    - Test coverage: new `tests/js/unit/ui_focus_helpers.test.js` with 9 cases — `focusElement` (null-guard, non-focusable-guard, live-focus path, `preventScroll` forwarding, default no-args path, preventScroll-throws fallback) and `blurActiveElement` (null activeElement, non-blurrable activeElement, live-blur path).
    - Net suite delta: 575 Vitest (+9), 836 pytest, 171 Playwright all pass.
  - **The shared interaction contract is now verified end to end in `tests/js/e2e/interaction-contract.spec.js` and documented in `ARCHITECTURE.md`.** It asserts the contract the helpers (`refocusComposerAfterAction`, `focusElement` / `blurActiveElement`, `bindPressable`, `bindDisclosure`, `bindDismissible`, `bindOutsideClickClose`) jointly encode against real mounted chrome surfaces rather than helper fixtures.
    - Eight new Playwright cases: five parametric scrim-overlay tests (FAQ, theme, options, workflows, shortcuts) each exercise all three close paths — explicit close button, backdrop click, `Escape` through the shared `closeTopmostDismissible()` dispatcher — and assert `#cmd` is refocused after every path; one FAQ-question disclosure case verifies `aria-expanded` stays in sync with the `.faq-open` class across a full open/close/open cycle (scoped to `#faq-overlay .faq-body` to avoid the share-redaction modal's reused `.faq-item.modal-inline-field`); one rail-Workflows-header case verifies the `panel: null` caller-owns-visibility path (aria-expanded stays in sync with the section's `.closed` class via `applySectionsState()`); one HUD save-menu case verifies the `bindOutsideClickClose` trigger-exemption contract end-to-end — trigger click toggles (exempt from outside-click dismissal), inside-panel click stays open (helper treats clicks inside the panel element as non-dismissing), outside click (dispatched at `document.body`) closes.
    - Coverage audit before the spec was written confirmed invariants 2 (press-style clears) and 3 (`Enter` / `Space` activation) are thoroughly covered at the Vitest unit level (`ui_pressable.test.js` blur-after-activate + `clearPressStyle` double-rAF, Enter/Space native-vs-non-native gating), so no duplicating E2E cases were added for those.
    - Documentation: `ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a dedicated "UI Interaction Helpers" section documenting each helper's purpose, signature, idempotency guard, and composition with neighbours, plus the six-point shared contract the family enforces. The module load-order listing was refreshed to include the four `ui_*` sibling modules (`ui_pressable.js` → `ui_disclosure.js` → `ui_dismissible.js` → `ui_outside_click.js`), `export_pdf.js`, `mobile_sheet.js`, and `mobile_chrome.js` which were missing from the prior snapshot.
    - Net suite delta: 179 Playwright (+8), 836 pytest, 575 Vitest all pass.
  - **Helper cleanup completed with symmetric `dispose()` support and the remaining pressable stragglers migrated.** No user-visible behavior change; this purely shores up the helper contract so future call sites that need `dispose()` get the symmetric behavior the API claims, and comparable controls in adjacent surfaces share one activation path.
    - `bindDismissible().dispose()` was previously only partially symmetric — it removed the registry entry and dataset flag but left both the backdrop click listener and any close-button listeners attached, so a rebound surface could leak handlers or fire duplicate closes. Both branches now capture references to their installed listeners (the backdrop click handler and either the plain close-button click handler or the underlying `bindPressable` handle) and remove them on `dispose()`.
    - To make that fully symmetric, `bindPressable` itself now returns a `{ dispose }` handle on successful bind (and `null` on guard-fail paths instead of `undefined`); the handle removes the click listener, the keydown listener (for non-native buttons), and the optional `pointerdown` focus-theft listener, and clears the `data-pressable-bound` marker so the element can rebind.
    - Adoption gaps closed: `app/static/js/history.js` (history drawer star action — was raw `addEventListener('click', ...)` while the adjacent copy/permalink/delete actions use `bindPressable`); `app/static/js/mobile_chrome.js` (recents starred filter and recents-clear — both raw click handlers in a sheet whose action rows are otherwise pressable-bound).
    - Test coverage: 6 new `tests/js/unit/ui_pressable.test.js` cases under a `describe('dispose')` block (handle returned on success, null on guard-fail, click listener unwound, keydown listener unwound, pointerdown listener unwound when `preventFocusTheft` was on, `data-pressable-bound` marker cleared); 3 new `tests/js/unit/ui_dismissible.test.js` cases (backdrop click no longer dismisses after dispose, close-button click no longer dismisses in the already-pressable branch, close-button click no longer dismisses in the pressable-bound branch and its `data-pressable-bound` marker is cleared).
    - Net suite delta: 584 Vitest (+9), 836 pytest, 179 Playwright all pass.

#### Keyboard Shortcuts and Discoverability

- **Keyboard shortcut reference now renders per-OS key labels** — the `shortcuts` built-in and the `?` overlay pick `Option` or `Alt` glyphs based on the viewer's platform instead of printing both and asking the reader to translate.
  - **Before:**
    - `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` stored a single printable string per binding.
    - OS-dependent entries listed both variants inline (`Option+T / Alt+T`, `Option+B/F or Alt+B/F`); the UI section quietly settled on `Alt+*` only, with no Mac equivalent shown.
    - A trailing note (`Note: on macOS, use Option for app-safe tab shortcuts; browser Command shortcuts remain environment-dependent.`) asked Mac readers to do the mental translation themselves.
  - **After:**
    - OS-dependent entries in `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` are now `{"mac": "...", "other": "..."}` dicts; universal entries (`?`, every `Ctrl+*` chord, `Up / Down on blank prompt`) stay plain strings.
    - New helpers in `app/fake_commands.py`: `_is_mac_user_agent()` checks the UA for a `Mac` token, `_resolve_shortcut_key()` picks the platform label, and `_detect_mac_from_request()` is a Flask-context-safe UA sniffer (returns `False` outside a request).
    - `get_current_shortcuts(is_mac=None)` accepts an explicit bool for direct callers and falls back to request-based detection; `_run_fake_shortcuts()` now renders through the same resolved payload so the terminal output and the JSON overlay cannot disagree.
    - The old trailing browser-shortcuts note was removed entirely once the bindings rendered per-OS labels natively; the overlay and the built-in now end on the shortcut list itself.
  - **Tests:**
    - `test_fake_shortcuts_lists_current_shortcuts` repinned to the non-Mac default (`Alt+T`, `Alt+Shift+C`, no `Option+` anywhere).
    - New `test_fake_shortcuts_renders_mac_keys_for_mac_user_agent` covers the Macintosh UA path.
    - `TestShortcutsRoute` gains `test_non_mac_user_agent_renders_alt_prefix` and `test_mac_user_agent_renders_option_prefix`.
    - `test_matches_shortcuts_builtin_source` now passes `is_mac=False` explicitly so the direct call matches the Werkzeug default (non-Mac) UA.
    - Net suite delta: 845 pytest (+3) + 666 Vitest + 197 Playwright = **1,708 tests**.
- **Keyboard shortcut reference pruned to real keyboard shortcuts only** — seven entries were removed from the Terminal section of `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` in `app/fake_commands.py` because they described modal conventions or intuitive autocomplete interactions rather than keyboard shortcuts worth surfacing in the overlay: `Welcome:` (type/Enter/Escape to settle the welcome animation), `Kill dialog:` (Enter to confirm / Escape to cancel), `Enter on blank prompt` (append a new empty prompt line), and the four `Autocomplete:` entries (`Up/Down`, `Tab`, `Enter`, `Escape`). The Terminal section now lists eleven bindings — `?`, `Ctrl+C`, `Up/Down on blank prompt`, `Ctrl+R`, `Ctrl+W`, `Ctrl+U`, `Ctrl+A`, `Ctrl+K`, `Ctrl+E`, `Option+B/F or Alt+B/F`, and `Ctrl+L`. The `shortcuts` built-in output and the `?` overlay reflect the pruned list automatically because both read from the same source.
- **Keyboard shortcut reference grouped into three sections** — `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` and its consumers now read as Terminal / Tabs / UI groups rather than a flat list.
  - **Before:** `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` in `app/fake_commands.py` was a flat list of `(key, description)` tuples; the `shortcuts` built-in and the `?` overlay rendered a single `Current shortcuts:` block with every binding mixed together.
  - **After:** restructured into `(section_title, items)` groups covering **Terminal** (composer-scoped — `?`, Ctrl+A/E/K/U/W, Alt+B/F, Ctrl+C/L/R, history cycle), **Tabs** (Option/Alt chord family — new/close/cycle/jump tab, permalink active tab, copy active-tab output), and **UI** (the six `Alt+\` / `Alt+S` / `Alt+H` / `Alt+,` / `Alt+Shift+T` / `Alt+G` chords). `GET /shortcuts` payload changed from a flat `{ items }` shape to `{ sections: [{title, items}, …] }`; `/shortcuts` counts the total via `sum(len(s["items"]))` for telemetry. The `shortcuts` built-in emits a `fake-section`-styled header per group (`Terminal:`, `Tabs:`, `UI:`) with a spacer line between. The overlay renderer (`renderShortcuts` in `controller.js`) iterates sections, renders each title as a full-width `shortcut-section-title` grid cell (blue, bold, `grid-column: 1 / -1`), and skips the top margin on the first title.
  - **Tests:** one new pytest case (`test_sections_cover_terminal_tabs_and_ui`) pins section titles and order; `test_payload_shape`, `test_includes_question_mark_self_reference`, `test_matches_shortcuts_builtin_source`, the `test_fake_shortcuts_lists_current_shortcuts` run-history test, and the `overlay and shortcuts built-in share the same source` Playwright invariant were all updated for the new payload shape.
- **Desktop tab strip restyled to match the mobile tab aesthetic** — six refinements ported from the mobile tab chrome now apply on desktop; the public DOM contract is unchanged (CSS-only).
  - **Before:** desktop tabs had their own visual language — larger padding, 8px radius, inset box-shadow + bloom glow on the active tab, always-visible `✕` close glyphs on every tab, and a `.tab-grip` drag handle scoped only to `body.mobile-terminal-mode`. `#new-tab-btn` carried a dashed-border gradient treatment that felt heavier than mobile's `+` button. Several `--theme-tab-*` variables were in use for `.tab` / `.tab.active` colouring.
  - **After:** six refinements. **(1)** `.tab-grip` six-dot drag handle promoted to a base component rule so every desktop tab signals drag-to-reorder without hover (mobile-scoped duplicate removed). **(2)** `.tab-close` opacity `0` by default, reveals to `1` on `.tab:hover` or `.tab.active`, so a row of `✕` glyphs no longer draws the eye away from the active tab. **(3)** `.tab .tab-status` sized down from `7px` to `6px` with `box-shadow: 0 0 8px color-mix(in srgb, var(--amber) 55%, transparent)` on the `.running` variant. **(4)** Strip density tightened: `.tabs-bar` padding `0 14px` → `6px 8px 0`, `.tab` padding `10px 12px` → `9px 12px`, `.tab` gap `6px` → `7px`, `.tab` font-size `12px` → `11px`. **(5)** `#new-tab-btn` chromeless: `background: transparent`, `border: 1px solid transparent`, `color-mix(in srgb, var(--text) 6%, transparent)` fill on hover. **(6)** Active-tab colour ported from mobile: inactive tabs render `color: var(--muted)` on transparent with 1px `--border-bright` side/bottom + 2px `--border-bright` top; active swaps to `color: var(--green)` on `--surface` with 2px `color-mix(in srgb, var(--green) 55%, transparent)` top border (bottom blends into surface). `.tab.active:has(.tab-status.running)` swaps only the top-border colour to `color-mix(in srgb, var(--amber) 60%, transparent)`. Corner radius unified at `6px 6px 0 0` across `.tab` and `#new-tab-btn` (down from `8px`). `--theme-tab-bg` / `--theme-tab-border` / `--theme-tab-active-bg` / `--theme-tab-active-border` / `--theme-tab-active-text` / `--theme-tab-active-shadow` no longer referenced by `.tab` / `.tab.active` (uses base tokens directly); `--theme-tab-text` and `--theme-tab-hover-text` still used by `#new-tab-btn` and `.tab:hover`; `--theme-tab-drop-shadow` / `--theme-tab-touch-drag-text-shadow` still used by drag-lift shadow and touch-drag text shadow. Dragged tab keeps the base lift-and-shadow — a 2px dotted green outline was tried and reverted because it read as busy rather than crisp.
  - **Tests:** no new cases needed — the public DOM contract (`.tab`, `.tab-label`, `.tab-status`, `.tab-close`, `.tab-grip`, `#new-tab-btn`) is preserved end-to-end. All 15 `tabs.spec.js`, 7 `kill.spec.js`, and 24 `shortcuts.spec.js` assertions pass unchanged.

#### Visual QA, Demo, and Capture Pipeline

- **Demo recording viewports bumped to larger, more modern screen sizes** — `config/playwright.demo.config.js` moved the desktop capture from `1280×960 @ 2x` to `1600×900 @ 2x` (genuine Retina-laptop shape, final images 3200×1800 instead of 2560×1920). `config/playwright.demo.mobile.config.js` moved the mobile capture from `393×852 @ 3x` (iPhone 14 Pro) to `430×932 @ 3x` (iPhone 15 Pro Max–class, final images 1290×2796 instead of 1179×2556). Comments, `scripts/record_demo.sh`, `scripts/record_demo_mobile.sh` GIF conversion hints, and the `tests/README.md` demo section were updated in lockstep. The resulting `assets/darklab_shell_demo.mp4` and `assets/darklab_shell_mobile_demo.mp4` were re-recorded at the new sizes.
- **HUD runtime pill merged into the status pill** — the separate `RUNTIME` pill was redundant once mobile already teleported status + timer as a pair.
  - **Before:** `RUNTIME` was a separate HUD pill that appeared alongside `STATUS` only while a command was running (`hud-runtime-cell` with its own `run-timer` span, toggled via `u-hidden`). With the mobile UI refactor already teleporting both `#status` and `#run-timer` into the mobile header as a pair, two cells always animated in/out together for one concept (is a command running, and for how long).
  - **After:** `hud-runtime-cell` removed from `index.html`; `#run-timer` now lives inside the same `hud-status-cell` as `#status`, wrapped in a new `.hud-status-value-row` inline-flex container. A `.hud-cell .run-timer:not(:empty)::before { content: " - "; }` rule injects the amber separator only while the timer has text, so the pill reads `RUNNING - 12.3s` while running and collapses to `IDLE` / `OK` / `FAIL` / `KILLED` otherwise. `#run-timer` stays a sibling of `#status` (not nested inside the pill) deliberately — `.status-pill` `textContent` stays exactly `RUNNING` / `IDLE` so the ~30 existing Playwright assertions of the form `expect(page.locator('.status-pill')).toHaveText(...)` need no changes. Mobile teleport unaffected: `_runTimerHomeParent` is captured at startup and now points at the new wrapper, so `syncMobileShellChromeLayout` still restores the timer to its original HUD home when leaving mobile mode. `showRunTimer` / `hideRunTimer` in `ui_helpers.js` no longer touch `hud-runtime-cell`; they still manage `runTimer.style.display` and clear its text on hide. Unused `hudRuntimeCell` reference in `shell_chrome.js` removed; obsolete `.hud-cell.hud-runtime.u-hidden { display: none; }` CSS retired.
  - **Tests:** all 475 Vitest unit tests continue to pass; Playwright assertions unchanged by design.

#### Documentation and Structure

- **Documentation Structure Refactor — six-phase pass to normalise reference-shaped sections across the top-level docs and promote a canonical templates reference** so that reviewers see consistent structure instead of ad-hoc prose across `CHANGELOG.md`, `README.md`, `FEATURES.md`, `ARCHITECTURE.md`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `DECISIONS.md`, `THEME.md`, and `tests/README.md`. Resolves the `Documentation structure refactor for scannability and navigation` technical-debt item in `TODO.md`. Goal was "same information, easier to scan" — no content loss, no audience-boundary drift. Doc gate (`tests/py/test_docs.py`, 21 meta-tests) and `markdownlint-cli2` stayed green end-to-end across every phase.
  - **Phase 1 — Promote canonical templates from existing gold-standard sections.** Lifted T1–T7 shape templates from working sources rather than designing in a vacuum: T1 (release-entry umbrella) from the UI Interaction Helper Refactor entry, T2 short/long (release-entry single-shot) from `[1.5]` `### Fixed` entries, T3 (merge-request doc) from `ui-interaction-refactor-merge-request.md`, T4 (architecture inventory) from `ARCHITECTURE.md`'s route inventory, T5 (feature inventory) from `FEATURES.md` `## Built-In Commands`, T6 (testing overview) from `tests/README.md`'s per-suite blocks, T7 (release-note entry) from `v1.5-release-notes.md` highlights. Each template names a canonical source, a skeleton, and the invariants the shape is meant to carry.
    - Added: new `DOCS_STANDARDS.md` at the repo root carrying the T1–T7 templates, general authoring rules, per-document guidance, review checklist, and anti-patterns; `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `README.md` Documentation Map, and the `README.md` project-structure tree all now reference it.
  - **Phase 2 — Audit and classify every target doc.** Walked each target top-to-bottom and tagged reference-shaped sections as (a) already conforms, (b) migration candidate, or (c) prose that should stay. Scope: all eight top-level docs plus the four merge-request and release-note drafts. Audit kept inline in the plan during execution, retired after Phase 6.
  - **Phase 3 — `CHANGELOG.md` `[1.5]` single-shot migrations.** Migrated long `[1.5]` entries under `### Added` / `### Changed` / `### Fixed` to the T2 long form so the outcome stays bold-lead-skimmable while root-cause/fix/tests (or why/what/tests, before/after/tests) split into labelled sub-bullets. Label alignment is section-specific: `### Fixed` → `Root cause` / `Fix` / `Tests`; `### Added` → `Why` / `What` / `Tests`; `### Changed` → `Before` / `After` / `Tests`. Pre-`[1.5]` release sections were left untouched — scope was current-release work.
  - **Phase 4 — High-traffic overview restructure.**
    - `README.md`: Configuration lead paragraph bullet-ified into override-layer rules; Documentation Map and Project Structure tree both link `DOCS_STANDARDS.md`.
    - `tests/README.md`: Suite Summaries entries for Demo Recording, UI Screenshot Capture, and Container Smoke Test collapsed into short summaries that point at new appendix references; `## History Seeding` shrunk to an overview pointer. Added `### Container Smoke Test Reference` and `### History Seeding Reference` to the Full Appendix carrying the flag tables, capture workflow, expectations-sync helper, and host-write rationale. Misplaced demo-pipeline rationale paragraphs that had drifted under UI Screenshot Capture were removed (already covered in `DECISIONS.md#demo-recording-pipeline`); Table of Contents updated.
    - `FEATURES.md`: every migration-candidate per-feature section normalised to T5 (Purpose / Behavior / Limits / Configuration / Related files) so readers can skim the same fields in the same order across feature blocks.
  - **Phase 5 — Deep reference restructure.**
    - `ARCHITECTURE.md`: the dense `### Frontend Architecture` prose paragraph split into labelled subsections — CSS composition, Desktop shell chrome, HUD runtime, Mobile chrome, Page exceptions, JS composition — with no content removed.
    - `THEME.md`: `## Editing Rules` restructured from a flat bullet list mixing authoring steps, operational behaviour, metadata fields, and CSS variable exposure into four labelled subsections (`### Authoring a theme`, `### Operational behavior`, `### Metadata fields`, `### CSS variable exposure`).
    - `DECISIONS.md`: ADR shape preserved per template guidance; several entries gained explicit bold lead sentences so the one-line decision is skimmable before the supporting paragraph.
    - `CONTRIBUTING.md`: inline pointer to `DOCS_STANDARDS.md` added alongside the existing ARCHITECTURE / tests/README references.
  - **Phase 6 — Consistency pass and gate verification.** Re-ran `python -m pytest tests/py/test_docs.py -q` (21/21) and `npm run lint:md` (0 errors) after every phase; confirmed anchors, cross-links, per-file appendix drift, documented-totals drift, and the `README.md` project-structure tree drift check all resolved. Test-count references across the canonical in-repo locations (`tests/README.md`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `ARCHITECTURE.md`) plus the merge-request and release-note drafts were not changed — this refactor is test-count neutral.
- **Repository structure cleanup** — tool and test config files that were cluttering the repo root have been consolidated into a `config/` subdirectory (`eslint.config.js`, `hadolint.yaml`, `yamllint.yml`, `vitest.config.js`, `playwright.config.js`, `playwright.parallel.config.js`, `playwright.shared.js`, `playwright.demo.config.js`, `playwright.demo.mobile.config.js`). The `docs/` directory has been renamed to `assets/` to better reflect its purpose as a media asset store rather than a documentation folder. The `scripts/node/` subdirectory has been removed and its single file (`capture_output_for_smoke_test.mjs`) moved up to `scripts/` root to avoid a language-named subfolder for one file. All internal references and `package.json` scripts have been updated.

### Fixed

- **Mobile e2e flake: `mobile menu › clicking outside the menu closes it` intermittently timed out on CI at `#mobile-menu-sheet-scrim.click()`.** The scrim is `position: fixed; inset: 0` (full viewport) and the mobile menu sheet is bottom-anchored at `z-index: 101` above the scrim's `100`. Playwright's default `.click()` targets the center of the locator's bounding box — for the full-viewport scrim that is the viewport center, which on a narrow CI viewport lands *behind* the tall menu sheet. Playwright's actionability check then logs "menu-sheet subtree intercepts pointer events" and keeps retrying against whichever menu item sits under the cursor (`ln`, then the `ts-toggle` expander, then the `timestamps` submenu label as the expander opens on hover), never stabilizes, and times out at 30s. Fix: target the scrim with an explicit `{ position: { x: 10, y: 10 } }` so the click lands in the top-left corner where the scrim is unobstructed — same pattern already used for overlay backdrop clicks in `interaction-contract.spec.js`. Verified the fix 5× in a row, sub-second each.
- **Mobile output text overflowed off-screen when timestamps or line numbers were enabled** — long output lines extended past the right edge of mobile viewports instead of wrapping.
  - **Root cause:** the `.line-content` shift that makes room for the timestamp/line-number prefix was implemented with `transform: translateX(calc(var(--output-prefix-width) + 1ch))`. `transform` shifts where an element is *painted* but does not change its layout width, so `.line-content` retained the full `.output` content-box width and long lines (common with `nmap`, `curl`, `dig`) extended past the viewport's right edge.
  - **Fix:** replaced `transform: translateX(...)` on `.line-content` / `.shell-prompt-wrap > .prompt-prefix` / `.shell-prompt-line` with `padding-left: calc(var(--output-prefix-width, 0ch) + 1ch)` on the parent `.line` / `.shell-prompt-wrap`. Padding reduces the content-box width so `white-space: pre-wrap` wraps at the correct edge. The absolutely-positioned `::before` prefix (width `var(--output-prefix-width)`, padding-right `1ch`) anchors to the padding-box left edge of the positioned parent and renders inside the padding area, so visual placement of the prefix is unchanged.
  - **Tests:** one new Playwright case in `tests/js/e2e/mobile.spec.js` (`mobile output wraps inside the transcript when timestamps and line numbers are on`) injects a long prefixed line at mobile viewport width and asserts `.line-content`'s right edge fits inside `.output`'s right edge — the same assertion fails with 110px of overflow against the pre-fix CSS.
- **Desktop chrome Alt chords now fire while the composer is focused; search rebound from `Alt+F` to `Alt+S`** — the five chrome chords were effectively inert because the composer holds focus >99% of the time.
  - **Root cause:** `handleChromeShortcut` in `app/static/js/app.js` bailed on any editable target (`isEditableTarget`), so the chords only worked when focus was outside the composer. On macOS this was especially loud because Option+letter produces glyphs (`«`, `˙`, `≤`, `©`, `ˇ`) that leaked into the prompt as "typed" characters. Separately, `Alt+F` for search conflicted with the composer's readline word-forward binding.
  - **Fix:** guard narrowed to `shouldIgnoreGlobalShortcutTarget`, which excludes the composer (`cmdInput`) while still blocking chrome chords from hijacking other editable fields (modal inputs, search field, options textarea). Each chord already calls `preventDefault()`, so no Option-glyph reaches the prompt. Search rebound from `Alt+F` to `Alt+S` — keeping it on `Alt+F` would have required a context-dependent chord (search from body, word-forward from the composer), a net UX loss. `Alt+S` has no readline conflict and works identically from every focus context. `Alt+F` remains in the Terminal section of `_CURRENT_SHORTCUTS` as readline word-forward and no longer appears in the UI section.
  - **Tests:** Playwright rewritten — the `desktop chrome keyboard shortcuts` `describe` block's `beforeEach` now focuses `#cmd` (previously blurred it) and each chord test asserts `#cmd` stays empty after the chord fires (catching "Option-glyph leaked into the prompt" regressions). New case `Alt+S toggles the transcript search bar from the composer` covers the new chord; old `Alt+F toggles the transcript search bar` test and the `chrome shortcuts are ignored while the composer is focused` negative test removed. Unit `supports Alt+B and Alt+F to move by word` in `app.test.js` still covers readline word-forward. Net Playwright count: −1 (169 vs 170).
- **History-drawer "clear all" button renamed to "delete all"; confirmation modal now fits three buttons on one row on mobile** — the destructive label is clearer, and the mobile confirmation no longer wraps awkwardly.
  - **Root cause:** "clear all" implied a cosmetic UI reset more than a destructive `DELETE FROM runs`, and the three-button mobile confirmation (`Cancel` / `Delete Non-Favorites` / `Delete all`) overflowed the modal body on narrow screens.
  - **Fix:** renamed the action in both locations (desktop history drawer `#hist-clear-all-btn` and mobile recents sheet `#mobile-recents-clear`, plus its `aria-label`). `.modal-actions-wrap` now uses `flex-wrap: nowrap`, and a `@media (max-width: 480px)` rule reduces the gap from 10px to 6px and the modal-primary/secondary horizontal padding from 18px to 10px so all three buttons fit side-by-side at 393px and above. The same wrap-class fix also benefits the share-redaction confirmation.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified in desktop and narrow mobile modal layouts.
- **Mobile demo recording script post–mobile-UI-refactor regressions** — three issues surfaced in the captured video after the mobile chrome rebuild.
  - **Root cause:**
    - The keyboard helper row (`.kb-key`) and every recents-sheet control (`.sheet-item-action`, `.sheet-clear-btn`, `.sheet-filter-row`, `.sheet-close`) rendered with Chromium's native light-grey button chrome because the rule sets omitted `appearance: none` / `-webkit-appearance: none`.
    - `demo.mobile.spec.js` still drove the old `hamburger → menu → history` path even though the canonical entry point is now the pull-up recents peek.
    - Mid-demo scroll occasionally pushed the header out of frame.
  - **Fix:**
    - Added `appearance: none` / `-webkit-appearance: none` plus explicit `background: transparent`, `border: 0`, `font-family: inherit`, and `-webkit-tap-highlight-color: transparent` where missing.
    - The spec now clicks `#mobile-recent-peek` directly once ping/nslookup have populated history.
    - The capture loop and `freezeFrame` helper now call `window.scrollTo(0, 0)` before each `page.screenshot()`, and demo bootstrap injects 6px top padding on `body.mobile-terminal-mode` so the header is never flush against the viewport edge.
  - **Tests:** demo spec is the verification; runs under `RUN_DEMO=1` only.
- **Mobile bottom-sheet drag-handle behavior was inconsistent across sheets** — three parallel handle implementations had drifted; unified to one module.
  - **Root cause:**
    - `bindMobileSheetDragClose` in `controller.js` injected a `.mobile-sheet-handle` div and bound drag-only behavior on eight sheets (menu, history panel, workflows, FAQ, options, kill, hist-del, share-redaction).
    - Inline pointer/keydown handlers in `mobile_chrome.js` bound drag + tap + keyboard close on the recents sheet via its built-in `.sheet-grab`.
    - Two parallel CSS rule sets (`.mobile-sheet-handle` and per-sheet `.sheet-grab` variants) styled the visual.
    - Result: drag-with-follow worked only on Options/FAQ; the menu sheet snapped back after a couple of pixels because the listener was attached to the auto-injected `.mobile-sheet-handle` while the template already provided its own `.sheet-grab`; tap-to-close and brighten-on-press worked only on recents.
  - **Fix:**
    - Extracted all sheet behavior to `app/static/js/mobile_sheet.js` exposing `bindMobileSheet(sheet, { onClose, threshold, tapMaxMovement })`.
    - The helper reuses an existing `:scope > .sheet-grab` if the template provides one, else injects.
    - It handles drag-with-follow (sheet translates with the finger; releases past `threshold` animate out and close, under it snaps back), tap-to-close (movement under `tapMaxMovement` + quick release), and keyboard close (Enter/Space).
    - `.mobile-sheet-handle` is retired and CSS is consolidated to one `body.mobile-terminal-mode .sheet-grab` rule (visual + cursor + touch-action + brighten on hover/active).
    - All nine sheets — menu, recents, history panel, workflows, FAQ, options, kill, hist-del, share-redaction — now share identical behavior.
    - Padding was tuned from `12px 0` to `20px 0 12px`, then to symmetric `20px 0`, after phone testing showed the bottom still felt cramped.
  - **Pull-to-refresh suppression:** `overscroll-behavior-y: contain` added (terminal has no refresh semantics — reload destroys session state) but had no effect in iOS Safari or Firefox mobile. Hoisting to `html:has(body.mobile-terminal-mode)` didn't help either. Actual root cause: both engines only honour `overscroll-behavior` on non-trivial scroll containers, and the mobile shell deliberately keeps body content within the viewport so neither `html` nor `body` is ever scrollable — making the property a no-op regardless of where it lived. Fix is a delegated `touchmove` guard in `mobile_chrome.js` (always installed, gated at event time on `body.mobile-terminal-mode`): walks the ancestor chain for a scrollable element that can absorb the gesture; if none found (or nearest scrollable is at its boundary for the direction), calls `preventDefault` so the browser can't interpret it as pull-to-refresh / overscroll bounce. Existing CSS rules retained as defense-in-depth for engines that do honour them. Sheet drag handlers unaffected — they run on Pointer Events with `setPointerCapture` and `touch-action: none` on the grab, already bypassing the browser's default touch handling.
  - **Tests:** Playwright walk through five representative sheets in an iPhone-sized viewport — 26/26 assertions passed (no `.mobile-sheet-handle` remains; each sheet has exactly one `:scope > .sheet-grab` of identical size; tap-to-close and drag-to-close both work on every sheet).

#### Reverse-i-search and Prompt Search

- **Reverse-i-search returned no matches for 1- and 2-character queries** — short queries now fall back to substring matching instead of silently producing zero trigram hits.
  - **Root cause:** `_build_fts_query` in `app/blueprints/history.py` formats every term as an FTS5 phrase, but the trigram tokenizer cannot index terms shorter than 3 characters, so queries like `ps` or `ls` generated no usable trigrams and matched nothing.
  - **Fix:** `_build_fts_query` now returns `None` when any term is shorter than 3 characters, which drives the endpoint onto the existing `LIKE` fallback against `command`.
