  - **Tests:** three pytest cases in `TestOutputSearch` cover the fallback and narrowing behavior: `test_short_query_under_trigram_threshold_matches_via_like`, `test_partial_typing_narrows_progressively`, and `test_scope_command_ignores_output_matches`.
- **Reverse-i-search matched on output text in addition to typed command text** — `Ctrl+R` now searches only command text, matching shell expectations.
  - **Root cause:** reverse-i-search was reusing the drawer’s `/history?q=...` path, and that path includes `output_search_text` matches for full-text drawer search.
  - **Fix:** a new `scope=command` query parameter suppresses the FTS path and matches only `r.command` via `LIKE`; `_histSearchFetch` in `history.js` now appends that scope for every reverse-i-search request while the drawer stays on the broader full-text behavior.
  - **Tests:** covered by the pytest scope-command regression above.
- **Reverse-i-search dropdown no longer loses or misplaces results during typing** — the dropdown now keeps client-known matches, stays on-screen, and reflects the actual live query.
  - **Root cause:** three smaller UI issues had drifted together: `_histSearchMatches` would replace in-memory matches with an empty server response, `_renderHistSearch` always tried to place the dropdown above the prompt even when there was no room, and the `input` listener in `controller.js` passed stale composer state instead of the live `cmdInput.value`.
  - **Fix:** the matcher now always seeds from `cmdHistory` before merging server-only hits; dropdown placement mirrors the autocomplete flip logic and clamps to an 8px viewport margin; the hist-search input path now reads `cmdInput.value` directly when hist-search mode is active.
  - **Tests:** two Vitest regressions cover the empty-server merge path (`dropdown keeps cmdHistory matches when server fetch returns empty`, `dropdown merges cmdHistory matches with unique server-only matches`); placement and stale-input fixes were verified through the browser search flow.
- **Desktop rail version footer no longer rendered in italic** — `.rail-nav-version` in `shell-chrome.css` had `font-style: italic` left over from an earlier rail iteration; removed so the footer reads as a normal label rather than an aside.
- **Mobile menu sheet close button now matches the recents-sheet close treatment** — `#mobile-menu-sheet-close` inherited default browser button styling because no CSS rule targeted it.
  - **Root cause:** only `.recents-sheet .sheet-close` was defined; `#mobile-menu-sheet-close` fell back to default browser button styling — visibly different sizing, colour, and padding from every other modal close button.
  - **Fix:** hoisted `.recents-sheet .sheet-close` to a generic `.sheet-close` selector (still scoped under `body.mobile-terminal-mode`) so both mobile sheets share identical styling. Picks up the canonical desktop modal-close treatment used by `.faq-close`, `.workflows-close`, `.theme-close`, `.options-close`, `.history-panel-close` — `transition: color 0.15s`, `:hover/:active → color: var(--text)`, `line-height: 1`, `margin-left: auto`. Dropped the asymmetric `opacity: 0.8` in favour of the muted-→text colour transition. Retained mobile-friendly `font-size: 18px` / `padding: 6px 10px` for touch ergonomics.
  - **Tests:** no new cases — visual consistency verified across both mobile sheets.

#### Session Identity and History

- **Client-side `session-token` subcommands no longer print a duplicate empty prompt after running** — every `session-token` result was followed by an extra empty `anon@darklab:~$` row.
  - **Root cause:** every client-side handler (`generate`, `set`, `clear`, `rotate`, `list`, `revoke`) plus the migration-answer flow called `appendPromptNewline()` at the end of its output. But the live `shellPromptWrap` composer below the transcript already serves as the next visual prompt, so the call produced a redundant row. Normal commands routed through SSE never call `appendPromptNewline()` for exactly this reason — client-side handlers were the only callers emitting the redundant prompt-echo line.
  - **Fix:** removed all 24 `appendPromptNewline()` calls across the six subcommand handlers and the migration-answer paths in `submitCommand`. Intentional call sites preserved: Ctrl+C interrupt in `interruptPromptLine`, the empty-Enter handler in `submitCommand`, and the welcome-settle handler.
  - **Tests:** no new cases — visual verification across all six subcommands.
- **Session-migration confirmation no longer caps the displayed run count at `history_panel_limit`** — migration prompts now show the true number of runs that would move.
  - **Root cause:** the prompt (`migrate N runs from old session?`) counted rows from `apiFetch('/history')`, but `/history` is capped by `history_panel_limit` (default 50), so large sessions understated the migration size.
  - **Fix:** added `GET /session/run-count`, which returns an uncapped `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM runs WHERE session_id = ?`; both migration-confirmation call sites in `controller.js` (`session-token generate` and `session-token set`) now use that endpoint.
  - **Tests:** four `TestSessionRunCount` pytest cases cover empty sessions, uncapped counts, counts above the history limit, and per-session scoping.
- **Stale `localStorage.starred` no longer masks server-side stars on slow load** — users with a stale empty `localStorage.starred` saw no star indicator until the server fetch resolved.
  - **Root cause:** `_getStarred()` had a `localStorage.starred` fallback for when the in-memory `_starredCache` was still null (e.g. before `loadStarredFromServer()` resolved). For users with a stale empty `localStorage.starred` array left over from before stars moved server-side, this fallback returned an empty Set even when the active session had real stars on the server.
  - **Fix:** removed the fallback — `_getStarred()` now returns either `_starredCache` (when populated) or an empty Set, so a still-loading cache no longer claims authority over the server. To clean up the orphaned key for users who never trigger a session change, `_seedLocalStorageStarsToServer()` is now called once at boot after `loadStarredFromServer()` succeeds — empty or invalid values are removed without a server round-trip; populated values are seeded to the server first and then removed.
  - **Tests:** three `_seedLocalStorageStarsToServer` Vitest cases strengthened to assert the localStorage key is removed in the no-key, empty-array, and invalid-JSON cases.
- **`session-token revoke` now enforces invalidation at the API layer** — revoked tokens could still read and write the same runs, snapshots, and stars.
  - **Root cause:** revoking a token deleted it from `session_tokens`, but the main data routes trusted any `X-Session-ID` header value unconditionally via `get_session_id()`. A browser or script that kept sending the old token retained full access.
  - **Fix:** `get_session_id()` now validates `tok_` tokens against `session_tokens` on every request; a revoked or never-issued `tok_` value is treated as anonymous (returns `""`) so the caller loses access to the session's data. `/session/token/info` also no longer echoes back a `tok_` header value when no matching row exists — both fields return `null`, matching the anonymous case.
  - **Tests:** covered by the existing `TestSessionToken` suite plus route-level checks.
- **Desktop notifications no longer expose full command arguments** — notification titles now use only the command root, not the full command line.
  - **Root cause:** `_maybeNotify()` built the title from `'$ ' + command` (truncated to 80 characters), which still exposed bearer tokens, API keys, auth headers, internal hostnames, or token values in commands like `session-token revoke <token>`.
  - **Fix:** the notification title now uses only the first word, e.g. `$ curl` instead of `$ curl -H "Authorization: Bearer sk-..."`. Exit code and elapsed time remain in the body.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases; verified through the existing notification flow.
- **Autocomplete no longer drops empty `arg_hints` entries or suppresses their early-return behavior** — terminal subcommands like `session-token clear` now preserve their display-only hint state correctly.
  - **Root cause:** the Python normalizer used `if hints:` and silently discarded empty lists like `[]`, so those entries never reached the browser; then the frontend `directHints` gate required membership in `expects_value`, even for subcommands that intentionally consume no value.
  - **Fix:** `_load_autocomplete_config` now writes all `arg_hints` entries unconditionally, and the frontend gate now checks `directHints !== null` instead of requiring `expects_value` membership. `expects_value` is back to describing only flags that actually consume a value.
  - **Tests:** covered by the later placeholder-hint regression work and the surrounding autocomplete/session-token flows.
- **Autocomplete value-taking flags now preserve case-sensitive distinctions such as `-W` vs `-w`** — the loader no longer collapses distinct flags just because they differ only by case.
  - **Root cause:** `app/commands.py` normalized `expects_value` entries through a lowercase dedupe path, and the local-overlay merge reused the same case-folded key. Commands that legitimately use both uppercase and lowercase flag forms therefore lost one of the two value-taking slots during normalization.
  - **Fix:** `expects_value` dedupe and overlay merge now preserve exact token case instead of lowercasing before comparison. The readable autocomplete schema (`takes_value`) keeps compiling down to the same runtime shape, but distinct case-sensitive flags remain distinct in that normalized output.
  - **Tests:** 2 new pytest cases in `tests/py/test_backend_modules.py` cover direct normalization and local-overlay merge behavior for side-by-side `-W` / `-w` flags.
- **`session-token generate` and `session-token set` now defer identity switch until after migration** — a failed migration used to leave the user on the new token identity while their runs and snapshots remained attached to the old session.
  - **Root cause:** both commands switched `SESSION_ID` to the new token before calling `/session/migrate`, so a partial failure stranded the user between identities.
  - **Fix:** the identity switch (and `localStorage` write) now happens only after migration succeeds. If the user declines migration, the switch still happens immediately (the new token activates without migrating history). If migration fails, the old session stays active and an error is shown; the newly generated token is discarded. The options-modal Generate and Set paths follow the same pattern. `rotate` was already atomic; this brings `generate` and `set` in line with it.
  - **Tests:** no new cases — existing `TestSessionMigrate` suite covers migration success/failure paths.
- **Session-token migration and seeding flows now fail closed instead of overstating or dropping state** — the migration UI and star-seeding path now preserve data and report counts accurately.
  - **Root cause:** three smaller integrity issues were present: `_seedLocalStorageStarsToServer` deleted `localStorage.starred` even when some POSTs failed, `_waitForMigrateChoice` accumulated stale button listeners across repeated opens, and `/session/migrate` reported `migrated_stars` using the delete-rowcount rather than rows actually inserted into the destination session.
  - **Fix:** star seeding now uses `Promise.allSettled` and writes only failed commands back to `localStorage`; `_waitForMigrateChoice` replaces buttons with `cloneNode` copies before rebinding listeners; `migrated_stars` now uses the `INSERT OR IGNORE` rowcount so it reports only rows actually written.
  - **Tests:** covered by the existing session-token route and migration flows plus the strengthened star-seeding regressions.
- **Session-token migration dismissal is now a true abort, and the migration confirm exposes an explicit `Cancel` action** — the token switch no longer continues when the migration prompt is dismissed.
  - **Root cause:** the migration-choice prompt only offered `Skip` and `Yes, migrate`, so dismissals from `Escape`, backdrop click, or mobile drag-down resolved through the same path as "do not migrate" and allowed the token-activation flow to continue.
  - **Fix:** the shared migration confirm now uses three actions: `Cancel`, `Skip`, and `Yes, migrate`. Both the Generate and Set token flows treat `Cancel` or any dismissal path as a full abort; only explicit `Skip` or `Yes, migrate` continues into token activation.
  - **Tests:** three new unit cases in `tests/js/unit/app.test.js` cover cancel/dismiss abort for both Generate and Set, plus the explicit `Skip` path for Set.
- **Toast notifications now appear above the options modal** — session-token toasts are no longer hidden behind the still-open options overlay.
  - **Root cause:** the toast stack used `z-index: 300`, below the options overlay at 320.
  - **Fix:** raised the toast layer to 400 so toasts render above all overlay surfaces.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified through the existing session-token flows.
- **Recent command chips and starred commands now reload immediately after any session token operation** — the shell chrome now reflects the active session without requiring a full page reload.
  - **Root cause:** `cmdHistory` and the starred set were hydrated only at page load, so session switches left the chip bar and star state stale until reload.
  - **Fix:** added `reloadSessionHistory()` in `history.js`, which sequences star-cache reload → history fetch → chip-bar hydration → history panel refresh (if open), and calls it from every session-switch path in `runner.js` and `controller.js`.
  - **Tests:** covered by the surrounding session-token browser flows.

#### Autocomplete and Prompt UX

- **Autocomplete schema cleanup and readability refactor** — `app/conf/autocomplete.yaml` now uses a clearer authoring model built around `flags`, `arguments`, `subcommands`, and `pipe` instead of scattering related behavior across older low-level fields.
  - **Why:** the old autocomplete config was flexible, but it was hard to author and review because one command's behavior could be split across multiple disconnected keys. Flags that consumed values, display-only placeholders, terminal subcommands, and pipe-stage entries all required the reader to mentally reconstruct how the pieces fit together.
  - **What:**
    - `flags` now keep `takes_value`, `value_hint`, `suggest`, and `closes` next to the flag they describe.
    - `arguments` now describe normal positional slots directly, including starter values and display-only placeholders.
    - `subcommands` now model command trees such as `session-token set <token>` without relying on positional pseudo-entries.
    - `pipe` now groups pipe-stage insertion and display metadata in one place instead of split `pipe_*` keys.
    - `argument_limit` now lets commands such as `man`, `which`, and `type` stop suggesting additional positional operands after the configured number of argument slots is filled, while still allowing flags later in the command.
  - **Implementation:** the backend loader now accepts only the new authoring shape and still normalizes it to the same runtime context structure the frontend already consumes (`flags`, `expects_value`, `arg_hints`, `pipe_command`, `pipe_insert_value`, `pipe_label`, `pipe_description`). The shipped `autocomplete.yaml`, its header comments, and the feature documentation were all updated to match the new model.
  - **Tests:** covered by backend normalization/merge coverage for the new schema plus the existing frontend autocomplete contract suite.
- **`session-token set` autocomplete no longer inserts the `<token>` placeholder** — `Tab` now leaves the composer ready for a pasted token instead of inserting literal placeholder text.
  - **Root cause:** the positional-hint builder in `autocomplete.js` was not forwarding `insertValue` from YAML items to `_buildAutocompleteItem`, so the display label (`set <token>`) doubled as the inserted text.
  - **Fix:** both call sites now propagate `label` and `insertValue` from the context item; `session-token set` keeps `insertValue: "set "` in the runtime built-in context, so `Tab` inserts `session-token set ` and stops there.
  - **Tests:** covered by the broader placeholder-hint regression work below.
- **Autocomplete placeholder hints (`<token>`, `<target>`, etc.) are now display-only across all commands** — three distinct issues combined to let `Tab` insert the literal placeholder text.
  - **Root cause:** (1) the Python normalizer `_normalize_context_suggestion` in `app/commands.py` only preserved `value` and `description` from YAML items, silently dropping `insertValue`/`label`/`hintOnly` — so an entry like `{ value: "set <token>", insertValue: "set " }` reached the browser as `{ value: "set <token>" }` and the `set <token>` string itself was used as the insertion text (an earlier "fix" to propagate `insertValue` through `autocomplete.js` was a no-op because the key never arrived from the backend). (2) `_acItemInsertValue()` in `autocomplete.js` called `.trim()` on the insertion string, so even after the backend fix an author-intended trailing space in `insertValue: "set "` was stripped. (3) typing `session-token set ` and pressing `Tab` would insert the literal string `<token>` from the `arg_hints.set` placeholder — the builder could not distinguish a display-only placeholder from a real completion value.
  - **Fix:** `_normalize_context_suggestion` now preserves `insertValue` (whitespace-significant, untrimmed), `label`, and `hintOnly` when present; `_buildAutocompleteItem` auto-detects `<placeholder>` values (regex `^<[^<>\s][^<>]*>$`) as `hintOnly: true` when no explicit `insertValue` is given; `acAccept` short-circuits on `hintOnly` items (keyboard focus preserved; nothing inserted); a new `_acItemInsertText` helper used only by `acAccept` preserves intentional trailing whitespace in `insertValue`. Author opt-out: set `insertValue` explicitly on a `<placeholder>` entry to make it Tab-insertable, or set `hintOnly: false` to force.
  - **Tests:** one new pytest case (`test_arg_hints_preserve_insert_value_with_trailing_whitespace`) covers the backend preservation; one new Vitest case covers the frontend (preserved whitespace, hintOnly detection, acAccept no-op on hintOnly).
- **Exact single-flag autocomplete matches now stay visible long enough to show their description** — typing a full flag token such as `curl -w` no longer collapses the dropdown before the user can read what the flag does.
  - **Root cause:** `getAutocompleteMatches()` hid the dropdown whenever there was exactly one exact non-placeholder match. That was reasonable for many completed tokens, but it also hid helpful flag descriptions the moment the user finished typing a flag.
  - **Fix:** the exact-match auto-hide rule now exempts flag tokens. Exact single flag matches remain visible until the user types the trailing space, while placeholder hints still stay visible and non-flag exact single matches still collapse as before.
  - **Tests:** covered by a new autocomplete unit regression for `curl -w`, alongside the existing contextual flag and value-hint coverage.
- **Above-the-prompt autocomplete dropdowns now stay pinned to the prompt as the item count shrinks** — when the dropdown opens above the prompt, narrowing the result set no longer makes the menu drift farther away from the composer.
  - **Root cause:** desktop `ac-up` mode positioned the dropdown with a computed `top` based on an estimated visible height. As the rendered dropdown became shorter, that estimate caused the menu to recede upward instead of keeping its lower edge anchored near the prompt.
  - **Fix:** desktop above-mode positioning now anchors the dropdown with `bottom` instead of recalculating `top`, so the edge nearest the prompt stays fixed while the menu shrinks. Below-mode and mobile positioning behavior are unchanged.
  - **Tests:** covered by two autocomplete unit regressions: one verifies above-mode uses bottom anchoring, and another verifies the bottom offset stays unchanged when the item count shrinks.
- **Long-lived `/run` streams now clean up stdout pipes reliably, even on disconnects and stream errors** — repeated command runs no longer risk leaking file descriptors until `select()` fails with `filedescriptor out of range in select()`.
  - **Root cause:** both the normal SSE generator path and the detached drain-thread path only closed `proc.stdout` and waited on the subprocess on the happy path after the stream loop exited normally. Client disconnects, generator errors, and other exception paths skipped that cleanup, leaving stdout pipes open and eventually pushing file descriptors past `FD_SETSIZE`.
  - **Fix:** the run streaming code now uses a shared `_stdout_ready()` helper backed by `selectors.DefaultSelector` instead of direct `select.select(...)`, and both stream paths now call shared process cleanup from `finally` so `stdout.close()` and `proc.wait()` still run when the client disconnects or the stream raises unexpectedly.
  - **Tests:** two new pytest regressions in `tests/py/test_run_history_share.py` cover stream-error cleanup and disconnect/detach cleanup, in addition to the existing `/run` streaming coverage.
- **Mobile tab bar now scrolls to keep the active tab fully visible** — active tabs no longer sit partially off-screen after activation or auto-rename.
  - **Root cause:** `shouldScrollActiveTabIntoView()` explicitly suppressed `ensureActiveTabVisible()` on mobile, so the strip never auto-corrected once the active tab drifted out of view.
  - **Fix:** removed the mobile guard so `ensureActiveTabVisible()` runs across both desktop and mobile. `setTabLabel()` now also calls it for the active tab so command-triggered auto-renames stay visible too.
  - **Tests:** covered by the mobile tabs bar browser regression coverage.
- **Mobile autocomplete dropdown truncated and not scrollable with 3+ items** — two separate bugs combined to make the third (and any further) autocomplete item inaccessible on mobile.
  - **Root cause:** (1) `touchstart` on each dropdown item called `e.preventDefault()`, which blocked the browser's native scroll gesture on the dropdown container — so touching the list to scroll it instead triggered the topmost item. (2) `maxHeight` in mobile mode was additionally capped by `available = rect.top - 12` (the vertical space above the composer), which could further clip the dropdown below the height needed to show all items.
  - **Fix:** replaced the `touchstart` + immediate-accept pattern with tap detection — `touchstart` now records the finger position passively (no `preventDefault`), and `touchend` only accepts the item if the finger moved less than 10px, letting swipe gestures fall through to native scroll. The secondary `available`-space cap was removed so the dropdown expands to fit up to 8 items (360px max) without depending on a runtime geometry check.
  - **Tests:** no new cases — visual verification at mobile viewport widths.
- **Reverse-history search now searches full session history** — `Ctrl+R` can now find commands beyond the small chip-bar cache.
  - **Root cause:** reverse-i-search searched only the in-memory recent-commands list, which is capped by `recent_commands_limit` (default 50).
  - **Fix:** it now fetches against `/history`, applying the query server-side before the `history_panel_limit` cap so earlier session commands remain reachable. Results are debounced per keystroke, capped at 10 in the dropdown, and the dropdown no longer pre-populates on open.
  - **Tests:** covered by the reverse-history regression suite and the `/history`-backed search path above.
- **Autocomplete examples not shown after accepting a command root** — choosing a command suggestion now immediately reveals that command’s examples.
  - **Root cause:** `acAccept` called `setComposerValue` before `acHide`, so the input event rendered examples and then `acHide` immediately closed them.
  - **Fix:** swapped the order: hide first, then set the composer value, letting the new autocomplete state render without being torn down.
  - **Tests:** covered by the autocomplete browser flow.
- **`session-token` subcommands now have per-subcommand autocomplete context** — after `session-token set `, the dropdown shows a `<token>` value hint. After `session-token generate `, `session-token clear `, or `session-token rotate `, the dropdown collapses (no further suggestions). Previously, all three terminal subcommands continued to suggest the other available subcommands as if additional arguments were expected. `generate`, `clear`, and `rotate` are removed from `expects_value` since they do not consume a value; only `set` remains.
- **Help flags marked as terminal in `arg_hints` across 24 commands** — typing a help flag and then pressing space no longer pops the autocomplete dropdown. The following flags are now marked with `[]` in `arg_hints`: `-h` for nmap, ffuf, curl, dig, nuclei, ping, mtr, wget, dnsrecon, dnsenum, dnsx, fierce, subfinder, pd-httpx, wpscan, gobuster, fping, sslscan; `--help` for traceroute, testssl, sslyze, wafw00f, masscan, rustscan; `-help` for naabu and katana. Excluded intentionally: `nikto -h` (target host, not help), `df -h` and `free -h` (human-readable output modifier, combinable with other flags).
- **Example command domains corrected** — command examples now use the right hostnames for DNS versus HTTP/IP-oriented tools.
  - **Root cause:** several examples in `autocomplete.yaml` and `scripts/smoke_test_commands.txt` used `ip.darklab.sh` where a plain domain was required, while `nmap` and `curl` had the reverse problem.
  - **Fix:** updated DNS-oriented examples (`dig`, `nslookup`, `host`, `dnsrecon`, `subfinder`, `dnsx`, `dnsenum`, `fierce`) to use `darklab.sh`, and corrected `nmap` and `curl` to use `ip.darklab.sh`. Both files now agree.
  - **Tests:** exercised by the autocomplete-backed smoke-test pipeline.
- **`man <built-in>` autocomplete coverage** — the `man` command's positional hints include every documented built-in command root so typing `man ` shows both real tool man pages and all built-in commands in the dropdown. The duplicate `nmap` entry was also removed.

#### Export and Permalink Rendering

- **`save txt` and `save html` no longer apply share redaction** — local exports now preserve the original terminal content instead of permalink-style sanitized content.
  - **Root cause:** the local file-export path reused the same redaction pass as permalink sharing, so downloaded files replaced IPs, hostnames, emails, and bearer tokens even though local saves are not shared.
  - **Fix:** redaction is now scoped only to the permalink share flow. `saveTab` uses the raw exportable lines, `exportTabHtml` uses `rawLines` directly, and only `permalinkTab` still calls `_getRedactedLines` before posting to `/share`.
  - **Tests:** covered by the export/save browser flows.

#### Testing, CI, and Smoke Infrastructure

- **Container smoke test now reports all failures instead of stopping after the first** — the regression suite now surfaces the full broken-command set in one run.
  - **Root cause:** `scripts/container_smoke_test.sh` passed `-x` to pytest, so the run aborted after the first failing command.
  - **Fix:** removed `-x`, allowing the full suite to complete and report every failure.
  - **Tests:** the smoke test run itself is the verification.
- **Container smoke test is now driven by `autocomplete.yaml` examples** — the command corpus for both `scripts/container_smoke_test.sh` and `scripts/capture_container_smoke_test_outputs.sh` is now sourced from `context.<root>.examples[].value` in `app/conf/autocomplete.yaml` instead of the manually maintained `scripts/smoke_test_commands.txt`. This ties the regression suite directly to the commands the shell suggests to users: adding or removing an example automatically adds or removes it from the smoke test. Any entry in `tests/py/fixtures/container_smoke_test-expectations.json` whose command does not appear in `autocomplete.yaml` examples is considered stale.
- **Capture script no longer kills long-running commands early** — the capture script previously sent SIGTERM to `nmap`, `masscan`, `nikto`, `testssl`, and `nuclei` as soon as early-output markers appeared, resulting in synthetic `-15` exit codes that masked real command failures and truncated output before useful scan results. The early-stop mechanism has been removed. Commands now run to completion (or until `--command-timeout-ms`), producing real exit codes and full output that operators can use to choose meaningful `expected_text` anchors such as actual port scan results instead of just banner lines.
- **Help examples added as first example for all tool commands** — every command entry in `app/conf/autocomplete.yaml` that declares a help flag (`-h`, `--help`, or `-help`) now has that help invocation as its first example. This surfaces the help output as a suggested starting point for users unfamiliar with a tool and ensures the tool's help flag is smoke-tested on every run.
- **Docker container networking tuning** — `examples/docker-compose.prod.yml` now raises the per-process file-descriptor ceiling to 65 535 via `ulimits.nofile` and adds network-namespace-local sysctls (`net.ipv4.ip_local_port_range`, `net.ipv4.tcp_tw_reuse`, `net.ipv4.tcp_fin_timeout`, `net.ipv4.tcp_max_tw_buckets`) to the shell container. This gives tools like `naabu` and `masscan` enough source ports and socket headroom to run wider port-range scans without silently dropping connections.
- **Parallel Playwright structure** — browser e2e now uses two Playwright configs instead of one shared local path. `playwright.config.js` stays simple for VS Code Test Explorer and focused debugging, while `playwright.parallel.config.js` drives the normal CLI run across 5 isolated Chromium projects. Each project gets its own Flask server port and `APP_DATA_DIR` state so SQLite history, run-output artifacts, and limiter/process state do not collide between workers. The old monolithic `welcome.spec.js` has also been split into smaller welcome-focused files so the parallel runner can balance the long welcome animation coverage instead of treating it as one large scheduling block.

#### Diagnostics and Operator Surfaces

- **Diagnostics redaction config rendering** — `/diag` now reports redaction settings with the correct value semantics.
  - **Root cause:** numeric zeroes were rendered as boolean `false`, and the rule-count label implied it included built-in redactions when it actually counted only custom regex rules.
  - **Fix:** the config table now renders numeric zeroes as `0`, and the field is renamed to `custom_redaction_rule_count`.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — verified through the diagnostics view.
- **`vitest.config.js` root path resolution** — Vitest now resolves the repo root correctly no matter where it is invoked from.
  - **Root cause:** after moving the config to `config/vitest.config.js`, `root: '..'` was resolved relative to the working directory instead of the config file.
  - **Fix:** compute the root from `import.meta.url`, making it absolute and invocation-directory independent.
  - **Tests:** verified through normal Vitest invocation paths.
- **naabu forced connect-scan mode** — containerized `naabu` runs now default to a reliable scan mode instead of depending on raw-socket capabilities.
  - **Root cause:** raw SYN scanning depends on libpcap and elevated capabilities that are not consistently available inside the container.
  - **Fix:** inject `-scan-type c` automatically when the command does not already specify `-scan-type` or `-st`, forcing TCP connect mode without overriding explicit user intent.
  - **Tests:** covered by the container smoke path and the command rewrite behavior.
- **Autocomplete stubs not discoverable via prefix matching** — roots with empty specs now still appear in prefix matches.
  - **Root cause:** `_normalize_autocomplete_context` only registered roots that had flags, `arg_hints`, or pipe metadata, so entries like `whois: {}` vanished from `acContextRegistry`.
  - **Fix:** removed the guard so every declared root is registered even if it has no additional spec data.
  - **Tests:** covered by the autocomplete prefix-matching regressions.
- **Deny-prefix combined short-flag matching** — short-flag deny rules now catch bundled forms like `-sUT` when `-sU` is blocked.
  - **Root cause:** `_is_denied()` required an exact token match, so deny entries for a short flag did not match bundled POSIX short-form tokens.
  - **Fix:** expand only true short-form bundles (single dash, alphabetic, at most 4 chars) when evaluating deny rules. Long-form single-dash flags used by Go tools such as `-list` and `-output` still require exact matching.
  - **Tests:** covered by the deny-rule regression suite.
- **Permalink page app title displayed inside stale green border** — the generic `header h1` rule in `base.css` applied a green border, gradient background, and padding to the permalink page's `<h1 class="permalink-title">` element, a style that had been removed from the main shell UI. The permalink-specific overrides in `components.css` covered font and color but not border, background, or padding. Fixed by adding explicit resets to `body.permalink-page .permalink-title`.
- **HTML export command text rendered in uppercase** — `buildTerminalExportStyles` in `export_html.js` applied `text-transform: uppercase` to `.export-meta`, making the command line appear all-caps in every downloaded HTML file from both the main UI and the permalink page. Removed the CSS property; command text now preserves its original casing, which is important for case-sensitive flags.
- **PDF export command and title text converted to uppercase** — both `tabs.js` and `permalink.html` called `.toUpperCase()` on the app name and meta line before passing them to jsPDF. Unlike CSS `text-transform`, this mutates the string, so commands with case-sensitive flags were corrupted. Removed the `.toUpperCase()` calls from all call sites.
- **PDF export backgrounds swapped vs HTML export** — the PDF header was filled with `colors.surface` (lighter) while the content body used `colors.bg` (darker), which is the reverse of the HTML export layout. Fixed by swapping the fills so the header uses `colors.bg` and the content body uses `colors.surface`, matching the HTML output.
- **HTML export had visible blank lines between output lines** — `buildExportLinesHtml` in `export_html.js` joined `<span class="line">` elements with `'\n'`. Because the container has `white-space: pre-wrap`, those literal newlines between block-level spans rendered as visible blank lines in the downloaded HTML file. Fixed by joining with `''` instead.
- **PDF and HTML export included timestamp/line-number prefix column regardless of terminal toggle state** — `exportTabHtml` used `line.tsC || ''` unconditionally, and `exportTabPdf` read `line.tsC` unconditionally, so exports showed timestamps even when the terminal had both timestamps and line numbers disabled. A new `_exportPrefix(line, index)` helper reads the same `tsMode`/`lnMode` globals that govern the live terminal display, so exports now match what is visible in the tab.
- **PDF export app name font too large and over-spaced** — the heading was rendered at 14pt with `setCharSpace(4)`, producing a heavier and more spread appearance than the HTML export's JetBrains Mono 300 at 20px with CSS `letter-spacing: 4px`. Fixed: 13pt with `setCharSpace(2)`.
- **PDF export header line spacing too cramped** — the baseline-to-baseline gaps between the heading, meta line, and badge row were 6pt and 5pt. Fixed: 20pt title-to-meta gap and 14pt meta-to-badge gap.
- **PDF export badge border unevenly padded** — the badge rect was positioned using the full em square above the text baseline, leaving too much space above the text and not enough below. Fixed using cap height (`hBadgePt × 0.72`) and descender height (`hBadgePt × 0.20`) for visually even vertical padding.
- **Permalink export files showed raw ISO 8601 timestamp** — the `created` field from the server is an ISO 8601 string (e.g. `2026-04-16T07:57:31.474893+00:00`). Both `saveHtml()` and `savePdf()` in `permalink.html` passed it directly into the export header. Now formatted with `new Date(created).toLocaleString()` so the timestamp reads like `4/16/2026, 7:57:31 AM` in the exported file.
- **Permalink history page showed only `$` instead of the full prompt echo** — when `appendPromptNewline` stored a trailing empty prompt entry (`{text: "$", cls: "prompt-echo"}`) in the command history, the `has_prompt_echo` check in `_normalize_permalink_lines` was satisfied by that bare entry, preventing the synthetic `$ {label}` command header from being added to the permalink output. Fixed by requiring the prompt-echo entry to have non-whitespace content after the first word, so a bare `$` no longer suppresses the header.
- **HTML exports used a hardcoded 13px font instead of the terminal font size** — `buildTerminalExportStyles` in `export_html.js` applied `font-size: 13px` and `line-height: 1.65` to the export body, ignoring the `--terminal-font-size` and `--terminal-line-height` CSS variables that are captured into the exported document's `:root` block. The export body now uses `font-size: var(--terminal-font-size, 14px)` and `line-height: var(--terminal-line-height, 1.65)` so the exported font matches the live terminal.
- **`session-token set` now validates the token exists on this server** — a typo or token from a different instance would previously activate silently and return empty results for all subsequent API calls.
  - **Root cause:** any `tok_` string was accepted by the client without checking whether the server had actually issued it.
  - **Fix:** a new `POST /session/token/verify` endpoint returns `{"ok": true, "exists": true/false}`; the terminal `session-token set` command and the options-modal Set flow now call it before applying the token. UUIDs (anonymous sessions) always pass. `/session/migrate` applies the same check on its `to_session_id` field, rejecting unissued `tok_` destinations with 400 before any data is moved. The verification is fail-closed: a network error or non-OK server response blocks the switch rather than allowing an unverified token through, so transient server issues cannot silently strand the user on a bogus identity.
  - **Tests:** covered by existing `TestSessionToken` plus route-level checks against unissued tokens.
- **Cross-tab session switch now refreshes history, chips, and the options panel** — the `storage` event listener in `session.js` only updated `SESSION_ID` in passive tabs; it did not reload the chip bar, history panel, or options-panel token display. After a session token is set or cleared in any tab, the listener now calls `reloadSessionHistory()` (if defined) and `_updateOptionsSessionTokenStatus()` (if defined) so the passive tab's UI reflects the new session identity immediately without a page reload.
- **Options panel session token buttons incorrect on mobile** — the Rotate and Clear buttons were visible on mobile even when no session token was set, because `_updateOptionsSessionTokenStatus()` was only called from a `click` listener on the desktop options button. On mobile, the panel opens via `openOptions()` directly, which never called it. Moved the call into `openOptions()` so it runs regardless of how the panel is opened; removed the now-redundant standalone listener.
- **Diagnostics page mobile breakpoint did not match the shell's mobile-mode threshold** — touch devices between 761px and 900px (where the shell is in mobile mode) showed no back button on `/diag`, while narrow desktop windows under 760px showed the mobile back button even in desktop mode.
  - **Root cause:** the back button and mobile header chrome on `/diag` were controlled by `@media (max-width: 760px)`, while the shell's `useMobileTerminalViewportMode()` switches into mobile mode at `max-width: 900px` combined with touch/coarse-pointer detection — a two-dimensional criterion that a single-width media query cannot match.
  - **Fix:** the responsive collapse block in `diag.css` has been split — grid and column layout continue to collapse at `max-width: 760px` for all device types, while the mobile chrome (back button, header layout overrides) now activates at `@media (max-width: 900px) and (pointer: coarse)` to match the same width + touch criteria the shell uses.
  - **Tests:** no new cases — visual verification across the boundary widths on touch and non-touch devices.

### Changed

#### Diagnostics and Mobile Chrome Plumbing

- **Diagnostics page CSS extracted to `diag.css`** — the 312-line inline `<style>` block in `diag.html` has been moved to `app/static/css/diag.css` and loaded as a linked stylesheet. `terminal_export.css` is now also linked from `diag.html` so the `export-header` and `export-header-copy` classes it defines are active on the diagnostics page, establishing the same shared header chrome foundation used by permalink pages. No visual change; this is a structural refactor.
- **`_setMobileActionLabel` centralises mobile menu label updates** — `_setTsMode` in `app.js` and `_setLnMode` in `output.js` previously each queried the mobile menu DOM independently to update action button labels. Both now go through a shared `_setMobileActionLabel(action, label)` helper in `app.js`, which holds the `mobileMenu` reference. `output.js` calls it via a `typeof` guard matching the pattern used elsewhere across the codebase.

#### Built-In Commands and Operator Surfaces

- **Built-in command presentation** — the shell’s built-in commands now read more like intentional terminal output instead of plain text dumps. `help`, `shortcuts`, `status`, `limits`, `retention`, `faq`, `history`, `last`, `version`, `whoami`, `env`, `ls`, `ps`, `ip a`, `route`, `jobs`, `df -h`, `free -h`, and plain `uname` now use clearer section headers, shell-style summaries, or session-aware output where appropriate. The snark pools for `sudo`, `reboot`, `poweroff` / `halt` / `shutdown now`, `su`, and the guarded `rm -fr /` / `rm -rf /` variants were also refreshed to use drier, more technical sarcasm while keeping the responses random.
- **`ps` command now shows active running processes** — `ps` previously returned command history. It now outputs PID, TTY, STAT, START, and CMD columns for currently running processes in the session (or a "no running processes" notice when idle), matching the conventional behavior of the real `ps` command.

#### Export and Permalink Rendering

- **Export rendering centralized through `ExportHtmlUtils`** — `export_html.js` is now the single source of truth for all HTML export rendering. `buildExportLinesHtml`, `buildTerminalExportHtml`, `buildTerminalExportStyles`, and `fetchTerminalExportCss` are consumed by all callers — desktop `tabs.js` and permalink `permalink.html` — so visual style changes propagate automatically to all save surfaces for HTML output without manual synchronization. `terminal_export.css` serves as the single source of truth for export-specific styles; `fetchTerminalExportCss` fetches it once (with module-level caching) and embeds it into every exported HTML document.

#### Operator Guidance and Diagnostics

- **Share snapshot wording and diagnostics visibility** — the active-tab action is now labeled `share snapshot` to distinguish it from the history drawer’s canonical run permalink path. The built-in FAQ now explains the difference explicitly, `config.yaml` documents the exact built-in redaction categories, and `/diag` now surfaces both `share_redaction_enabled` and the configured `custom_redaction_rule_count` in its Config section.

#### UI Polish and Consistency

- **Tab drag-and-drop polish** — desktop tabs no longer use the browser’s native drag ghost and now move live under the pointer, matching the direct-manipulation feel of the mobile tab strip. Mobile reordering now uses an intentional hold-to-drag gesture so normal horizontal swipes still scroll the strip, and both desktop and mobile visually isolate the dragged tab by lifting it, dimming/scaling sibling tabs, and using a dashed border when an inactive tab is being moved.
- **Mobile history drawer actions** — common mobile history actions now feel less desktop-like. On touch-sized screens, the toggleable star sits beside the command instead of consuming an action-row slot, `copy` and `permalink` keep the drawer open instead of dismissing it after every tap, and the remaining action buttons use larger touch targets in a cleaner single-row three-button layout.
- **History row star toggle polish** — the history star is now a dedicated glyph beside the command instead of a full action-row button, it uses a larger visual target on desktop and mobile, and toggling it keeps the drawer open on desktop as well as mobile.
- **HUD clock timezone preference** — the desktop HUD `CLOCK` pill is no longer locked to UTC.
  - **Before:** the pill always rendered `HH:MM:SS UTC`, with no way to switch to the browser's local timezone even when the rest of the shell was being used as a live operator dashboard.
  - **After:** the Options modal now includes a `HUD Clock` preference with `UTC` and `Local Time` modes. The selected mode is persisted in the same cookie-backed preference layer as timestamps and line numbers, the pill updates immediately when the setting changes, and local mode now prefers the browser's short timezone label (`CDT`, `EST`, and similar) with a GMT offset fallback when the browser cannot provide a stable abbreviation.
- **Desktop HUD polling is now visibility-aware** — the HUD keeps its live-dashboard feel in the foreground without needlessly hammering `/status` in background tabs.
  - **Before:** the desktop shell polled `GET /status` every 15 seconds regardless of whether the tab was visible.
  - **After:** visible tabs poll every 3 seconds, hidden tabs stay on the original 15-second cadence, and returning to a visible tab triggers an immediate refresh.
- **Mobile recents sheet now dismisses the keyboard when the user scrolls results** — searching on the mobile history sheet no longer keeps the keyboard open while browsing results.
  - **Before:** after typing a search query in the mobile recents sheet, the on-screen keyboard stayed open while the user scrolled through results. On phone viewports this left only 2 visible result rows at a time, requiring a separate manual tap to dismiss the keyboard before browsing.
  - **After:** a `touchmove` listener on `#mobile-recents-list` (with `{ passive: true }`) blurs the search input whenever the user starts scrolling while it is focused. The keyboard falls away naturally as the finger begins moving down the results, revealing the full result list — matching the iOS Mail and Contacts dismiss pattern.
  - **Tests:** no new automated cases — iOS keyboard dismiss behavior is not replicable in Playwright's desktop Chromium driver. Net suite total unchanged: 842 pytest + 666 Vitest + 197 Playwright = **1,705 tests**.
- **Shortcuts and options overlays now use the same stripped-down footer treatment as the rest of the shell** — low-value explanatory notes were removed instead of lingering as one-off modal chrome.
  - **Before:** the keyboard-shortcuts overlay still carried a browser-shortcuts disclaimer at the bottom, and the Options modal ended with a `Persistence` footer item that mostly restated obvious per-browser behavior.
  - **After:** both notes are gone. The shortcuts surface now ends cleanly on the actual shortcut list, and the Options modal keeps the preference controls only.
- **Keyboard shortcuts modal now uses the shared overlay tokens** — the shortcut reference no longer has bespoke visual treatment.
  - **Before:** `#shortcuts-overlay` and `#shortcuts-modal` used a special transparent/translucent styling that made the shortcuts surface look like a one-off instead of part of the same modal family as FAQ, theme, and options.
  - **After:** the shortcuts overlay now uses the shared backdrop and modal-surface CSS variables (`--theme-overlay-backdrop-bg` and `--theme-faq-modal-bg`) so it matches the rest of the shell's overlay system.
- **FAQ limits layout** — the FAQ limits block now renders as a responsive label/value grid instead of a cramped inherited table. Long labels like `Permalink & history retention` no longer wrap awkwardly, the `&amp;` entity leak is fixed, and the block now reads like a proper modal summary rather than raw UI scaffolding.
- **PDF export extracted to `export_pdf.js`** — the PDF rendering logic (`parseCssColor`, `themeColors`, `renderAnsiLine`, `buildTerminalExportPdf`) previously duplicated across `tabs.js` (~180 lines) and `permalink.html` (~170 lines) has been extracted into a standalone `app/static/js/export_pdf.js` module following the same IIFE / `window.ExportPdfUtils` pattern as `export_html.js`. Both call sites now delegate to the shared module. Six Vitest unit tests cover the public API with a canvas mock that works around jsdom's lack of native canvas support.
- **Permalink page controller extracted to `permalink.js`** — the inline `{% block scripts %}` controller in `permalink.html` (~250 lines, `const`/arrow-function style) has been extracted into a standalone `app/static/js/permalink.js` IIFE module that reads server data from a minimal `window.PermData` bridge. The module reuses `ExportHtmlUtils.renderExportPromptEcho` and `ExportHtmlUtils.exportTimestamp` instead of the inline duplicates, delegates clipboard copy and toast to `copyTextToClipboard` / `showToast` from `utils.js` (loaded in `permalink_base.html`), and uses `data-action` event delegation instead of inline `onclick` attributes. The `#copy-toast` element was renamed `#permalink-toast` to match the ID that `showToast` in `utils.js` already expects. 37 Vitest unit tests cover output rendering, toggle cycling, prefix formatting, and all four action dispatch paths.
- **Theme resolution and font manifest unified into `helpers.py`** — `_current_theme()` in `permalinks.py` and `_current_theme_name()` in `content.py` were separate implementations of the same cookie → default fallback logic. Both are replaced by `current_theme_name()` and `resolve_theme()` in `helpers.py`. `resolve_theme()` returns `(name, source)` so `content.py` can still emit the `THEME_SELECTED` debug event with the resolution source without re-implementing the lookup. The font manifest (`_FONT_FILES` in `permalinks.py` and `_VENDOR_FONT_FILES` in `assets.py`) was also two separate lists of the same five fonts; `assets.py` now derives its route allowlist from the shared `FONT_FILES` constant in `helpers.py`, so adding or removing a font propagates to both surfaces automatically.
- **Vendor asset routes simplified** — the `/vendor/ansi_up.js`, `/vendor/jspdf.umd.min.js`, and `/vendor/fonts/` routes previously carried a vendor-path-first / static-fallback pattern inherited from an earlier CDN-download-on-boot approach. Since all assets are now committed to `app/static/` and that is the authoritative source in both dev and Docker (via bind mount), the build-time `/usr/local/share/shell-assets/` copy and font download steps have been removed from the Dockerfile and the route handlers simplified to serve directly from the static path. The `/diag` vendor assets section now reports `loaded` / `missing` instead of `vendor` / `fallback`.
- **`.env` renamed to `.env.example`** — the committed environment file was renamed to `.env.example` (copy → edit locally) and `.env` added to `.gitignore`. The README quick-start and file tree were updated to reflect the new workflow.

### Added

- **README project-structure tree drift test** — the `## Project Structure` section in `README.md` is now verified against `git ls-files --cached --others --exclude-standard` by three new pytest cases in `tests/py/test_docs.py`.
  - **Why:** without a gate, the tree drifts silently as files are added, renamed, or removed. The first run of this test exposed 26 files that had drifted out of the tree over the v1.5 development cycle and four directory entries that were missing entirely.
  - **What:** `TestProjectStructureCoverage.test_no_files_missing_from_structure` fails when a tracked-or-untracked-but-not-gitignored file isn't listed in the tree (catching the same MR that introduces a new file, before it's even committed); `test_listed_paths_exist_in_git` fails when the tree references a file that doesn't exist (catching typos and stale entries); `test_opaque_dirs_appear_in_structure` fails when a directory declared opaque in `_PROJECT_STRUCTURE_OPAQUE_DIRS` isn't shown as a parent entry. Two narrow forms of intentional omission are supported: `_PROJECT_STRUCTURE_EXCLUSIONS` for individual paths (currently `app/blueprints/__init__.py` only) and `_PROJECT_STRUCTURE_OPAQUE_DIRS` for whole subtrees summarised by a single parent entry (`app/conf/themes/`, `app/static/fonts/`, `assets/`, `tests/js/e2e/fixtures/`). All drifted files have been added back to `README.md` in this MR with proper descriptions, restoring the tree to its intended role as a complete navigation map.
  - **Tests:** three new pytest cases in `TestProjectStructureCoverage`; doc gate rises from 18 to 21 tests.
- **`scripts/seed_history.py` for populating history during user testing** — a new helper that inserts ~70 realistic runs into `history.db` under a caller-specified session.
  - **Why:** manual testing of history drawer filters (command-root, exit code, starred, date range, FTS trigram search) needs realistic rows; generating them by hand is slow and doesn't exercise the FTS5 `runs_ai` trigger path. Writing to SQLite from two processes whose versions disagree on the FTS5 internal page format corrupts the `runs_fts_data` btree ("database disk image is malformed") — a real footgun when seeding from the host while the container is running.
  - **What:** identities — `--new-token` generates and registers a fresh `tok_` token, `--token tok_...` registers the token if missing, `--uuid` uses an anonymous UUID session. Commands are drawn from a pool of ~40 templates covering DNS, HTTP, nmap/port scan, WHOIS, connectivity, web fuzzing/enum, and shell built-ins. Runs are spread across the last N days (default 7, bias toward recent), exit codes vary (0 / 1 / 2 / 3 / 22 / 28 / 127), output is wrapped into the same `{text,cls,tsC,tsE}` preview-entry shape the live shell writes, and `output_search_text` is populated so the FTS5 `runs_ai` trigger indexes every row at INSERT time. `--count`, `--days`, `--star`, and `--seed` tune volume, date span, number of starred commands, and RNG reproducibility. The script uses raw `sqlite3` (not `db_connect()` from `app/database.py`) so importing it has no write side effects — `db_init()` runs DROP/CREATE TRIGGER and an FTS rebuild, which we do not want a seeding script to perform — and `APP_DATA_DIR` is resolved with the same fallback as the app (`/data` if it exists, else `/tmp`). `_require_schema()` fails fast if the target DB has not been initialised by the app yet. `_guard_host_write_to_project_data()` refuses to write to the project's own `data/history.db` when invoked from the host (detected via the absence of `/.dockerenv`), and prints a ready-to-paste `docker compose exec -T shell python - <forwarded args> < scripts/seed_history.py` invocation (the script is piped over stdin because `scripts/` is not mounted into the container — only `./app:/app:ro` and `./data:/data` are); an `--allow-host-write` escape hatch is provided for cases where the container is genuinely stopped.
  - **Tests:** the guard is manually-validated (destructive corruption path can't be automated safely); command pool exercised via end-to-end history drawer runs.
- **Expanded HUD status pills** — the desktop HUD bar now renders eleven live status pills instead of the original four.
  - **Why:** the original four (`STATUS`, `TRANSPORT`, `MODE`, `DB`) told operators almost nothing about live server or session state — no latency, no uptime, no visibility into active runs or session identity.
  - **What:** seven new pills — `LAST EXIT` (most recent run's exit code, coloured green/red/amber for ok/fail/killed), `RUNS` (running / total tabs, amber while any tab is running), `LATENCY` (round-trip time to `/status`, coloured by `<250ms / <500ms / >=500ms` thresholds), `SESSION` (masked `tok_xxxx` or `ANON`), `UPTIME` (server uptime, ticking client-side between polls to avoid a frozen-looking pill), `CLOCK` (live clock with user-selectable `UTC` or browser-local mode), and `REDIS` (online/offline/N-A when unconfigured). A new lightweight `/status` endpoint in `assets.py` returns `{uptime, db, redis, server_time}` as always-200 JSON; visible tabs now poll every 3 seconds, hidden tabs stay on a 15-second cadence, the HUD measures latency via `performance.now()` around the fetch call, and uptime is interpolated locally between polls. Local clock mode prefers the browser's short timezone label and falls back to a GMT offset label when needed. `setHudLastExit(code)` is exposed on `window` and called from `runner.js` on every SSE `exit` event and on kill. All pills start muted with a `—` placeholder and transition to live values on first poll. The pill row uses `overflow-x: auto` so narrow windows fall back gracefully without reflowing the HUD actions on the right.
  - **Tests:** new Vitest cases for `setHudLastExit` colour mapping and `UPTIME` client-side interpolation between polls.
- **`session-token list` and `session-token revoke`** — two session token safety operations added to the built-in `session-token` command. `session-token list` calls `GET /session/token/info` and displays the current token and its creation date. `session-token revoke <token>` calls `POST /session/token/revoke`, which permanently deletes the token from the server; if the revoked token is the currently active one, the client also clears local storage and falls back to an anonymous session. Possession of the token string is the only authorization check, matching the existing session model. Both new subcommands are intercepted client-side and dispatched to the new endpoints; `session-token revoke` is included in the runtime built-in autocomplete context with a `<token>` positional hint.
- **Browser notifications on run completion** — the Options panel now includes a "Run Notifications" toggle. When enabled, a browser notification fires each time a run exits (any exit code) or is killed by the user. The notification title is `$ <command>` (truncated to 80 characters) and the body is `exit <code> in <elapsed>` or `killed after <elapsed>`. Enabling triggers the browser's native permission prompt if permission has not yet been granted; if the browser has already blocked notifications, the toggle reverts to off and a toast is shown. The preference is stored as `pref_run_notify` in the same cookie store as other display preferences and syncs to the toggle on every page load.
- **Demo recording pipeline** — desktop and mobile demo recording scripts and Playwright specs for producing the README demo videos.
  - **Why:** the README's hero videos need Retina-resolution, theme-switching, and mobile-keyboard-correct frames that Playwright's built-in video recorder cannot produce (it ignores `deviceScaleFactor` and triggers Chromium's gray mobile-keyboard overlay on any input focus).
  - **What:** `scripts/record_demo.sh` / `scripts/record_demo_mobile.sh` health-check the container, invoke Playwright with a dedicated config (`config/playwright.demo.config.js` / `config/playwright.demo.mobile.config.js`), and stitch the captured frames into a video with ffmpeg (HEVC via VideoToolbox on macOS, VP9 via libvpx on Linux) at 15 fps. Frames are captured with `page.screenshot()` (respects scale factor, produces full Retina images). Theme transitions use `applyThemeSelection()` called directly in the page context rather than dispatching a DOM click event — clicking a `<button>` triggers Chromium's native focus-scroll management which repositions the theme container even when the card is already fully visible, producing a one-frame jump. The mobile spec injects a fake keyboard image over the composer area rather than focusing the real input (focusing any input in Chromium's headless mobile emulation triggers a gray keyboard-simulation overlay that sits above all page content regardless of z-index). The specs are not part of the normal test suite and are only matched by their respective demo configs; they are also guarded by `RUN_DEMO=1` so they cannot run accidentally.
  - **Tests:** not applicable — the specs are themselves the recording tooling; validation is visual review of the output `.mp4`.
- **Developer linting infrastructure** — twelve static analysis and audit checks are wired into a unified pre-commit hook at `scripts/hooks/pre-commit` (activated once with `git config core.hooksPath scripts/hooks`).
  - **Why:** the old `.githooks/pre-commit` was Python-only, so JS, YAML, shell, Docker, and Markdown drift slipped into commits unchecked. Vendor JS drift and dependency CVEs were caught (if at all) only in CI.
  - **What:** ESLint for JS config and test files; shellcheck for tracked bash/sh scripts; hadolint for the Dockerfile; yamllint for all YAML files; markdownlint-cli2 for all Markdown files; `npm audit` for JS dependency CVEs (high/critical only); `vendor:check` to ensure committed vendor JS is in sync with npm; and the existing Python checks (flake8, bandit, pytest, pip-audit) and Vitest unit run. The pre-commit hook was consolidated and moved to the tracked `scripts/hooks/` directory. Individual npm scripts: `npm run lint:py` (flake8 + bandit), `npm run lint:js`, `npm run lint:shell`, `npm run lint:docker`, `npm run lint:yaml`, `npm run lint:md`, `npm run vendor:check`; `npm run lint` runs all. Audit scripts: `npm run audit:py` (pip-audit), `npm run audit:js` (npm audit), `npm run audit` runs both.
  - **Tests:** the hook itself is the gate — every commit exercises it; CI runs the same scripts as a safety net.
- **Vendor JS management** — `ansi_up` and `jspdf` are now tracked as `dependencies` in `package.json`. `scripts/build_vendor.mjs` generates the committed browser builds from npm packages: `ansi_up` is wrapped as an IIFE browser global (it is ESM-only in v6) and `jspdf` is copied directly from its npm UMD build. Run `npm run vendor:sync` to regenerate after a version bump; `npm run vendor:check` verifies the committed files in `app/static/js/vendor/` match what would be produced from the current `node_modules/` packages. The check runs in CI (`lint-js` job), in the pre-commit hook, and as part of `npm run lint`.
- **`--commands-file` flag for the capture script** — `scripts/capture_container_smoke_test_outputs.sh` now accepts `--commands-file <path>` to run a specific subset of commands from a plain-text file (one per line, `#` comments ignored) instead of the full `autocomplete.yaml` example set. Useful for re-capturing only the commands that are missing expectations or whose output has changed intentionally.
- **Share/export redaction rules** — snapshot permalinks and local `save txt` / `save html` exports now use a built-in basic redaction baseline for common sensitive values such as bearer tokens, email addresses, IPs, and hostnames, with optional operator regex rules appended after it. The feature is controlled by `share_redaction_enabled`, keeps normal run history unchanged in this first phase, and is enforced server-side before snapshot persistence.
- **Permalink share-time redaction choice** — when share redaction is enabled, creating a snapshot permalink now asks whether to share the redacted or raw version, explains the kinds of values redaction covers, and can optionally write that chosen raw/redacted mode back into the persistent Options default. The `/share` route now honors an explicit `apply_redaction` flag so the server matches the UI’s raw-vs-redacted choice instead of always forcing the redacted path.
- **History drawer filtering and search** — the run history drawer now supports search by command text plus filters for command root, exit code, recent date range, and starred status. Active filters are shown as removable chips, non-today runs show a date token in the result metadata, and the command-root field now uses app-owned autocomplete suggestions backed by a server-provided `roots` list instead of a native browser datalist.
  - **History pagination** — the history drawer and mobile history sheet now paginate stored runs instead of treating `history_panel_limit` as a hard cap. The backend now returns `page`, `page_size`, `total_count`, `page_count`, `has_prev`, and `has_next` for panel fetches; both surfaces render a three-number window with `..` ellipses plus `Prev` / `Next`; and starred-only filtering is server-side so the pager stays accurate. Reverse-i-search and other non-panel consumers still fetch without `include_total`.
  - **Mobile/search text-input defaults** — the stable app inputs that should suppress browser text assistance now declare that directly in markup with `autocomplete="off"`, `autocapitalize="none"`, `autocorrect="off"`, `spellcheck="false"`, and `inputmode="text"`. A narrow `applyMobileTextInputDefaults()` helper remains only for dynamically created inputs such as the session-token modal, and the intermediate attempt to apply that helper to the live mobile composer at boot was removed after it broke mobile input events, autocomplete, and keyboard-helper visibility.
- **Reconnect active runs after reload** — the shell now restores in-flight runs for the current session after a reload using a new `/history/active` route. Reloaded tabs keep the command label, normal prompt-echo formatting, and kill action while they wait, poll for completion in the background, and automatically swap into the saved run view once the command finishes.
- **Session restore for tabs and drafts** — non-running tabs now persist their labels, transcript previews, status, and draft input in browser session storage so a reload can rebuild the recent shell workspace without replaying welcome or losing in-progress draft text. Restored completed tabs remount a usable live prompt immediately, keep prompt-prefix formatting in restored transcript lines, and preserve non-active tab drafts as well as the active tab draft. Active runs still restore through `/history/active`, so reload continuity now covers both live and idle tabs.
- **More bash-like tab completion** — autocomplete `Tab` handling now expands to the longest shared prefix before cycling suggestions, repeated `Tab` presses walk the current matches, `Shift+Tab` cycles backward, and `Enter` remains the accept key for the highlighted suggestion. This keeps the shell-feel improvement scoped to the frontend autocomplete path without changing subprocess semantics.
- **Context-aware autocomplete** — autocomplete is no longer limited to a flat string list. The browser now loads a structured command-context registry from `/autocomplete`, prefers root-aware suggestions after the first token, renders short inline descriptions for contextual flags and value hints, suppresses already-used flags such as duplicate `nmap` options, and replaces only the current token when accepting a contextual suggestion instead of rewriting the whole command line.
- **Built-in pipe support** — the shell now supports a narrow app-native `command | grep ...`, `command | head ...`, `command | tail ...`, and `command | wc -l` model without enabling general shell pipes. `grep` supports `-i`, `-v`, and `-E`; `head` and `tail` support the default 10-line form or `-n <count>`; `wc` is limited to `-l`. Only the base command executes, the app applies the post-filter before streaming and persistence, and the filtered transcript is the canonical saved output for that run.
- **Pipe-stage autocomplete** — built-in pipe support now participates in contextual autocomplete. After typing `command |`, the dropdown can suggest the supported pipe commands (`grep`, `head`, `tail`, `wc -l`), then switch into stage-specific hints such as `grep -i/-v/-E`, `head -n`, `tail -n`, and common count values after `-n`.
- **Expanded user options** — the options modal now also stores a persistent welcome-intro preference and a persistent share-snapshot redaction default. The welcome intro can stay animated, render immediately without animation, or be removed completely, and the snapshot redaction prompt is skipped once a persistent raw/redacted default has been chosen.
- **Mobile keyboard edit-bar improvements** — the mobile composer helper row now adds word-left and word-right cursor jumps alongside the existing Home, End, character-move, and delete-word actions. This keeps longer mobile command editing practical without introducing a separate mobile-only command model.
- **New security tools** — seven additional tools are now installed, allowed, and covered by contextual autocomplete: `sslscan` and `sslyze` for TLS certificate and cipher scanning; `naabu` (ProjectDiscovery) and `rustscan` for fast port scanning; `katana` (ProjectDiscovery) for web crawling; `wafw00f` for WAF detection; and `masscan` for high-speed host discovery. `openssl s_client` and `openssl ciphers` are also now allowed, scoped to TLS inspection use cases with file-read flags denied. All new tools use per-tool deny rules to block file output flags and loopback targets, and `naabu` and `masscan` have `cap_net_raw`/`cap_net_admin` capabilities set in the Dockerfile so they can run without full root privileges.
- **`sort` and `uniq` pipe stages** — the built-in pipe model now supports `command | sort`, `command | sort -r`, `command | sort -n`, `command | sort -u`, and combined flags (e.g. `command | sort -rn`), as well as `command | uniq` and `command | uniq -c`. Like the existing `grep`, `head`, `tail`, and `wc -l` stages, these run as post-filter steps in the app after the base command completes and the filtered output becomes the canonical saved transcript.
- **Guided workflows panel** — the shell now includes a Workflows panel (⊡ button) with curated multi-step command sequences for common diagnostic scenarios: DNS troubleshooting, TLS/HTTPS inspection, quick reachability checks, and email server verification. Each workflow card shows the steps in order with a short note per command, and any step can be clicked to load its command directly into the active prompt. Operators can extend or replace the built-in workflows via `conf/workflows.yaml`.
- **PDF export** — all save surfaces (desktop tab action bar, permalink page, mobile menu) can now export a themed PDF directly in the browser using jsPDF. The PDF matches the HTML export's visual layout: a header with the app name, command, exit-status badge, and timestamp, followed by ANSI-rendered terminal output. Theme colors are resolved from the active CSS custom properties at export time. Export is a direct browser download with no server round-trip.
- **Unified `save ▾` dropdown** — the three output export formats (txt, html, pdf) are now grouped under a single `save ▾` dropdown button on the desktop tab action bar, the permalink page header, and the mobile menu. Previously the desktop bar had separate "Download" and "Export HTML" buttons; the permalink page had three separate buttons; the mobile save path was inconsistent.
- **Full-text search across run output** — the history drawer search field now searches through stored command output content, not just command text. A SQLite FTS5 virtual table (`runs_fts`) indexes each run's `command` and `output_search_text` columns using the trigram tokenizer (falls back to unicode61 on SQLite < 3.38), enabling substring matching for port numbers, CVEs, IPs, flags, and other security tool output. New runs populate the index automatically via INSERT/DELETE triggers; existing databases are backfilled and rebuilt on first startup. The history search placeholder was updated from "search commands" to "search commands and output". Fallback to command-text `LIKE` search is applied automatically if FTS is unavailable.
- **Native share-sheet for permalink URLs** — the `share snapshot` action now calls `navigator.share()` on browsers that support the Web Share API, providing a native OS share sheet on mobile devices. If the browser does not support the API or the user cancels the share, it falls back silently to copying the URL to the clipboard.
- **Mobile e2e `runCommandMobile` race condition** — the helper fired `simulateMobileKeyboard` after `pressSequentially`, which triggered a `visualViewport` resize event with 120 ms async callbacks that could leave the composer empty and the run button disabled by the time the test tried to click it. Fixed by firing the keyboard simulation first and replacing `pressSequentially` with the atomic `setComposerValueForTest` helper so button state is evaluated only after the value is cleanly set.
- **Dead DOM wiring in `dom.js`** — `faqLimitsText` and `faqAllowedText` were cached at module load time via `getElementById`, but those elements are created dynamically and do not exist at load time, so the constants were always `null`. The constants were removed and the two call sites updated to call `getElementById` directly at use time.
- **CI lint scripts used `git ls-files` without git installed** — `yamllint` and `shellcheck` invocations in both `package.json` and `.gitlab-ci.yml` used `git ls-files` to enumerate files, but the CI runner images (`python:3.14-slim`, `node:22-slim`) do not have git installed. Replaced with `find` using explicit `.git/` and `node_modules/` exclusions. The `git` package was also removed from the `lint-js` CI job's apt install since it is no longer needed.
- **`.dockerignore`** — a `.dockerignore` was added to exclude development directories (`.git/`, `.venv/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `node_modules/`, etc.) from the Docker build context. The CI pipeline already referenced this file but it did not previously exist.
- **Options modal session token buttons execute operations natively** — Generate, Set, Rotate, and Clear no longer run commands in the terminal or pre-fill the composer.
  - **Why:** pre-filling the composer with a `session-token ...` line dragged the user out of the options flow and into a terminal they didn't ask for. The token paste path also risked visible secrets in the transcript.
  - **What:** Generate and Rotate issue the token directly via the server, copy the new token to the clipboard, and show a toast. Set opens a dedicated theme-aware input modal (`#session-token-set-overlay`) so the user can paste a token without typing in the terminal. Clear reverts to the anonymous session inline. History migration confirmation is handled by a separate theme-aware modal (`#session-token-migrate-overlay`) shared by all paths (CLI and UI) that trigger migration. Both sub-modals use the `.modal-overlay` + `.modal-card` CSS classes and respond to theme changes automatically.
  - **Tests:** Playwright coverage for each button's native path; theme-audit spec validates the two new overlays across every theme.
- **Server-side starred commands (Phase 2)** — starred commands are now synced to the server via a `starred_commands` table and `/session/starred` REST endpoints (`GET`, `POST`, `DELETE`).
  - **Why:** Phase 1 kept stars in `localStorage`, which didn't follow session tokens across devices or survive a browser reset. Starred commands need to be scoped to session identity just like runs and snapshots are.
  - **What:** `history.js` keeps a local cache (`_starredCache`) so star state is available synchronously on every render without blocking. `loadStarredFromServer()` populates the cache on page load and after every session switch. On first token activation (`session-token generate` or `session-token set`), any commands already starred in `localStorage` are migrated to the new session token automatically and the `localStorage` entry is cleared. `session-token rotate` now also migrates starred commands and reports the count in its output alongside runs and snapshots.
  - **Tests:** new `TestStarredCommands` pytest suite covers the three endpoints; Vitest cases cover `_starredCache` synchronous reads and migration-on-first-token-activation.
- **Persistent session tokens (Phase 1)** — users can now generate a named session token with `session-token generate` and optionally associate it with their existing run history.
  - **Why:** anonymous UUID sessions lived only in the browser's `sessionStorage` — clearing it, switching browsers, or reloading with a different identity destroyed access to prior runs. A persistent, copyable token lets users carry their history across browsers and sessions without introducing accounts or passwords.
  - **What:** a `tok_<32 hex>` token is stored in the `session_tokens` database table (added via automatic schema migration) and in `localStorage` under `session_token`. All API requests send the active identity in the `X-Session-ID` header; `updateSessionId()` switches the identity at runtime without a page reload. `session-token set <token>` accepts an existing token and optionally migrates history from the current anonymous UUID session. `session-token clear` reverts to the auto-generated UUID session. `session-token rotate` generates a new token and atomically migrates all run history before switching identity. Bare `session-token` prints the current session token status in the terminal. An options panel row shows the masked active session token and provides Generate, Set, Rotate, and Clear shortcut buttons; Generate and Set are shown only when no token is active, Rotate and Clear only when one is. The `/session/token/generate` and `/session/migrate` (POST) routes are registered under the new `session` Blueprint. `maskSessionToken()` is a shared utility in `session.js` for display-safe token representation (`tok_XXXX••••` or `uuid8ch••••••••`). Session token subcommands are intercepted client-side and never reach the server; the bare `session-token` status command is handled as a normal fake command.
  - **Tests:** `TestSessionToken` pytest suite covers generate, set, clear, rotate, migrate, and schema migration; Vitest cases cover `maskSessionToken` formatting and `updateSessionId` runtime switching.

### Removed

- **`parse_synthetic_grep()` compatibility shim** — the function was a thin wrapper around `parse_synthetic_postfilter` left over from an earlier rename. All six callers in `tests/py/test_validation.py` have been updated to call `parse_synthetic_postfilter` directly and the wrapper has been deleted.
- **`readme-screenshot.spec.js` and `readme-screenshot-mobile.spec.js`** — the one-off screenshot capture specs used to produce static README hero images have been removed. The README now embeds the full demo `.mp4` videos produced by the demo recording pipeline instead.
- **`scripts/smoke_test_commands.txt`** — the manually maintained command list has been deleted. The smoke test corpus is now sourced exclusively from `autocomplete.yaml` examples, making the file redundant.

---

## [1.4] — 2026-04-12

### Fixed
- **Firefox mobile keyboard shell instability** — the mobile terminal shell was rebuilt around a simpler normal-flow layout after the investigation proved the browser itself was not the root cause.
