The fixed-shell / page-scroll / `visualViewport` pan-compensation stack was removed, `#mobile-shell` now stays in normal document flow, and the composer block stays layout-driven instead of relying on page transforms, scroll correction, or keyboard-height spacing on `#mobile-composer-host`. This removes the intermittent flash, gray-gap, floating-composer, and repeated open/close drift regressions that were showing up in Firefox mobile when the keyboard opened.
- **Mobile keyboard open/close consistency** — the mobile keyboard helper row and composer now follow the focused visible mobile input without synthetic tap-to-focus handlers on the input or lower composer area. The keyboard-open path keeps the last real open offset when viewport reporting lands late, stores a closed-height baseline for later comparisons, and resets the closed layout immediately on hide / blur / backgrounding so repeated opens do not accumulate position drift.
- **Mobile shell polish** — the mobile transcript/composer boundary now keeps a consistent gap in both closed and keyboard-open states, the permalink/copy/save action row uses the same horizontal gutter as the mobile composer block, and the mobile header status pill was re-aligned next to the hamburger button for a cleaner stacked layout.
- **Recent-command chip row alignment and overflow** — the recent-command strip now sits closer to the header instead of floating inside the global page gap, the chip contents are optically centered between the two seams, and the desktop overflow logic now keeps the `+ more` chip on the first row instead of letting it wrap into a clipped second line.
- **Desktop and mobile tab-row seam polish** — the tab rows now sit flush against the terminal seam without the earlier duplicate borders, gap artifacts, or transient right-edge scrollbar strip. The desktop row also hides the horizontal scrollbar chrome while preserving scrolling behavior.
- **Shell chrome polish pass** — the desktop and mobile header/title lockup, recent-command row, footer/action strip, terminal controls, welcome-to-prompt handoff, and mobile history panel were all tightened so the shell chrome reads more like one composed surface instead of a stack of unrelated bands. Mobile sheet-style overlays now also expose a drag handle and support downward drag-to-close gestures.
- **MOTD placement** — the optional operator message no longer renders as a separate strip above the shell. When configured, it now appears inside the welcome sequence as a centered “Message From The Operator” notice and stays visible there until the welcome output is cleared, which gives operators a place for downtime/change messaging without adding permanent shell chrome.
- **Welcome block separation** — the settled welcome block now has a little more breathing room before normal transcript content begins, so the welcome ASCII/status area reads like a completed section without turning the live prompt into a styled component.
- **Theme selector preview workflow** — the theme modal keeps live theme switching, but the desktop experience now uses a right-side drawer so most of the shell stays visible while you compare variants. Mobile keeps the existing full-screen chooser. The desktop diagnostics button also now opens `/diag` in a separate tab while the diagnostics page header uses the same shell badge language as the main UI instead of the older permalink-style header, and the mobile diagnostics page keeps an in-page `back to shell` action.
- **Proxy-aware diagnostics gate** — `diagnostics_allowed_cidrs` now checks the same resolved client IP used by logging and rate limiting instead of only `request.remote_addr`, so `/diag` access and the `diag_enabled` header/menu button work correctly behind trusted reverse proxies. `X-Forwarded-For` still only influences the gate when the direct peer IP falls inside `trusted_proxy_cidrs`.
- **Tab close hover tone** — the tab close button no longer uses a red destructive-looking hover ring in the dark defaults and `darklab_obsidian`. The hover treatment now follows the shell’s neutral/accent language instead of reading like an error state.
- **Theme parity on mobile and dark-theme palette polish** — the mobile composer shell now uses the same injected theme variables as desktop instead of hardcoded dark surfaces, and the obsidian-family themes now ship with darker base backgrounds plus lighter gray chrome values for better contrast. The built-in dark fallback palette and `theme_dark.yaml.example` were aligned with the revised `darklab_obsidian` values.
- **Theme default-family fallback and generated examples** — theme variants can now declare `color_scheme: dark|light` so partial operator themes inherit from the correct built-in default family instead of always merging onto the dark palette. The checked-in `theme_dark.yaml.example` and `theme_light.yaml.example` files are now generated from `_THEME_DEFAULTS` via `scripts/generate_theme_examples.py`, with a backend drift test enforcing that the examples stay in sync with the hardcoded defaults.
- **Obsidian theme variant naming** — the shipped obsidian accent variants now use the filename pattern `cobalt_obsidian.yaml`, `emerald_obsidian.yaml`, and `ember_obsidian.yaml`, which keeps the registry naming consistent with the rest of the theme set and matches the current release documentation.
- **Theme chrome cleanup** — terminal window buttons now inherit per-theme accent values instead of hardcoded traffic-light colors, the last separate `tabs_bar_bg` token was removed so the tab row and terminal header always share one surface, and light-theme shell chrome no longer splits the history row and tab row into competing background bands.
- **Scrollbar polish** — the main scrollable surfaces now share a consistent thin theme-aware scrollbar treatment across the terminal output, history drawer, permalink output, FAQ/theme/options modal bodies, and autocomplete dropdowns while keeping intentionally hidden mobile/tab-strip scrollbars untouched.
- **Permalink / diag theme parity** — the live permalink page, diagnostics page, and downloadable permalink `.html` export now use the same terminal-bar and panel theme tokens as the main shell instead of mixing in raw base palette surfaces, so theme changes carry across those auxiliary pages more consistently.
- **Mobile search close affordance** — the search bar now exposes an in-bar close button on mobile, so you no longer have to re-open the hamburger menu just to dismiss search.
- **Playwright rate-limit isolation** — the browser helpers now generate deterministic `198.18.x.x` test-network addresses for `X-Forwarded-For` instead of rotating through a tiny one-octet pool. That gives the share, mobile, and timestamp specs stable per-test limiter buckets and removes the flaky “history entry never appears because the run was rate limited” failure mode.
- **CSS modularization without a build step** — the old monolithic `app/static/css/styles.css` was split into ordered static files (`base.css`, `shell.css`, `components.css`, `welcome.css`, `mobile.css`) while keeping `styles.css` as a compatibility entrypoint that imports them. This keeps the no-bundler frontend model intact while making the stylesheet easier to navigate and less conflict-prone.
- **Built-in README link source** — the FAQ and synthetic README-style helper output now use the built-in project README constant rather than a configurable `project_readme` YAML setting, which keeps the shipped documentation links aligned across `/config`, fake shell helpers, and the FAQ route.
- **Production Docker override** — the old GELF-only Compose override was replaced with `examples/docker-compose.prod.yml`, which now serves as the production-ready layer for reverse-proxy-aware deployments. It removes host port publishing from the base shell service with a Compose `!reset` override so production uses `expose` instead of a published host port, joins the external `darklab-net` Docker network, sets `VIRTUAL_HOST` / `LETSENCRYPT_HOST` for `nginx-proxy`, pins production-specific container names for `shell` and `redis`, and enables Docker GELF transport for both containers behind the optional `DOCKER_GELF_ADDRESS` setting.
- **Operator runtime tuning via `.env`** — Gunicorn worker and thread counts are now documented as operator-facing `.env` knobs (`WEB_CONCURRENCY`, `WEB_THREADS`) instead of being treated as entrypoint-only implementation details, so runtime sizing can be managed alongside the other deployment options.
- **Mobile output follow-after-keyboard-open** — when the mobile keyboard opens, the active tab’s output is now re-stuck to the bottom so the last line stays visible instead of being clipped behind the composer. A focused Vitest regression locks that behavior in alongside the existing mobile-shell layout guard.
- **Live output tail helper** — when a tab has output but is scrolled off the live tail, the output pane now shows a small jump-to-live / jump-to-bottom button that follows the tab's streaming state. The button stays tab-scoped, swaps from the live label to the bottom label when the stream ends, and snaps the output back to the live tail when clicked. A CSS `[hidden]` override now guarantees the helper actually disappears when hidden, so the button no longer looks stuck visible just because its base display rule is `inline-flex`.
- **Desktop output-selection shortcut replay** — when output text is highlighted on desktop, pressing `ArrowUp`, `ArrowDown`, `Enter`, or `Ctrl+R` now hands control back to the prompt without dropping the shortcut keystroke. History navigation, submit, and reverse-search therefore still work immediately after selecting transcript text.
- **Regression coverage expansion** — added a focused pytest regression for the Container Smoke Test early-kill path, plus Playwright coverage for the live output tail helper and desktop transcript-selection shortcut replay. That closes the biggest remaining gap between the user-visible browser behavior and the earlier jsdom-only coverage.
- **Content view logging expansion** — the main content/config GET routes now emit `CONTENT_VIEWED` info logs with the client IP, session ID, and route/context fields, the home page’s `PAGE_LOAD` log includes the resolved theme, and theme resolution emits a `THEME_SELECTED` DEBUG breadcrumb with the theme name and source so startup and content reads are easier to correlate in production logs.
- **History list access logging** — opening the `/history` list now emits a `HISTORY_VIEWED` info log with the session and returned run count, matching the existing permalink/share access logs and giving operators a trace for history-panel reads.
- **Composer helper state drive** — the shared cursor and mobile edit-bar helpers now read and write selection from `composerState` instead of depending on stale DOM selection, so caret motion stays in sync with the active input even as the input-decoupling refactor continues. A targeted Vitest regression proves caret movement follows shared state rather than whatever selection the hidden desktop input last held.
- **Composer keydown / submit state drive** — the remaining controller key handlers and submit paths now read the active composer text from shared state before they mutate, submit, or inspect it, so `controller.js` and `runner.js` no longer depend on `cmdInput.value` as the global source of truth for Enter and shortcut handling. The runner harness and app tests now seed the shared composer path directly in the phase-5 coverage.
- **Composer draft / history state drive** — tab draft capture, hist-search restore, and the remaining chip/autocomplete restore paths now use the shared composer state instead of pulling directly from whichever DOM input happened to fire last. That keeps draft persistence aligned across desktop typing, mobile typing, and tab switches while the input-decoupling refactor continues.
- **Composer prompt render state drive** — the shell prompt render now reads value and selection from `composerState` instead of from the hidden desktop input, so the prompt line stays correct regardless of which composer view is active. A dedicated Vitest regression proves the prompt render ignores stale DOM input state and follows the shared store.
- **Empty mobile Run button submits** — the shared run-button sync logic now disables both desktop and mobile Run buttons whenever the active tab is running or the current composer value is empty / whitespace-only. Programmatic composer updates use the same path, so recent-command chips and other helpers cannot leave the mobile Run button enabled against a blank prompt.
- **Recent mobile command chip clutter** — mobile recent-command chips no longer prepend the inline star glyph inside the chip body, and chip clicks blur the tapped chip before loading its command so the touch path does not keep stale focus styling around the composer.
- **Loopback address blocking** — commands containing `localhost`, `127.0.0.1`, `0.0.0.0`, or `[::1]` anywhere in the command string are now blocked by `_LOOPBACK_RE` in `commands.py`, using the same pattern as the existing `/data` and `/tmp` path checks. This prevents web shell users from curling internal Flask endpoints (e.g. `curl http://localhost:8888/diag` or `curl 127.0.0.1:8888/config`) regardless of how the URL is formatted. Word-boundary anchors prevent false positives on external hostnames like `notlocalhost.com`. Client-side deny entries (`!curl localhost`, `!curl 127.0.0.1`, `!wget localhost`, etc.) in `conf/allowed_commands.txt` provide immediate browser feedback for the most obvious bare-hostname patterns.
- **History drawer closes on typing** — typing in the command input while the run history drawer was open no longer left the drawer visible. The `input` event handler in `controller.js` now calls `hideHistoryPanel()` when the drawer is open, matching the behavior of submitting a command or opening a modal.
- **Modal overlay keyboard blocking** — the FAQ, Options, and Theme modals now block all keyboard input from reaching the terminal, not just printable characters. Previously, pressing `Enter` while a content modal was open appended a new prompt line to the terminal output, and `Ctrl+C` could trigger kill-confirmation on a running tab. Both the `cmdInput` keydown handler and the `document` keydown handler in `controller.js` now return early for all keys (except `Escape`) when any of those three overlays are open. `Escape` still closes the active overlay and refocuses the terminal input.
- **App name font consistency across pages** — the app name in the header of permalink and diag pages was using `var(--font-display)` (Syne) at 16px glow, while the main shell uses `var(--font-mono)` (JetBrains Mono) at 20px glow. The `.permalink-title` rule in `styles.css` now uses `var(--font-mono)`, 20px glow, and the same weight and letter-spacing as the main header so the app name renders identically across all pages.
- **Permalink and diag action button hover** — the `← shell` link and other action buttons on permalink and diag pages had no hover highlight. A scoped `.permalink-actions .term-action-btn:hover` rule was added to `styles.css` to apply the same green border and text color used by action buttons on the main shell.
- **Gunicorn orphan-process crash (`init: true`)** — added `init: true` to both `docker-compose.yml` and `examples/docker-compose.standalone.yml` so Docker's bundled tini process runs as PID 1. Without this, scanner tools like `wpscan` that exit with code 3 as a normal status code (meaning "potentially interesting findings") could crash the server: when the entire subprocess chain receives SIGTERM simultaneously, intermediate parents may die before the leaf tool, orphaning it to PID 1 (Gunicorn). Gunicorn's `reap_workers()` collects the orphan via `waitpid(-1)` and interprets `exit(3)` as `WORKER_BOOT_ERROR`, halting the server. With `init: true`, tini is PID 1, Gunicorn is PID 2+, and orphaned scanner processes are silently reaped by tini.
- **`/kill` endpoint PGID race condition** — the endpoint now uses the stored subprocess PID directly as the PGID instead of calling `os.getpgid(pid)` at kill time. Since all subprocesses are spawned with `preexec_fn=os.setsid`, PGID equals PID at creation, so the stored value is always correct. The previous `os.getpgid()` call would return the wrong PGID if the subprocess had already been reaped and its PID reused by a new Gunicorn worker, causing `kill -TERM -<worker_pgid>` to send SIGTERM to the entire Gunicorn worker pool.
- **Late kill / exit prompt race** — when a command finishes at the same time the user clicks Kill, the runner now re-attempts deferred prompt mounting after the kill path so the active tab does not get stuck without the prompt below the output. The same prompt-remount path also runs when the late exit event arrives after a kill click.
- **Container Smoke Test DinD filesystem mismatch** — the `container_smoke_test` fixture no longer depends on runtime bind mounts that assume the Docker daemon can see the test process's filesystem. It now builds the base image, creates a temporary container, copies the repo `app/` tree plus a generated `config.local.yaml` into `/app`, commits that as a runtime image, and starts compose from that image with no client-side bind mounts. This fixes the GitLab DinD case where the daemon runs in a separate sidecar and cannot reliably mount paths from the job container.
- **Container Smoke Test DinD port selection** — the fixture no longer guesses a free localhost port from the job container namespace. It now publishes `8888` on an ephemeral host port and discovers the real published port with `docker compose port`, which avoids cross-namespace port collisions under DinD.
- **Container Smoke Test corpus refresh** — the smoke-test expectation baseline was refreshed for current `host`, `dig`, `nc`, and `dnsrecon` output so the fixture keeps matching the upgraded tool behavior in `app/conf/auto_complete.txt`.
- **SQLite bootstrap race under Gunicorn startup** — `db_init()` now takes a filesystem lock before schema creation, migration, and retention pruning. Without that lock, multiple Gunicorn workers importing `database.py` at the same time could race through `PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL` and startup migration work, intermittently failing with `sqlite3.OperationalError: database is locked`.
- **Search bar hidden-on-load** — `ui_helpers.js` now sets `searchBar.style.display = 'none'` at initialisation so the inline style overrides the conflicting `.search-bar { display: flex }` rule (same specificity, later in the stylesheet) that was causing the bar to appear visible on load when `.u-hidden` was also applied. `isSearchBarOpen()` was also tightened from `!== 'none'` to `=== 'flex'` so the bar is treated as closed before any JS interaction sets the inline style explicitly.
- **Blank Enter while a command is running** — pressing Enter on an empty prompt while a tab is in the `running` state no longer appended a spurious blue prompt line to the output. The empty-command path in `submitCommand` now returns early when the active tab is running.
- **Deny-prefix flag matching rewrite** — `_is_denied()` now tokenizes both the command and deny entries using the shared `split_command_argv` helper, matches tool and subcommand prefixes case-insensitively, and matches flags with exact case. Previously, the entire deny entry was lowercased before comparison, so `!curl -K` also blocked `curl -k`. The new implementation also handles combined short flags (e.g. `-sU` is caught by a `!nmap -sU` deny entry) correctly.
- **Draft input corrupted when switching tabs with a keyboard shortcut** — pressing a keyboard shortcut that contains the Tab key (such as `Alt+Tab`) while `cmdInput` had focus triggered the autocomplete accept handler (`acAccept`) because the `Tab` key case in the `cmdInput` keydown handler had no modifier guard. If `acFiltered` still held stale suggestions from the previous tab's typing session (e.g. `['whoami']`), `acAccept` would overwrite the current input and fire an input event that saved the wrong value into the active tab's `draftInput`. On the next switch, that tab's draft was restored as the stale suggestion instead of the original command. Fixed by adding `!e.altKey && !e.ctrlKey && !e.metaKey` guards to the `Tab` handler in `controller.js` so modifier-key combinations no longer trigger autocomplete logic.
- **Stale autocomplete suggestions persisting across tab switches** — `activateTab` in `tabs.js` now calls `acHide()` and resets `acFiltered = []` when switching tabs, so suggestions filtered for one tab's typing session cannot bleed into another tab. Without this, pressing bare Tab on a newly activated tab could accept a suggestion from the previous tab's last input instead of filtering for the current draft.
- **Ctrl+R hist-search auto-fill** — typing in hist-search mode immediately overwrote the input with the first matched command, so continuing to type appended to the full match instead of refining the query (e.g. typing `w` matched `whoami` and populated the field, so typing `ho` then produced `whoamiho`). `handleHistSearchInput` no longer calls `setComposerValue` during typing; the typed query stays in the input while matches appear in the dropdown. ArrowDown/Up and Ctrl+R navigate the list and fill the input with the highlighted match; Tab accepts without running; Enter accepts and runs.
- **Ctrl+C in hist-search left autocomplete open** — pressing Ctrl+C to exit hist-search called `exitHistSearch(false)`, which restored the pre-search draft via `setComposerValue` with `dispatch: true`. That fired an input event that triggered `handleComposerInputChange`, reopening the autocomplete dropdown if `acFiltered` had entries. A second Ctrl+C was required to dismiss it. Fixed: `exitHistSearch` now accepts a `keepCurrent` option. The Ctrl+C handler passes `{ keepCurrent: true }` so the typed query stays in the input instead of restoring the pre-search draft. `exitHistSearch` also calls `acHide()` unconditionally at the end so autocomplete cannot reopen regardless of the exit path.
- **Hist-search ArrowDown/Up fell through to command history navigation** — pressing ArrowDown/Up while hist-search was active was not handled by `handleHistSearchKey`, so the keys fell through to the command history navigator instead of navigating the hist-search dropdown. Added ArrowDown/Up cases that step `_histSearchIndex` through the match list, fill the input with the selected match via `setComposerValue`, and re-render the dropdown highlight.
- **Hist-search Tab accepted from the wrong source** — Tab while hist-search was active fell through to the `acFiltered`-based autocomplete Tab handler in `controller.js`, which could accept a stale suggestion unrelated to the hist-search results. Added a Tab case to `handleHistSearchKey` that calls `exitHistSearch(true)` to accept the currently selected hist-search match and close the dropdown without running the command.
- **Hist-search Enter did not run the command** — `exitHistSearch(true)` on Enter filled the input with the selected match but never called `submitComposerCommand`, so the menu closed without executing anything. The Enter handler now calls `submitComposerCommand(cmdInput.value, { dismissKeyboard: true })` after accepting. When there are no matches it exits with `keepCurrent: true` (preserving the typed query) and runs that instead of restoring the pre-search draft.
- **Hist-search typing appended to pre-search draft** — `enterHistSearch()` did not clear the input when activating search mode, so if the user had a command like `ping -c 10 google.com` in the input and pressed Ctrl+R, the first keystroke would append to that text rather than starting a fresh query. Fixed: `enterHistSearch` now saves the current input as `_histSearchPreDraft` and then clears it (without dispatching) so subsequent typing goes directly into the search query. Escape and Ctrl+G still restore the original draft.
- **Mobile edit-bar hold-to-repeat** — the left and right cursor-move buttons in the mobile composer now repeat while held: a 400 ms initial delay starts the repeat, which then fires every 60 ms. Document-level `pointerup`, `pointercancel`, `touchend`, and `touchcancel` safety listeners ensure the timer is always cancelled even if the pointer leaves the button while held. Previously a single tap moved the cursor one position with no repeat.
- **Mobile composer tap-to-reposition cursor** — tapping on the mobile composer input to reposition the cursor within the existing text no longer snaps back to the end of the line. The `pointerdown` and `touchstart` handlers now return early (without calling `preventDefault` or `focus`) when the input is already focused, so the browser can place the cursor at the tapped position normally. A `click` handler additionally captures the tapped cursor position and restores it on the next tick if a downstream synchronisation call moves it to end.
- **Mobile composer cursor-to-end jitter** — after tapping to reposition, the cursor was intermittently jumping back to the end of the line. The root cause was a cascade: `setComposerValue` dispatched an `input` event on the desktop input, which re-read the desktop `selectionStart` (still at end) and wrote that back to the mobile input via `setSelectionRange`. Fixed by adding an `exclude` option to `setComposerValue` that skips the `.value` assignment on the source input when called from `handleComposerInputChange`, and by rewriting `syncHiddenCommandInputFromVisible` to write directly to `cmdInput` without triggering the dispatch cascade.
- **Mobile `composerRefs.row` stealing focus from taps** — tapping on the mobile composer input bubbled to the row's `pointerdown`/`touchstart` handlers, which called `focusCommandInputFromGesture()` and reset the cursor. The row handlers now exclude the mobile input element as a valid trigger target.
- **macOS accent picker / hold-to-repeat on desktop** — holding a key on the desktop prompt on macOS would open the OS accent chooser instead of repeating the character. The `cmdInput` keydown handler now calls `e.preventDefault()` for all printable, non-modifier, non-IME keys and manually inserts the character via `replaceCmdRange`, signalling to the OS that the key event is handled and suppressing the accent picker. The handler is skipped while the welcome intro is active so Space/Enter/Escape welcome-settle triggers and printable insertion remain under the `document` keydown handler that owns welcome key routing.
- **Desktop hidden input soft-keyboard guard** — `#cmd` (the hidden desktop input) now carries `inputmode="none"` so mobile browsers do not raise the soft keyboard if the element receives focus unexpectedly.
- **Desktop command chip row overflow** — the recent-command chip row now truncates to a single line on desktop. Chips that would wrap to a second row are removed and replaced with a `+ more` chip that opens the run history drawer, matching the behavior of the mobile chip row (which caps at three chips). The chip count re-evaluates on window resize. A `max-height` clip on `.history-row` ensures any briefly-wrapped chips during render are never painted before JS removes them.
- **Text selection in terminal output** — clicking and dragging to select output text no longer immediately clears the selection by stealing focus back to the command prompt. The `terminalBody` click handler now skips `focusAnyComposerInput` when `window.getSelection().toString()` is non-empty so a just-completed drag selection survives.
- **Keystrokes forwarded after selecting text** — pressing a printable key while focus is outside the command input (e.g. after selecting output text) now forwards the keystroke to the prompt instead of discarding it. A catch-all at the end of the `document` keydown handler focuses `cmdInput`, inserts the character via `replaceCmdRange`, and calls `e.preventDefault()`. The catch-all is skipped when a modal is open, when the target is a button or link, or when the target is an editable field.
- **Scroll to bottom on typing** — typing in either the desktop or mobile composer now immediately scrolls the active output to the bottom and resets `followOutput` to `true`. Previously, if the user had scrolled up to review output, typing did not return the view to the prompt.
- **Mobile landscape orientation overlay** — a full-screen `#landscape-overlay` element is shown on touch devices in landscape orientation with a viewport height under 500px (phones, not tablets). The overlay uses `var(--bg)` and `var(--text-muted)` to follow the active theme and displays an animated rotate icon prompting the user to return to portrait. It is purely CSS-driven via `@media (orientation: landscape) and (pointer: coarse) and (max-height: 500px)` and requires no JavaScript.
- **Mobile composer layout broken after app backgrounding** — returning to the browser after switching to another app (or the home screen) left the mobile composer and keyboard helper bar pinned near the top of the screen with a large gray gap. The OS closes the keyboard when the app is backgrounded, but on iOS the `visualViewport` `resize` event does not always fire on return, so the stale `mobile-keyboard-open` class and `--mobile-keyboard-offset` value persisted. A `visibilitychange` listener added to `bindMobileComposerKeyboardListeners` re-runs `syncMobileComposerKeyboard()` followed by `syncMobileViewportState()` after a 50 ms settle delay whenever the page transitions from hidden to visible. `syncMobileViewportState` calls `isMobileKeyboardOpen()` which returns `false` when the offset is at or below the baseline, clearing the stale class and restoring the correct layout.
- **HUD clock "local" mode Playwright assertion fails on UTC CI runners** — the `options modal` e2e test asserted that switching the HUD clock to local mode produces a display string that does not contain `"UTC"`. CI runners whose system timezone is UTC negate that assumption: `_formatLocalClock` appends the short timezone label, which is `"UTC"` when local = UTC, so the assertion always failed on those machines even though the preference was correctly applied. The test now sets `timezoneId: 'America/New_York'` via `test.use` at the describe level so the local-clock label is always a non-UTC zone (`EST`/`EDT`), making the assertion environment-independent.
  - **Tests:** no count change — this is a fix to an existing Playwright case, not a new test. Net suite total unchanged: 842 pytest + 666 Vitest + 197 Playwright = **1,705 tests**.

### Changed
- **Composer state Phase 3** — focus and selection changes now publish directly into `composerState`, and the last hidden-input mirroring helper was removed. Mobile focus, desktop focus, and selectionchange events now update shared composer state instead of pushing DOM state from one input into the other.
- **Mobile composer-host spacing guard** — added a unit regression that reads `styles.css` and asserts the simplified mobile shell does not put keyboard-height spacing back onto `#mobile-composer-host`. This keeps the stale gap fix from being silently reintroduced during later mobile-shell tuning.
- **Composer state Phase 2** — `setComposerValue()` now renders only the active input and dispatches only to that target, while the mobile history/autocomplete paths publish through the shared `composerState` instead of mirroring into the hidden desktop input. The selection-change and mobile tap helpers were tightened to update shared state directly, which keeps desktop and mobile composer ownership one-way without reintroducing the mobile shell coupling that the Firefox fix removed.
- **iptables loopback block for scanner user** — `entrypoint.sh` now adds an iptables `OUTPUT` rule (before the `gosu` drop) that `REJECT`s TCP connections from the `scanner` uid to the app port with a TCP reset. This provides an OS-level backstop for tools that could reach internal endpoints even if they bypass command validation (e.g. scripting languages, `nc`). `iptables` is now installed in the Dockerfile. The rule uses `|| true` so startup is not aborted in environments where `xt_owner` is unavailable.
- **Configurable app port (`APP_PORT`)** — the application port is now controlled by a single `APP_PORT` environment variable (default `8888`). `Dockerfile` uses `ARG APP_PORT` / `EXPOSE ${APP_PORT}`; `entrypoint.sh` uses `${APP_PORT:-8888}` for both the gunicorn bind address and the iptables rule; both `docker-compose.yml` and `examples/docker-compose.standalone.yml` use `${APP_PORT:-8888}` for `expose`/`ports`, build args, the `APP_PORT` environment variable passed into the container, and the healthcheck URL. A `.env` file is included in the repo with the default (`APP_PORT=8888`); edit it to move the whole stack to a different port. The inline `:-8888` fallbacks in `docker-compose.yml` and `ARG APP_PORT=8888` in `Dockerfile` are safety nets only for bare `docker build` runs that bypass Compose. When running `docker compose -f examples/docker-compose.standalone.yml` from the project root, pass `--env-file .env` explicitly because Compose looks for `.env` in the same directory as the compose file.
- **Playwright e2e test commands** — all Playwright specs that previously used `curl http://localhost:5001/...` as the test command were updated to use built-in fake shell commands (`hostname`, `date`, `uptime`, `whoami`, etc.). The `curl localhost` pattern triggers the `_LOOPBACK_RE` block added in this release, causing those tests to fail immediately. Fake commands bypass both the allowlist check and the loopback block because `/run` resolves them before calling `is_command_allowed()`. Tests that run two consecutive commands back-to-back (`clear all history` in `history.spec.js`, `Delete Non-Favorites` in `history.spec.js`, `clearing history` in `failure-paths.spec.js`) also received a `page.waitForTimeout(1200)` between commands: fake commands complete in ~5ms, so without the gap both runs land in the same 1-second rate-limit window under the default `rate_limit_per_second: 5` config. The `history.spec.js` `beforeEach` also gained a `page.reload()` after `localStorage.clear()` to ensure a clean state on each run.
- **`diagnostics_allowed_cidrs` guidance updated** — the `config.yaml` comment for this setting now recommends against including `127.0.0.1/32` and explains that any process inside the container (including web shell commands running as `scanner`) connects from `127.0.0.1`. Host browser and curl access arrives as the Docker bridge gateway IP instead, so `172.16.0.0/12` is the correct scope for operator access.
- **Backend route decomposition** — `app/app.py` has been split into focused Flask Blueprints under `app/blueprints/`: `assets.py` (vendor assets, favicon, health check), `content.py` (index, config, themes, FAQ, autocomplete, welcome endpoints), `run.py` (command execution and kill, with all run-output helpers and the rate-limited `/run` route), and `history.py` (history and share permalink routes with preview-output helpers). Shared per-request helpers live in `app/helpers.py` (trusted-proxy IP resolution, session ID extraction) and the Flask-Limiter singleton in `app/extensions.py`. `app/app.py` is now a thin factory that configures logging, calls `limiter.init_app`, registers blueprints, and wires the before/after-request logging hooks and the 429 error handler. Route behavior, response formats, status codes, rate limits, and SSE streaming are unchanged.
- **Frontend controller split** — `app/static/js/app.js` now keeps the shared UI helpers, while the page bootstrap, config loading, modal and search/history wiring, and mobile composer setup live in `app/static/js/controller.js`. The browser template and jsdom harness both load the controller after `app.js`, preserving the existing classic-script globals while separating the composition root from the reusable helpers.
- **Global-state and script-order coupling cleanup** — `app/static/js/state.js` now owns the shared store boundary and explicit tab state accessors, while DOM-facing helpers live in `app/static/js/ui_helpers.js`. The browser template and jsdom harness load that helper layer explicitly before the DOM-bound modules that depend on it, which keeps the classic-script architecture intact while reducing implicit ordering requirements.
- **DOM construction and template cleanup** — the repeated tab-history and FAQ-limit rendering paths now use direct DOM construction instead of stitched HTML strings, and the shell modal chrome moved to class-based hidden/dialog wrappers in the template. The visible UI and accessibility behavior are unchanged, but the markup is easier to maintain and less brittle.
- **Search highlighting hardening** — `app/static/js/search.js` now highlights matches by walking text nodes and cloning the line structure instead of rewriting serialized `innerHTML`, so mixed-content lines keep their helper markup intact while plain-text search, regex mode, case sensitivity, and current-match navigation behave as before.
- **FAQ inline style cleanup** — the three inline `style="color:var(--...)"` attributes and the `<ul style="...">` layout attribute in the built-in FAQ entries in `app/commands.py` were replaced with CSS classes (`.faq-link` for green documentation links, `.faq-kill-verb` for the red Kill label), removing presentation details from the content layer. The keyboard-shortcuts `<ul>` inline style was removed entirely since the existing `.faq-a ul` rule already handles the layout.
- **Fake command dispatch map** — the 30-way `if/elif` chain in `execute_fake_command()` in `app/fake_commands.py` was replaced with a module-level `_FAKE_COMMAND_DISPATCH` dict of lambdas normalised to `(cmd, sid) -> list[dict]`. The public function body is now four lines: resolve the root, look up the handler, return the unsupported-command error if absent, or call the handler. Behavior is unchanged.
- **Autocomplete above-prompt item order** — removed the extra reversal logic that rendered the suggestion list bottom-to-top and flipped `ArrowDown`/`ArrowUp` direction when the dropdown appeared above the prompt. Items now render top-to-bottom in their natural order regardless of dropdown position, matching the Ctrl+R hist-search dropdown and eliminating the inconsistent navigation direction when the list flipped above.
- **Autocomplete and hist-search wrap-around navigation** — `ArrowDown` at the last item wraps back to the first; `ArrowUp` at the first item (or with no selection) wraps to the last. Both the autocomplete dropdown and the Ctrl+R hist-search dropdown now support indefinite cycling in either direction.
- **CSS section comments** — `app/static/css/styles.css` now has 22 consistent `/* ── Section ── */` markers covering every major surface (CSS variables, base reset, header, shell input, autocomplete, terminal, tab panels, history row, header buttons, modals, theme overrides, tabs, search, permalink toast, permalink pages, run history panel, starred chips, hamburger menu, welcome typeout, tab rename, mobile composer, mobile layout). The theme-override block (body-scoped selectors) also has an explanatory comment describing why `body .foo` specificity is needed over the `:root` defaults.
- **CSS duplicate selector cleanup** — removed 10 redundant `body`-prefixed rules from `app/static/css/styles.css` whose base counterparts already used the same `--theme-*` variables: `body .tabs-bar` (background + scrollbar), all three `body .tabs-bar::-webkit-scrollbar-*` rules, both `body .tabs-scroll-btn` hover/base rules, `body .ac-dropdown`, `body .ac-dropdown.ac-up`, `body .ac-item`, and `body .line.notice`. The two `.ac-dropdown` base box-shadows were updated to `rgba(0,0,0,0.08)` (what the now-removed body override had been enforcing via specificity) before removal. The two split `body.mobile-terminal-mode #mobile-composer-host` declarations were merged into one, dropping the dead first `background` value that the later declaration immediately overwrote.
- **CSS hardcoded color tokenization** — six hardcoded color literals scattered across component rules in `app/static/css/styles.css` were replaced with new `--theme-*` variables: `#000` on green-background elements (caret char, run button) → `--theme-on-accent-text`; selection highlight text colors `#f7fff2` and `#eef7ee` → `--theme-selection-text` and `--theme-selection-line-text`; modal button text `#fff` and `#000` → `--theme-modal-danger-btn-text` and `--theme-modal-warning-btn-text`. All six default values are defined in `:root` so future theme files can override them without touching component rules.

### Added
- **Ctrl+R reverse-history search** — pressing `Ctrl+R` in the command prompt enters reverse-i-search mode. A dropdown appears above the prompt (mirroring the autocomplete dropdown position) listing up to 20 history entries with the query substring highlighted. Typing narrows results and auto-fills the top match; pressing `Ctrl+R` again cycles to the next match; `Enter` accepts; `Escape` or `Ctrl+G` cancels and restores the draft that was in the prompt before search started. Implemented in a new section of `history.js` (`enterHistSearch`, `exitHistSearch`, `handleHistSearchInput`, `handleHistSearchKey`), with `controller.js` routing keydown events through `handleHistSearchKey` first when in search mode and intercepting `Ctrl+R` to enter search. DOM element `#hist-search-dropdown` added to `index.html` and `dom.js`; CSS in `styles.css`.
- **Per-tab draft input persistence** — composer text that has not been submitted is now saved per tab when switching away and restored when switching back. Drafts are not saved for running tabs (the command was submitted). Implemented via a `draftInput` field on each tab object in `tabs.js`, with `activateTab` flushing the leaving tab's draft from `cmdInput.value` directly (bypassing `getComposerValue()` to avoid a mobile/desktop selector race) and restoring the arriving tab's draft via `setComposerValue(..., { dispatch: false })`. The `controller.js` input handler also keeps `draftInput` live on every keystroke so the flush at switch time is always consistent.
- **Snapshot metadata block on permalink pages** — every `/history/<run_id>` and `/share/<id>` page now shows a metadata strip in the header. Run permalinks display an exit code badge (green border for exit 0, red for non-zero), duration (`1m 30s`), line count with full/preview/truncated scope, and app version. Snapshot permalinks show line count and app version (no exit code or duration — snapshots are tab captures with no single exit state). Downloaded HTML exports include the same metadata in their header via inline styles so the self-contained file stays portable. Implemented via a new `_format_duration()` helper in `permalinks.py`, a `meta` keyword argument on `_permalink_context()` and `_permalink_page()`, metadata construction in both `get_run()` and `get_share()` in `blueprints/history.py`, and new CSS classes in `styles.css`.
- **`rate_limit_enabled` config switch** — rate limiting can now be toggled via `config.yaml` or `config.local.yaml`. Defaults to `true`; set to `false` in a local overlay to bypass throttling during the Container Smoke Test corpus capture without touching production config. The `RATELIMIT_ENABLED` Flask-Limiter flag is set from this value at startup.
- **`Option+Tab` / `Alt+Tab` tab cycling** — `Option+Tab` (macOS) / `Alt+Tab` (Linux/Windows) cycles to the next tab; adding `Shift` reverses direction. Behaves identically to `Option+←/→` and is listed in the `shortcuts` helper output and FAQ.
- **Optional local config overlays** — sibling `*.local.*` files are now supported across the checked-in config assets, so operators can keep private per-server overrides out of git while leaving the base config and asset files portable for other deployments
- **One-hour command timeout default** — the checked-in config and built-in runtime default now set `command_timeout_seconds` to `3600`, so long-running commands are bounded by default instead of starting out disabled
- **Configurable prompt prefix** — `prompt_prefix` is now a first-class config setting, so operators can customize the terminal prompt text and welcome samples independently of the app name
- **Theme externalization** — the theme palette and component chrome values are now documented in the named YAML files under `app/conf/themes/`, injected into the live pages as shared CSS/JS theme variables, and reused by the permalink/export helpers so exported HTML stays in sync with the selected theme variant. The root `app/conf/theme_dark.yaml.example` and `app/conf/theme_light.yaml.example` files are copyable templates only.
- **Mobile theme parity** — the simplified mobile composer shell now consumes the same injected theme variables as the desktop shell instead of hardcoded dark CSS. The mobile composer host uses `--theme-mobile-composer-host-bg`, and the visible mobile composer surface now follows `--theme-panel-bg`, `--theme-panel-border`, and `--theme-panel-shadow`, so light themes and custom themes render consistently on mobile.
- **Theme color-scheme hinting** — the app now infers a best-effort document `color-scheme` (`only light`, `only dark`, or `light dark`) from the resolved theme background, emits that via `<meta name="color-scheme">` and `:root { color-scheme: ... }`, and updates it live when the user switches themes. This does not replace the theme system itself, but it gives mobile browsers a standards-based hint not to darken light themes heuristically.
- **Runtime theme selector** — the completed dedicated theme selector modal now exposes a grouped preview grid fed by the theme registry, with `label:`, `group:`, and `sort:` metadata controlling the visible names and section layout, so the live shell can choose among the named YAML variants under `app/conf/themes/` without a page reload while keeping permalinks and exports aligned with the selected theme
- **Operator diagnostics endpoint (`/diag`)** — a new IP-gated `/diag` route in `blueprints/assets.py` returns a themed HTML summary (or JSON with `?format=json`) of app version and name, operational config values (rate limits, timeouts, output limits, retention, proxy CIDRs, log settings), SQLite run/snapshot counts, Redis connectivity, vendor-asset source (built-in vs fallback), per-tool availability derived from the allowlist, and usage statistics (run counts by period, exit-code outcome breakdown, top 10 commands by frequency, and top 5 longest individual runs). The route returns 404 unless the direct TCP peer IP falls within the `diagnostics_allowed_cidrs` list in `config.yaml`; the list defaults to empty so the endpoint is off by default. Because it uses `request.remote_addr` directly rather than the resolved `X-Forwarded-For` client IP, `X-Forwarded-For` spoofing cannot bypass the gate — only requests whose connection originates from an allowed address are served. Denied access is logged as `DIAG_DENIED` with the peer IP and configured CIDRs; allowed access is logged as `DIAG_VIEWED`. A new `ip_is_in_cidrs()` helper was added to `helpers.py`, reusing the existing `_trusted_proxy_networks` CIDR cache. The page layout places all four status cards (App, DB, Redis, Vendor Assets) in a single equal-width row so cards stay compact; the Activity and Top Commands sections each use a two-column split below the status row.
- **Diag link in the main UI** — when the `/config` response includes `diag_enabled: true` (set when the visiting IP is in `diagnostics_allowed_cidrs`), a `⊕ diag` button appears in the desktop header alongside history/options/theme/FAQ, and a matching entry appears in the mobile hamburger menu. Both are hidden by default (`u-hidden`) and revealed only after the config fetch confirms access. The desktop button is an `<a>` element styled to match the other header buttons, including full participation in the theme-override CSS block so it follows `--theme-toolbar-button-*` variables consistently.
- **Mobile theme selector layout** — the theme picker now opens as a full-screen chooser on mobile with a two-column preview layout on wider phones, so the preview cards stay readable and the grouped sections keep a uniform width instead of collapsing unevenly on small screens

## [1.3] — 2026-04-07

### Added
- **Terminal-native input surface** — the visible command-entry UI is now rendered inline inside terminal output while keeping a hidden real input for browser/mobile keyboard semantics
- **Shell-like editing and control behavior** — blank/whitespace `Enter` now emits a fresh prompt line, and `Ctrl+C` now opens kill confirmation during active runs or emits a new prompt line when idle
- **Keyboard shortcut layer** — app-safe shortcuts now cover tab lifecycle, active-tab actions, and shell-style line editing
  - `Alt/Option+T`, `Alt/Option+W`, `Alt/Option+ArrowLeft/Right`, and `Alt/Option+1...9` manage tab creation, closing, and navigation
  - `Alt/Option+P`, `Alt/Option+Shift+C`, and `Ctrl+L` trigger permalink, copy, and clear actions for the active tab
  - `Ctrl+U`, `Ctrl+K`, and `Alt/Option+B` / `Alt/Option+F` add readline-style prompt editing on top of the existing `Ctrl+W` support
- **Keyboard shortcut discovery** — new `shortcuts` web-shell helper prints the current shortcut set and is exposed through `help`, autocomplete, the README, and the FAQ modal
- **Shortcut helper cleanup** — the old `keys` helper alias and fallback-notes wording were removed so `shortcuts` is the only supported name in help, autocomplete, docs, and in-terminal output
- **Bundled local fonts** — JetBrains Mono and Syne are now served through local vendor routes backed by build-time font downloads, with repo fallbacks for local dev, so the shell and permalink pages no longer make external font requests on load
- **Bundled local ansi_up** — the browser-facing `ansi_up` asset is now copied from the checked-in repo build into the image at build time, with the repo copy still serving as the local/docker-compose fallback
- **Template-backed permalink pages** — the live `/history/<id>` and `/share/<id>` pages now share Jinja templates plus shared CSS/JS instead of carrying duplicated inline HTML/CSS in `permalinks.py`, which makes the permalink UI easier to maintain while keeping the downloadable HTML export path self-contained
- **Shared HTML export helper** — tab `save html` and permalink export now share browser-side HTML/CSS helpers instead of duplicating export markup in two places, and downloaded tab exports embed vendor fonts at export time so the saved file stays portable
- **Mobile keyboard helper row race** — the mobile helper row now stays visible when viewport resize lands before the focus event, preventing the intermittent gray gap/scroll shift on touch keyboards
- **Tab overflow controls** — left/right scroll buttons were added to the tab bar for overflowed tab lists
- **Tab drag reorder** — tabs can now be reordered directly in the strip using drag-and-drop, including mobile touch drag with visual lift/drop indicators
- **FAQ markup syntax** — custom `faq.yaml` entries can now use lightweight markup for bold, italics, underline, inline code, bullet lists, and clickable command chips that load into the prompt
- **Autocomplete placement logic** — the suggestion list now supports above/below prompt placement and aligns to command start in the inline prompt model
- **Display toggles for output prefixes** — line numbers can now be toggled independently from timestamps, with mobile-menu access and shared prefix alignment across output, prompt, and exit rows
- **User options modal** — a new options modal lets users set timestamp mode and line-number display from one place, with cookie-backed persistence across sessions while keeping the existing quick-toggle buttons in sync. Theme selection lives in its own dedicated modal
- **Permalink display toggles** — permalink pages now expose line-number toggles for all views and timestamp toggles anywhere saved line metadata exists, including fresh canonical run permalinks backed by structured output persistence
- **Mobile composer UX** — the visible mobile composer now keeps Run, Enter-to-submit, history chips, autocomplete, and the edit-helper row wired to the same visible input so the touch keyboard path stays in sync
- **Mobile welcome assets** — added `ascii_mobile.txt` and `/welcome/ascii-mobile` for the dedicated mobile banner path

### Changed
- **Composer state store groundwork** — `state.js` now owns a shared `composerState` with explicit value, selection, and active-input accessors. The shared composer helpers have started reading selection/value from that store, which is the first step in the mobile/desktop input decoupling plan and sets up the later removal of DOM-to-DOM mirroring.
- **Mobile keyboard investigation** — a stripped-down control surface was used during debugging to isolate the Firefox mobile keyboard bug to the main shell integration layer. The shipped fix keeps the simplified normal-flow shell model without exposing that dedicated debug surface in the release.
- **Composite local test command** — `npm test` now runs the full local validation chain (`pytest`, then Vitest, then Playwright) instead of only the JS suites, making the package-level default match the current verification flow.
- **Local overlay ignore pattern** — `.gitignore` now ignores `app/conf/*.local.*` rather than only `app/conf/config.local.yaml`, matching the app’s broader sibling-overlay support for local operator overrides.
- **FAQ single source of truth** — built-in FAQ entries now come from the backend alongside custom `faq.yaml` entries, `/faq` now returns the merged canonical FAQ dataset, and the modal renders from that backend response instead of a hard-coded HTML copy
- **Mobile welcome flow** — touch-sized screens now use `ascii_mobile.txt` with the same staged status and rotating-hint timing as desktop, while skipping the sampled-command phase from `welcome.yaml`
- **Full-output permalink behavior** — tab permalink snapshots now fetch the full persisted run output when it exists, so the main-page permalink button can share the complete result instead of the preview-only tab state
- **Live-output rendering** — fast bursts now flush in small batches so the browser can repaint during large commands, and the live terminal follows the bottom only while the user remains at the tail
- **Welcome interruption and settle behavior** — welcome fast-forward now consistently responds to keyboard actions used in the inline-prompt flow and preserves correct prompt mounting after settle
- **Welcome asset split** — desktop and mobile welcome flows now use separate hint files, with mobile keeping its own `app_hints_mobile.txt`
- **Tab activation model** — switching tabs now keeps the prompt input neutral (no automatic command repopulation), preventing cross-tab draft leakage
- **Prompt rendering model** — submitted commands are preserved as styled prompt lines in output and running tabs hide the live prompt until completion, matching shell transcript flow more closely
- **Autocomplete presentation** — dropdown framing was removed in favor of a terminal-style suggestion list that can flip above the prompt when space is tight
- **Autocomplete matching and navigation** — suggestions now match from the beginning of commands only, keep the active row in view, and use visual Up/Down navigation even when the list is rendered above the prompt
- **Output actions UX** — `copy` and `save txt` now report a friendly no-output toast when the tab only contains welcome/decorative lines
- **Run-output persistence format** — fresh run previews and full-output artifacts now preserve structured `{text, cls, tsC, tsE}` entries instead of flattening everything to plain text, allowing canonical run permalinks to keep prompt echo and timestamp metadata while remaining backward-compatible with older plain-text artifacts
- **Theme parity and light-mode polish** — light-mode colors were softened across the main shell and permalink pages, and share/permalink views now follow the current session theme so saved output matches the live UI
- **History and modal UX** — the history drawer now closes on outside click and Escape, and the clear-all / kill confirmation flows honor Escape consistently
- **HTML export wording and behavior notes** — docs and UI copy now describe `save .html` as a themed HTML export that uses app-hosted vendor fonts when available and falls back to browser monospace fonts offline, matching the current implementation

### Fixed
- **Trusted proxy resolution** — forwarded client IPs are now honored only from configured trusted proxy CIDRs, direct clients can no longer spoof request identity through `X-Forwarded-For`, and untrusted forwarded headers log the peer/proxy IP so operators can identify the missing proxy entry
- **Prompt alignment** — when line numbers or timestamps are enabled, the new prompt stays aligned under the output gutter instead of leaving the prompt prefix pinned flush left
- **Tab isolation and close-running-tab kill** — running one tab no longer blocks the others, and closing a running tab now kills that tab before switching away
- **Kill-spec rate-limit stability** — the kill modal e2e coverage now isolates its limiter bucket per run and stubs the long-running SSE locally so repeated full-suite runs do not hang on a shared `/run` bucket
- **Vendor font route hardening** — `/vendor/fonts/...` now only serves the known vendored font files instead of accepting arbitrary joined paths, and route coverage now includes unknown/traversal rejection
- **Theme selector Escape handling** — the dedicated theme preview modal now closes on Escape and returns focus to the terminal, matching the other overlay close behaviors
- **Release metadata alignment** — the Node package metadata now reports `1.3.0`, matching the app version used elsewhere in the release
- **Mobile tab close focus** — closing the only mobile tab no longer leaves the reset `X` visually focused, and tab close controls no longer stay highlighted after use
- **Mobile tab row overflow** — mobile tabs now scroll horizontally with hidden scrollbars, tab labels resist text selection during drag, and tab chrome reads as separate bordered tabs instead of a plain text strip
- **Mobile header layout** — the mobile app name, status pill, timer, and hamburger control now use the available header space more evenly instead of looking undersized
- **Mobile action-button focus cleanup** — `permalink`, `copy`, `clear`, and history action buttons now drop focus after tap/click so they don’t remain visually brighter than the rest
- **Mobile input focus control** — tab switches, close/reset, and other app-driven flows no longer force focus back into the composer on mobile; only an explicit user tap on the input does
- **Mobile clear / close-tab run preservation** — clearing a running tab and closing a running tab now preserve the command lifecycle correctly so the kill path stays available and output does not leak into a replacement tab
- **Permalink preference defaults** — permalink pages now honor saved line-number and timestamp cookies on load
- **macOS keyboard shortcuts** — app-safe `Option` shortcuts now match physical key codes instead of the produced symbol, preventing `Option+T`, `Option+W`, `Option+Shift+C`, and `Option+B/F` from inserting special characters into the prompt
- **Mobile permalink copy flow** — the `/share/...` permalink page now hides its copy toast correctly on mobile and falls back to `execCommand('copy')` when the Clipboard API is unavailable
- **Mobile helper-row styling** — the touch helper buttons keep their dark-theme appearance on Chrome and Safari mobile instead of falling back to light browser defaults
- **Mobile Run guard** — the mobile Run button now disables while a command is active, matching the desktop Run control and preventing duplicate submits
- **Cursor mirroring** — holding desktop arrow keys now updates the visible prompt cursor immediately instead of waiting for key release
- **Prefix toggle layout** — enabling line numbers or timestamps no longer reflows wrapped output or jumps the live tail to a mid-buffer line
- **Permalink truncation notices** — fresh permalinks no longer show stale preview-truncated warnings when the full persisted output is available
- **Tab output truncation alignment** — long outputs now keep `currentRunStartIndex` aligned when old raw lines are pruned from the front, so shared permalinks do not splice stale output fragments into the saved view
- **Welcome skip edge case** — pressing Enter while welcome is active no longer leaves a stray legacy prompt marker in output
- **Prompt cursor rendering** — prompt caret visibility now remains stable after welcome interruption, normal settle, and follow-up command execution
- **History navigation regression** — blank-input Up/Down recall no longer gets stuck after the first recalled command
- **Tab-bar resize edge case** — tab overflow controls now recalculate correctly when tab width changes (for example after rename)
- **Welcome output prefix bleed** — line numbers and timestamps no longer distort the decorative welcome animation or shift its status rows
- **Mobile helper-row overlap** — the compact `Home` / `←` / `→` / `End` / `Del Word` row now stays hidden until the mobile keyboard is actually open, and helper taps no longer reopen autocomplete over the row
- **Mobile composer hit-target fix** — taps on the lower half of the mobile composer now focus the input reliably, which stops the intermittent keyboard-open scroll shift in Chrome and Safari
- **History drawer action close** — clicking any button in the history drawer now closes the panel immediately
- **Batched live output** — large output bursts now flush in small chunks so the browser can repaint during fast commands, and the live terminal only stays pinned to the bottom while the user has not scrolled away
- **Shared Run guard** — desktop and mobile Run buttons now disable together while a command is active, preventing duplicate submits from either input path

---

## [1.2] — 2026-04-05

### Added
- **Split run-output persistence** — completed runs now keep a capped preview in SQLite for the history drawer and normal run permalink, while optional full output is persisted separately as compressed artifacts with metadata in a dedicated `run_output_artifacts` table
  - canonical run permalinks at `/history/<run_id>` now serve the full saved output when an artifact exists
  - `/history/<run_id>/full` remains as a backward-compatible alias
  - full-output artifacts are deleted alongside their parent run on single-run delete, clear-history, and retention pruning
- **Fake shell command framework** — `/run` now recognizes a small synthetic-command layer before process spawning so common shell helpers can be useful without weakening the allowlist model
  - `banner` prints the configured ASCII art without replaying the full welcome sequence
  - `clear` clears the current terminal tab through the normal `/run` flow
  - `date` prints the current server time
  - `env` prints a stable web shell environment for the current session
  - `faq` prints the built-in FAQ plus custom `faq.yaml` entries inside the terminal
  - `fortune` prints a short operator-themed one-liner
  - `groups` prints web shell group membership
  - `help` lists the available web shell helpers
  - `history` prints recent commands from the current session in shell-style history order
  - `hostname` prints the configured app/instance name
  - `id` prints a stable web-shell identity for the app
  - `last` prints recent completed runs with timestamps and exit codes
  - `limits` prints the configured runtime, retention, and rate-limit settings in-terminal
  - `ls` prints the current allowlist grouped by category
  - `man <allowed-command>` renders the real system man page for allowlisted topics through a non-interactive, terminal-safe path
  - `man <fake-command>` reuses the matching helper description instead of rejecting the topic
  - `retention` prints run-preview retention and full-output persistence settings directly in-terminal
  - `reboot`, `sudo`, and exact `rm -fr /` / `rm -rf /` patterns now return explicit web-shell guardrail messages
  - `status` prints a short session and instance summary
  - `tty` prints a web terminal device path
  - `type <cmd>` and `which <cmd>` distinguish helper commands, real commands, and missing runtime binaries
  - `pwd` prints a web-shell workspace path
  - `version` prints web shell, app, Flask, and Python version details
  - `who` prints the current web shell user/session
  - `whoami` prints a short project description and the GitLab README link
  - `ps` / `ps aux` / `ps -ef` now show the current `ps` invocation with a fake PID plus prior completed commands with separate exit/start/end columns
  - `uname -a` prints a stable web-shell environment string instead of host kernel details
  - `uptime` prints app uptime since process start
- **Richer welcome startup flow** — first load can now show a decorative ASCII banner from `app/conf/ascii.txt`, fake startup-status lines, curated sampled commands from `app/conf/welcome.yaml`, and rotating footer hints from `app/conf/app_hints.txt`
  - sampled welcome commands are clickable and load into the prompt without running
  - the featured sample gets a clickable `TRY THIS FIRST` badge
  - `/welcome/ascii` serves the banner as plain text and `/welcome/hints` serves footer hints as JSON
- **Welcome sampling metadata** — `welcome.yaml` entries now support `group` and `featured` fields so the sampled command set can stay varied while still biasing one primary onboarding command
- **Configurable welcome status labels** — new `welcome_status_labels` key in `config.yaml`, exposed through `/config`, lets operators tune the fake startup block without editing frontend code
- **Configurable welcome pacing knobs** — `welcome_sample_count`, `welcome_hint_interval_ms`, and `welcome_hint_rotations` now let operators tune how many sampled commands are shown and how the footer hint feed behaves while idle, with `0` rotating until interrupted and `1` keeping the first hint static
- **FAQ modal sizing** — the desktop FAQ modal now has an explicit width again so it stays compact instead of stretching close to full-screen; the theme modal keeps its separate mobile/full-screen treatment
- **Dependency version tracking** — added a local `scripts/check_versions.sh` helper for spotting pinned Python packages, Node devDependencies, the Docker base image line, and pinned Go/pip/gem tool versions from `Dockerfile`, while ignoring prerelease Docker tags like alpha and rc builds; Go lookups resolve the module root from `go install .../cmd/...` paths before querying the proxy. The helper also supports `--python-only`, `--node-only`, `--docker-only`, `--go-only`, `--pip-only`, `--gem-only`, and `--debug` so you can inspect one surface at a time.
- **Manual dependency drift check job** — GitLab CI now has a `dependency-version-check` job that is visible as a manual run in pipelines, runs the local version checker, and publishes its output as a short-lived artifact
- **Fresh-image Container Smoke Test** — added opt-in wrapper scripts for the live-browser corpus capture and the Docker-backed container regression. The fresh-image `tests/py/test_container_smoke_test.py` check still builds a fresh Docker image, starts the app, and runs every command from `app/conf/auto_complete.txt` through `/run` with per-command output assertions so missing apt/pip/go/gem tools or broken fake-command wiring show up before an image update lands; the fixture also streams Docker build/start/health progress so long builds do not look idle, packages the repo `app/` tree and generated `config.local.yaml` into a committed runtime image instead of relying on runtime bind mounts, includes focused `_docker_reach_host()` and compose-port parsing regressions for GitLab DinD, and writes a JUnit report to `test-results/container_smoke_test.xml` when run directly
- **CI smoke job for Container Smoke Test** — GitLab CI now has a `container-smoke-test` job that is visible as a manual run in pipelines and runs the same fresh-image command corpus check when you want to verify Dockerfile/toolchain changes before merging
- **Container Smoke Test DinD reachability** — the smoke-test fixture now detects `tcp://...` `DOCKER_HOST` values and probes the Docker daemon host instead of hard-coding `127.0.0.1`, which keeps GitLab DinD jobs talking to the published container port instead of the job container loopback; a focused `_docker_reach_host()` regression in the same module locks that behavior in
- **Container Smoke Test corpus capture timeout tuning** — the live-browser corpus capture script now gives heavyweight commands like `nmap -p-` a longer per-command timeout instead of failing the whole run mid-scan
- **Container Smoke Test corpus resume point** — the live-browser capture script now accepts `--start-from-command` so you can restart from a specific command without redoing earlier captures
- **Container Smoke Test corpus default timeout bump** — the live-browser capture script now uses a five-minute default command timeout, with heavier commands still getting larger per-command budgets
- **Test-only rate-limit bypass** — `rate_limit_enabled` is now a config switch, and the fresh-image Container Smoke Test uses it in its temporary overlay so the corpus run can bypass throttling without changing production defaults
- **Container Smoke Test output settle wait** — the live-browser corpus capture script now waits for the output line count to stop changing for a moment after a command finishes, which keeps fast-finishing commands like `man curl` from being saved before the text stream has settled
- **Container Smoke Test long-scan early stop** — the live-browser corpus capture script now stops long-running scans like `nmap`, `masscan`, `nikto`, `testssl`, and `nuclei` after their early success markers appear, then saves the top portion of the output and moves on
- **Additional welcome timing knobs** — `welcome_first_prompt_idle_ms` and `welcome_post_status_pause_ms` now let operators tune how long the first ready prompt sits before typing begins and how clearly the boot/status block hands off into the command phase
- **Full-output persistence config** — `persist_full_run_output` and `full_output_max_mb` (5 MB by default) now let operators keep complete run output outside the `runs` table without loading massive scans back into the interactive tab UI; the app multiplies the MB cap by `1024 * 1024` internally
- **Startup command-history hydration** — the frontend now hydrates recent-command recall from `/history` on boot so blank-input `ArrowUp` / `ArrowDown` works on first load, not only after a command has been run in the current tab
- **Structured logging** — new `logging_setup.py` module providing four log levels (ERROR / WARN / INFO / DEBUG) and two output formats (`text` and `gelf`)
  - `text` format: human-readable `2026-04-02T10:00:00Z [INFO ] EVENT  key=value ...` lines with structured context appended as sorted key=value pairs
  - `gelf` format: newline-delimited GELF 1.1 JSON with `short_message` as the event name and all context in `_`-prefixed additional fields, compatible with Graylog / OpenSearch and other GELF back-ends
  - Client IP (`_ip`) included on all INFO, WARN, and ERROR events; auto-detected from `X-Forwarded-For` when it contains a valid IP, otherwise falls back to the direct connection IP
  - Full log event inventory: `REQUEST`, `RESPONSE`, `KILL_MISS`, `HEALTH_OK` (DEBUG); `PAGE_LOAD`, `CONTENT_VIEWED`, `THEME_SELECTED`, `RUN_START`, `RUN_END`, `RUN_KILL`, `DB_PRUNED`, `LOGGING_CONFIGURED`, `SHARE_CREATED`, `SHARE_VIEWED`, `RUN_VIEWED`, `HISTORY_DELETED`, `HISTORY_CLEARED`, `CMD_REWRITE` (INFO); `CMD_DENIED`, `RATE_LIMIT`, `CMD_TIMEOUT`, `KILL_FAILED`, `HEALTH_DEGRADED`, `RUN_NOT_FOUND`, `SHARE_NOT_FOUND` (WARN); `RUN_SPAWN_ERROR`, `RUN_STREAM_ERROR`, `RUN_SAVED_ERROR`, `HEALTH_DB_FAIL`, `HEALTH_REDIS_FAIL` (ERROR)
  - `log_level` and `log_format` keys added to `config.yaml` (default: `INFO` / `text`)
- **`CMD_TIMEOUT` warning** — when the server kills a command that exceeds `command_timeout_seconds`, a WARN log is now emitted server-side (previously the timeout was only signalled to the client via the SSE stream)
- **`HEALTH_DB_FAIL` / `HEALTH_REDIS_FAIL` errors** — `/health` endpoint now logs ERROR with traceback when the DB or Redis health check fails, making health degradation visible in log aggregators
- **`DB_PRUNED` info** — `db_init()` now logs the number of runs and snapshots deleted when retention pruning removes records on startup
- **`SHARE_CREATED` info** — share (permalink snapshot) creation is logged at INFO with IP, share ID, and label
- **JavaScript testing framework** — Vitest (unit) and Playwright (e2e) added with `package.json`, `vitest.config.js`, and `playwright.config.js`
  - Vitest unit tests (`tests/js/unit/`) cover `escapeHtml`, `escapeRegex`, `renderMotd` (utils.js), `_formatElapsed`, kill flow, and status mapping (runner.js), `_getStarred` / `_saveStarred` / `_toggleStar` (history.js), session ID persistence and `apiFetch()` header injection (session.js), autocomplete rendering and acceptance, tab state/rename/export guards, welcome animation cancellation, search helpers, output rendering, and selected app bootstrap behavior including search-bar close handling, copy/save/html export refocus, and clearing un-ran composer input; no browser required
  - `tests/js/unit/helpers/extract.js` provides a `fromScript(file, ...names)` helper that loads browser script files into an isolated execution context via `new Function`, extracting only the named functions; includes a self-contained `MemoryStorage` class that replaces `localStorage` to avoid jsdom opaque-origin quirks
  - Playwright e2e tests (`tests/js/e2e/`) exercise the full UI against a live Flask server: command execution and denial, kill, history drawer and action-button close behavior, snapshot and single-run permalinks, rate limiting, autocomplete, welcome interruption, search/highlight, output actions (copy, clear, save .txt/.html with embedded-font export assertions and focus-return checks), tab rename/close/recall/max-tabs, timestamp toggle, theme switch, FAQ modal, mobile menu, and the mobile composer hit-target regression; `workers: 1` prevents rate-limit collisions between tests
  - Pre-commit hook updated to run Vitest when `node_modules` is present; Playwright documented as pre-push
  - `.nvmrc` pins Node 22; `node_modules/`, `playwright-report/`, and `test-results/` added to `.gitignore`
- **Star-to-chips promotion** — starring a command from the history drawer now adds it to the recent-commands chip bar if it isn't already there, giving quick access to commands from previous sessions without needing to re-run them
- **Command recall on tab switch** — each tab now remembers its last-run command; switching to a tab automatically restores that command in the input bar, making it easy to re-run or edit without copying from the output
- **Delete Non-Favorites** — the "clear all history" confirmation modal now offers a third option alongside **Delete all** and **Cancel**: **Delete Non-Favorites** removes only runs that are not starred, leaving pinned commands untouched
- **Retention FAQ entry** — the FAQ "Is there a time or output limit?" entry has been replaced with a live retention settings table showing command timeout, output line limit, and permalink retention with their actual configured values; a note clarifies that these are set by the operator of the instance. `permalink_retention_days` is now included in the `/config` API response
- **`HEALTH_OK` debug** — `/health` now logs at DEBUG when all checks pass, making it easy to confirm health probe activity when running at DEBUG level
- **`HEALTH_DEGRADED` warning** — `/health` logs at WARN (with `db` and `redis` status fields) when the aggregate status is degraded, complementing the per-component `HEALTH_DB_FAIL` / `HEALTH_REDIS_FAIL` ERROR events
- **`KILL_FAILED` warning** — kill handler now logs at WARN with `pid`, `run_id`, and `error` when `os.getpgid` or `os.killpg` raises, replacing the previous silent `pass`
- **`RUN_SAVED_ERROR` error** — the DB INSERT after a command completes is now wrapped in a try/except; failures are logged at ERROR with traceback instead of being silently swallowed inside the SSE generator
- **`LOGGING_CONFIGURED` info** — `configure_logging()` now emits an INFO event with `level` and `format` fields immediately after setup, giving operators a confirmation line in startup logs
- **`PAGE_LOAD` info** — every `GET /` now logs at INFO with the client IP, session ID, and resolved theme, giving operators visibility into when the app is being accessed and which theme was applied
- **`CONTENT_VIEWED` info** — config, theme, FAQ, autocomplete, and welcome reads now log at INFO with the route, client IP, session ID, and route-specific context so content fetches are visible without turning them into write-path noise
- **`THEME_SELECTED` debug** — theme resolution now logs at DEBUG with the theme name, source, route, and session so startup theme behavior can be traced when debugging odd browser or cookie state
- **`RUN_NOT_FOUND` warn** — accessing an expired or invalid run permalink logs at WARN with IP and run ID
- **`SHARE_NOT_FOUND` warn** — accessing an expired or invalid snapshot permalink logs at WARN with IP and share ID
- **`SHARE_VIEWED` info** — retrieving a snapshot permalink (`GET /share/<id>`) now logs at INFO with IP, share ID, and label
- **`RUN_VIEWED` info** — retrieving a run permalink (`GET /history/<id>`) now logs at INFO with IP, run ID, and command
- **`HISTORY_DELETED` info** — deleting a single history entry logs at INFO with IP, run ID, and session (only emitted when a row is actually deleted)
- **`HISTORY_CLEARED` info** — clearing all history for a session logs at INFO with IP, session, and count of deleted runs
- **Smart client IP detection** — `get_client_ip()` now validates the `X-Forwarded-For` value against a regex before trusting it; invalid or absent values fall back to the direct connection IP, making the app work correctly with or without a reverse proxy and without any config setting
- **Configurable project README link** — `project_readme` in `config.yaml` now controls the README URL used by the built-in FAQ and synthetic README-style helper output, so operators can point the UI at their own documentation without changing code

### Fixed
- **Friendlier client fetch failures** — dead-server or rejected `/run` requests now render a clear offline message instead of surfacing the browser’s raw `NetworkError` text
- **Better `/run` bad-path handling** — non-403/429 non-streaming error responses now show a clearer server-side failure message instead of falling through to opaque client behavior
- **Kill request failure visibility** — failed `/kill` requests now surface a toast and inline notice so the user knows the command may still be running server-side
- **Autocomplete exact-match submit** — typing a command that exactly matches a suggestion now closes the autocomplete menu so `Enter` submits immediately instead of needing a second press
- **Allowlist deny-case fix** — deny entries in `allowed_commands.txt` now preserve their flag case, so `!curl -K` blocks `curl -K` without also blocking `curl -k`; tool and subcommand names remain case-insensitive
